## Processed Chapters

### Chapter 1: First Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-6
- Source PDF pages: 7, 8, 9
- Printed page numbers: 11, 12, 13
- Key entities: Narayana, Valmiki, Lava, Kusha, Dasharatha, Brahma, Narada, Rama
- Places: Ayodhya, Tamasa, Ganga, Yamuna, Kosala, Sarayu

**Summary:** This chapter introduces the Ramayana, beginning with creation by Narayana, the story of Valmiki's inspiration, the composition of the Ramayana, and the qualifications of Lava and Kusha to sing it. It also describes the glory of Ayodhya under King Dasharatha's rule.

#### Q1

**Question:** At the beginning of the kalpa, when Lord Narayana intended to start creation, whom did he first create by his mere will?

**Options:**
- 1. Vaivasvata Manu
- 2. Four-faced Brahma
- 3. Marichi
- 4. Narada Maharshi

**Correct answer:** Four-faced Brahma

**Key entities:** Narayana, Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** When Valmiki Maharshi saw a Nishada killing one of a pair of Krauncha birds in the forest, on the bank of which river had he gone to bathe at that time?

**Options:**
- 1. Ganga River
- 2. Yamuna River
- 3. Narmada River
- 4. Tamasa River

**Correct answer:** Tamasa River

**Key entities:** Valmiki, Tamasa

#### Q3

**Question:** After having his doubts resolved by Narada Maharshi, with the grace of Lord Brahma, through whom did Valmiki Maharshi first propagate the Ramayana he wrote in the world?

**Answer:** Kusha and Lava

**Key entities:** Narada, Brahma, Valmiki, Kusha, Lava

#### Q4

**Question:** What was the qualification of Lava and Kusha to sing the Ramayana in Ayodhya?

**Answer:** Valmiki Maharshi taught the Ramayana, composed with all his penance, to his disciples Lava and Kusha. Having thoroughly studied the Sama Veda and possessing good knowledge of music, they sang the epic with the sage's approval, adding music to the words and deep meanings. Thus, having learned all the nuances of singing from Valmiki, Lava and Kusha sang the Ramayana in hermitages during sacrificial ceremonies, delighting the listeners. Later, while singing in the streets of Ayodhya, Lord Rama heard them and, during his Ashvamedha sacrifice, summoned them and had them sing the Ramayana before him.

**Key entities:** Lava, Kusha, Ayodhya, Valmiki, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** During King Dasharatha's reign, how magnificent was the capital of Kosala, the city of Ayodhya?

**Answer:** The kingdom of Kosala, situated on the banks of the Sarayu River, abounded in wealth, grain, and all riches. The city of Ayodhya, built by the Prajapati Vaivasvata Manu, was the capital. During the reign of King Dasharatha, Ayodhya was impregnable to enemies, surrounded by high ramparts, deep moats outside the walls, and broad royal roads on four sides with shops on both sides, making it visually delightful. The city was filled with scholars, warriors, perpetual fire-sacrificers, those endowed with qualities like self-control and tranquility, experts in Vedic study, and truth-speakers. King Dasharatha was well-versed in the Vedas, honored heroes and scholars with wealth and grain, and kept them under his control. He was a knower of future events. The people of Ayodhya were devoted to their respective duties. Thus, King Dasharatha, endowed with a fourfold army, righteously ruled the prosperous Kosala empire.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kosala, Ayodhya, Sarayu

### Chapter 2: Second Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 7-12
- Source PDF pages: 9, 10, 11
- Printed page numbers: 13, 14, 15
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Rishyashringa, Romapada, Shanta, Sumantra, Vishvamitra, Jabali
- Places: Ayodhya, Kosala

**Summary:** King Dasharatha, desiring sons, is advised to invite the sage Rishyashringa to perform a sacrifice. Dasharatha travels to Anga kingdom, meets King Romapada, and brings Rishyashringa and his wife Shanta to Ayodhya. Preparations for the Ashvamedha sacrifice begin under Rishyashringa's guidance.

#### Q1

**Question:** How many ministers did King Dasharatha, who ruled the Kosala kingdom, have?

**Options:**
- 1. Seven
- 2. Ten
- 3. Eight
- 4. Nine

**Correct answer:** Eight

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kosala

#### Q2

**Question:** Who advised Dasharatha to first invite Rishyashringa and bring him for the sacrifice he intended to perform for obtaining sons due to lack of progeny?

**Options:**
- 1. Sumantra
- 2. Vasishtha
- 3. Vishvamitra
- 4. Jabali

**Correct answer:** Sumantra

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rishyashringa, Sumantra

#### Q3

**Question:** Where was Rishyashringa at the time when King Dasharatha went with all his people to invite him to Ayodhya?

**Answer:** In the Anga kingdom

**Key entities:** Rishyashringa, Dasharatha, Ayodhya

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rishyashringa's arrival in Ayodhya take place?

**Answer:** King Dasharatha, along with all his queens and royal retinue, set out and went to Anga kingdom, met King Romapada, and received special honors. Then he met sage Rishyashringa. After staying in Anga for a week, Dasharatha told Romapada: 'O king, send your daughter Shanta and your son-in-law Rishyashringa to my city. A great task is to be performed there. I am inviting this couple to participate in it.' Romapada accepted Dasharatha's invitation and told Rishyashringa: 'O sage, accept King Dasharatha's invitation and go to Ayodhya with your wife Shanta, following Dasharatha.' Rishyashringa agreed and, with his wife, set out with Dasharatha and reached Ayodhya. Dasharatha reverently worshipped Rishyashringa who came to his palace. Shanta and Rishyashringa stayed happily in Ayodhya for some time.

**Key entities:** Rishyashringa, Ayodhya, Dasharatha, Romapada, Shanta

#### Q5

**Question:** What arrangements did King Dasharatha make for the sacrifice he intended to perform?

**Answer:** At the beginning of the spring season, King Dasharatha intended to start the Ashvamedha sacrifice. First, he bowed to sage Rishyashringa and requested him to be the chief priest for the sacrifice meant for the prosperity of his dynasty. Rishyashringa accepted the king's request and told him to prepare the sacrificial materials. Then Dasharatha, pleased, summoned his intimate minister Sumantra and said: 'Go quickly and bring Vasishtha and other preceptors and priests.' According to the king's order, Sumantra went quickly and brought them all. King Dasharatha duly worshipped the arrived preceptors and priests, and requested sage Vasishtha: 'O revered one among sages, you who desire the elevation of our dynasty, please ensure that the sacrificial task I have undertaken is completed without obstacles.' Then all of them said to the king: 'Let it be as per your command!' and agreed to perform their respective duties in the conduct of the sacrifice along with sage Rishyashringa.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rishyashringa, Sumantra

### Chapter 3: Third Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 13-18
- Source PDF pages: 11, 12, 13
- Printed page numbers: 15, 16, 17
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Vishnu, Ravana, Rama, Bharata, Lakshmana, Shatrughna, Narayana, Brahma, Kausalya, Kaikeyi, Sumitra
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** King Dasharatha performs the Ashwamedha sacrifice and later the Putrakameshti yagna to obtain sons. The gods, pleased with the offerings, decide to incarnate as monkeys and bears to assist Vishnu, who will be born as Dasharatha's sons to defeat Ravana. Dasharatha's queens give birth to four sons: Rama, Bharata, Lakshmana, and Shatrughna. The sage Vishwamitra visits Dasharatha's court.

#### Q1

**Question:** On which tithi, determined by the priests, did Dasharatha release the sacrificial horse after performing all the yajna rites?

**Options:**
- 1. Chaitra Shuddha Navami
- 2. Chaitra Shuddha Purnima
- 3. Chaitra Shuddha Dashami
- 4. Chaitra Shuddha Ekadashi

**Correct answer:** Chaitra Shuddha Purnima

**Key entities:** Dasharatha

#### Q2

**Question:** After the sacrificial horse returned and Dasharatha completed the Ashwamedha yagna according to scriptural rites, which yagna did he perform to obtain sons?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishwajit Yagna
- 2. Vajapeya Yagna
- 3. Putrakameshti Yagna
- 4. Ishti Yagna

**Correct answer:** Putrakameshti Yagna

**Key entities:** Dasharatha

#### Q3

**Question:** In what form did the divine being appear at the yajna vedika and offer the fruit of the yajna to Dasharatha?

**Answer:** In the form of Payasa (a sweet porridge)

**Key entities:** Dasharatha

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the gods, satisfied with the offerings given by Dasharatha, decide according to future developments?

**Answer:** All the gods who had gathered at the yajna, thinking about the terrible atrocities of the demons, sought refuge in Narayana. At the request of all the gods, Narayana decided to incarnate on earth to destroy Ravana and other demons and protect the devotees. Brahma commanded all the gods to be born with their respective aspects to assist him. Thus, thousands of monkeys, bears, and langurs were born with divine aspects. Mahavishnu decided to be born as four sons to Dasharatha. After the yajna concluded, Dasharatha lived happily with his three pregnant queens, and a year passed.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Narayana, Ravana, Brahma

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Dasharatha's joy of having sons proceed?

**Answer:** Among the three pregnant queens, the senior queen Kausalya gave birth to a male child at the beginning of spring, on Chaitra Shuddha Navami, in the fourth quarter of the Punarvasu nakshatra, under the zodiac sign of Cancer. Then on Chaitra Shuddha Dashami, Queen Kaikeyi gave birth to a male child. Later that same day, Sumitra gave birth to two male children. Eleven days after the birth of the sons, Dasharatha performed the Jatakarma and naming ceremonies, gave generous gifts to the deserving, and rejoiced. Sage Vashistha came and named the eldest Rama, Kaikeyi's son Bharata, and Sumitra's sons Lakshmana and Shatrughna. Dasharatha, who had been without children for a long time, spent his time in great joy with his four sons. Among them, his love for the eldest Rama was greater than his own life. He had the four princes study the Vedas and scriptures under a guru. They became proficient in archery and were devoted to the welfare of the people. Rama, the great scion of the Raghu dynasty, possessed invincible valor. From childhood, Lakshmana was devoted to his elder brother Rama. Dasharatha was filled with supreme joy with his four sons, who were endowed with auspicious marks. Rama's childhood passed joyfully with his brothers, with learning and humility, and they all reached youth. One day, while Dasharatha was holding court, the great sage Vishwamitra arrived. Dasharatha welcomed the sage and worshipped him appropriately.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kausalya, Kaikeyi, Sumitra, Rama, Bharata, Lakshmana, Shatrughna

### Chapter 4: Fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 19-24
- Source PDF pages: 13, 14, 15
- Printed page numbers: 17, 18, 19
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Rama, Vasishta, Lakshmana, Shiva, Tataka, Maricha, Shatrughna, Bharata, Sumantra, Jabali, Kausalya, Indra
- Places: Sarayu, Ganga

**Summary:** Vishwamitra asks King Dasharatha to send Rama to protect his sacrifice. Dasharatha initially hesitates but agrees on the advice of Vashishta. Rama and Lakshmana accompany Vishwamitra, who teaches them the Bala and Atibala vidyas. They travel to the confluence of Sarayu and Ganga, where Vishwamitra narrates the story of the place, including Shiva's destruction of Manmatha. They then cross the Ganga and enter a forest, where Vishwamitra tells the story of the demoness Tataka and her son Maricha, who have devastated the Malada and Karusha kingdoms.

#### Q1

**Question:** Whom did Vishwamitra ask King Dasharatha to send with him for the protection of the sacrifice he had undertaken?

**Options:**
- 1. Shatrughna
- 2. Lakshmana
- 3. Bharata
- 4. Rama

**Correct answer:** Rama

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Following Vishwamitra's request, Dasharatha expressed his inability to send his eldest son Rama. On whose advice did he agree?

**Options:**
- 1. Sumantra
- 2. Vashishta
- 3. Jabali
- 4. Queen Kausalya

**Correct answer:** Vashishta

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Vasishta

#### Q3

**Question:** When Rama and Lakshmana, following Vishwamitra, were stopped by the sage at a place south of the Sarayu river, what were the names of the vidyas (knowledge) he taught them?

**Answer:** Bala and Atibala

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sarayu

#### Q4

**Question:** Rama and Lakshmana rested on the banks of the Sarayu. Waking up at dawn, they traveled some distance and reached a place. How did Vishwamitra answer their doubt about that place?

**Answer:** Rama and Lakshmana, traveling with their guru, saw the holy confluence of the Sarayu and Ganga. There, sages had been performing penance for thousands of years. The princes asked Vishwamitra, 'O great sage! Whose is this holy hermitage? Who are the great men living here? Tell us its ancient history.' Then the sage said, 'O Rama! In ancient times, Lord Shiva performed penance here. Once, Manmatha (Kamadeva) tried to disturb Shiva's penance. Shiva looked at him in anger, and Manmatha was burnt to ashes in that fiery gaze. Since then, Manmatha became bodiless and is called Ananga. Because Kama (desire) abandoned his body (anga), this region became Angadesha. All the ascetics here are devoted to Shiva. O princes! Let us spend this night at this holy confluence of Ganga and Sarayu. Tomorrow we can cross the Ganga.' So they all rested there.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sarayu, Ganga, Shiva

#### Q5

**Question:** After crossing the Ganga, Rama and Lakshmana traveled some distance and saw a terrible forest. When they asked Vishwamitra about the history of that forest, how did the sage explain?

**Answer:** Sage Vishwamitra said to Rama, 'My son! In ancient times, this place consisted of two kingdoms called Malada and Karusha. They were abundant in wealth and grain. After some time, a yakshini named Tataka, who had the strength of a thousand elephants from birth, roamed here assuming any form she wished. She was the wife of the mighty Sunda. She had a son named Maricha, who was as strong as Indra. The wicked Tataka constantly destroyed the two kingdoms of Malada and Karusha, making them devoid of human habitation. Since then, this region became a desolate forest. Rama! Do not fear; you will be safe. We must now cross this Tataka forest.' Saying this, Vishwamitra walked ahead, and Rama and Lakshmana followed.

**Key entities:** Ganga, Rama, Lakshmana, Tataka, Maricha, Indra

### Chapter 5: Fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 25-30
- Source PDF pages: 15, 16, 17
- Printed page numbers: 19, 20, 21
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Tataka, Maricha, Subahu, Agastya, Vali, Indra
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana accompany Vishwamitra to Siddhashrama, where Rama kills the demoness Tataka. Vishwamitra bestows celestial weapons on Rama and later on Lakshmana. Rama protects Vishwamitra's sacrifice by defeating the demons Maricha and Subahu.

#### Q1

**Question:** Which sage cursed the yakshini Tataka, saying 'Because of various reasons you have come to devour me, may you become a terrible demoness living on human flesh'?

**Options:**
- 1. Agastya
- 2. Vishwamitra
- 3. Vasishtha
- 4. Jamadagni

**Correct answer:** Agastya

**Key entities:** Tataka, Agastya

#### Q2

**Question:** At what time did Rama slay Tataka, following the command of sage Vishwamitra?

**Options:**
- 1. As midday approached
- 2. As the first twilight approached
- 3. As the last twilight approached
- 4. At night

**Correct answer:** As the last twilight approached

**Key entities:** Rama, Tataka

#### Q3

**Question:** After being pleased with the slaying of Tataka, Vishwamitra gave various celestial weapons along with their invocation and dismissal mantras to Rama. Later, who taught all those weapons to Lakshmana?

**Answer:** Rama

**Key entities:** Tataka, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q4

**Question:** When Rama asked about the history of Siddhashrama, how did Vishwamitra explain it to him?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra, upon being asked by Rama, explained about Siddhashrama: 'Rama! Lord Mahavishnu performed penance here for ages. The great ascetic Kashyapa performed penance here and attained perfection. Here, Mahavishnu was born as Vamana to Aditi and Kashyapa, and begged three steps of land from King Bali. Then, becoming Trivikrama, the all-pervading Supreme Self, he sent Bali to the netherworld and gave heaven to Indra. This place is sanctified by the touch of the great Vamana's feet. Hence it is called Siddhashrama. Therefore I have taken refuge here. My son Rama! Obstructionist demons often come to this hermitage. It is here that you must slay those wicked ones.' As Vishwamitra entered the hermitage, the sages residing in Siddhashrama welcomed Vishwamitra, Rama, and Lakshmana with honors.

**Key entities:** Rama, Vali, Indra, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana protect the sacrifice being performed by Vishwamitra?

**Answer:** Rama and Lakshmana said to Vishwamitra, who was initiated into the sacrifice, 'O Brahmarshi! When will the demons who obstruct the sacrifice come? We remain vigilant to stop them.' Hearing this, the sages there rejoiced and told them, 'From today, for six days, Vishwamitra will be in a vow of silence. O princes! You must remain alert and protect the sacrifice for these six days.' Then Rama and Lakshmana, bearing bows and arrows, guarded the sacrifice for five days. On the sixth day, as the sacrifice was proceeding properly with Vedic mantras, a terrible sound was heard from the sky. The fearsome demons Maricha and Subahu, along with their followers, came there wielding their illusions and scattered blood and flesh on the sacrificial altar. Then Rama of the Raghu dynasty, using the human weapon called 'Shiteshu', struck Maricha so that he fell into the ocean. Then, using the Agneya weapon, he killed Subahu. Thus, after Rama also slew other obstructionist demons, the blood and flesh scattered on the altar, being the demons' illusions, vanished from sight. After the sacrifice was completed without obstruction, Vishwamitra praised and blessed Rama and Lakshmana. In this way, Rama protected the sacrifice.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Maricha, Subahu

### Chapter 6: Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 31-36
- Source PDF pages: 17, 18, 19, 20
- Printed page numbers: 21, 22, 23, 24
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Kusha, Parvati, Vishvamitra, Brahma, Menaka, Shiva
- Places: Mithila, Ganga

**Summary:** After the completion of the sacrifice, following Vishwamitra's suggestion, Rama and Lakshmana set out for Sita's swayamvara in Mithila. They travel north, stopping at the Shona River. Rama asks about the region, and Vishwamitra recounts his lineage, including Kusha, Kushanabha, Gadhi, and the story of his sister Satyavati (Kaushiki). Later, at the Ganges, Vishwamitra narrates the origins of Ganga and Parvati, daughters of Himavan, and the descent of Ganga due to Bhagiratha.

#### Q1

**Question:** After the completion of the sacrifice, following Vishwamitra's suggestion, Rama and Lakshmana set out for Sita's swayamvara in Mithila. In which direction did they travel from Siddhashrama?

**Options:**
- 1. East
- 2. South
- 3. West
- 4. North

**Correct answer:** North

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Mithila

#### Q2

**Question:** All those traveling with Vishwamitra reached the banks of the Shona River by evening and rested there. Then Rama bowed to Vishwamitra and asked, 'O Guru! Under whose rule is this place where we are now?' Whose rule did Vishwamitra say the place was under?

**Options:**
- 1. Kusha
- 2. Kushanabha
- 3. Vasu
- 4. Adhurtarajas

**Correct answer:** Vasu

**Key entities:** Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** While answering Rama's question, Vishwamitra, in the course of telling the story of his ancestor Kushanabha's daughters, revealed who the progenitor of his lineage was?

**Answer:** Kaushika

**Key entities:** Rama, Vishvamitra

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the sage Vishwamitra describe the history of his lineage to Rama on the banks of the Shona River?

**Answer:** O Rama! Brahma's mind-born son is Kusha. His son Kushanabha had a hundred daughters, whom he married to Bhagadatta, the lord of Kampilya, and sent them to their in-laws' house. Later, the king, to compensate for the lack of sons, performed the Putrakameshti sacrifice. After some time, Kushanabha, through his wife Ghritachi, obtained a son named Gadhi. This Gadhi was highly righteous. The righteous king Gadhi is my father. Because I was born in the lineage of Kusha, I am also called Kaushika. O Rama! Satyavati is my sister. She was married to the sage Richika. Since my sister was also born in Kusha's lineage, she is also called Kaushiki. Being a great pativrata, she followed her husband and went to heaven with her physical body. Later, as the supremely generous Kaushiki, she flows as a great river on this earth. Due to my love for my sister, I reside on the banks of the Kaushiki River. O Rama! For the purpose of performing a sacrifice, I came here from that region. By your valor in Siddhashrama, I have become fulfilled and am returning. In telling you about the special features of this region, I have also spoken about my lineage. Thus the sage concluded.

**Key entities:** Rama, Brahma, Kusha, Vishvamitra

#### Q5

**Question:** Where and how did Vishwamitra describe the special features of Ganga and Parvati to Sri Rama?

**Answer:** Following Vishwamitra, Rama and others traveled some distance and reached the banks of the holy Ganges by midday. After completing their baths in the holy Ganges and offering libations to the ancestors, Rama asked about the story of the Ganges. Vishwamitra said: O Rama! Menaka and Himavan had two daughters. The elder daughter is Ganga Devi, and the second daughter is Parvati Devi. Once, the gods, for their own purpose, asked Himavan to hand over Ganga to them. The righteous Himavan, for the welfare of the world, handed over Ganga, who flows everywhere, to them. The second daughter, Parvati Devi, while still a maiden, performed severe penance, desiring to obtain Shankara as her husband through her vow. Himavan, according to his daughter's wish, gave her in marriage to Parama Shiva. Born as a daughter of Himavan and reaching the heavens, this holy Ganga is this Ganges River. Pleased with Vishwamitra's narration of Ganga's story, Rama asked: O Maharshi! How did this Ganges River come to be called Tripathaga? Then Kaushika told the story of the birth of Kumaraswami and also explained how Ganga descended from heaven to earth due to Bhagiratha. Thus Vishwamitra fully narrated the story of the Ganges as asked by Rama.

**Key entities:** Ganga, Parvati, Rama, Menaka, Shiva, Vishvamitra

### Chapter 7: Seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 37-42
- Source PDF pages: 20, 21, 22
- Printed page numbers: 24, 25, 26
- Key entities: Indra, Brahma, Narayana
- Places: Ganga, Himalaya

**Summary:** This chapter covers the story of King Sagara's horse sacrifice, the theft of the horse by Indra, the search by Sagara's 60,000 sons, their destruction by Kapila's anger, and the eventual retrieval of the horse by Anshuman. It also includes the later efforts of Dilipa and Bhagiratha to bring the Ganga to earth to purify the ashes of Sagara's sons.

#### Q1

**Question:** At the request of all the gods, whom did Lord Brahma appoint as their commander?

**Options:**
- 1. Vighneshwara
- 2. Kumaraswami
- 3. Nandishwara
- 4. Vishvaksena

**Correct answer:** Kumaraswami

**Key entities:** Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** Because Emperor Sagara had no children, he went to the Himalayas with his two wives and performed penance for whom?

**Options:**
- 1. Parashiva
- 2. Lord Brahma
- 3. Bhrigu Maharshi
- 4. Narayana

**Correct answer:** Bhrigu Maharshi

**Key entities:** Himalaya

#### Q3

**Question:** During the horse sacrifice, who stole the horse released by Emperor Sagara?

**Answer:** Indra

**Key entities:** Indra

#### Q4

**Question:** After the sacrificial horse was stolen, what effort did Sagara make to search for the horse?

**Answer:** Following the words of the priests that if the sacrifice is not completed without the horse, calamity will occur, Sagara summoned his sixty thousand sons and said, 'Dear sons! Because I am in the vow of the sacrifice, I cannot go. Therefore, you go and search for the sacrificial horse. Search everywhere on earth; if not found, dig the earth and go to the netherworld and search. May you be blessed.' Thus he sent them. They all set out and searched everywhere on earth, but found no trace of the horse. Then each of them took a yojana, dug the earth, and reached the netherworld. There they saw the sacrificial horse near the hermitage of Kapila Maharshi, and thinking that the sage had stolen the horse, they all abused Kapilacharya. Enraged by their harsh words and behavior, Kapila Maharshi roared. By Kapila's roar, the sons of Sagara were burnt to ashes. Thus Sagara's effort failed.

**Key entities:** None listed

#### Q5

**Question:** Who brought back Sagara's sacrificial horse and in what manner, completing the sacrifice? What became of the sons of Sagara who lay as heaps of ashes?

**Answer:** King Sagara, worried that his children did not return for a long time, called his grandson Anshuman and said, 'Dear son! Your uncles went in search of the sacrificial horse and have not returned. You go, find your uncles and the sacrificial horse, and bring them back to complete the sacrifice.' Immediately, Anshuman obeyed his grandfather's command, followed the path his uncles had taken by digging the earth to the netherworld, and there in the hermitage of Kapila Maharshi saw all his relatives lying as heaps of ashes. Following the suggestion of Garutman, he took the sacrificial horse and completed the sacrifice. Then Anshuman informed his grandfather Sagara that his uncles had been reduced to ashes by Kapila's anger, and to grant them the attainment of the world of the fathers, the sacred celestial Ganga had to be brought to earth. Thereafter, Sagara, while contemplating the attainment of the higher worlds for his sons, passed away. Subsequently, Anshuman and Dilipa in turn made efforts to bring Ganga to earth for the salvation of their ancestors, but they did not succeed. Finally, Dilipa's son Bhagiratha prayed to Lord Brahma, Ganga, and Ishwara. Pleased with his penance, Parameshthi bore Ganga and released her onto the earth. Ganga followed Bhagiratha, moistened the ashes of the king's ancestors, and granted them the worlds of the fathers. Thus, due to Bhagiratha, his ancestors attained the higher worlds.

**Key entities:** Ganga, Brahma

### Chapter 8: Eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 43-49
- Source PDF pages: 22, 23, 24
- Printed page numbers: 26, 27, 28
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Gautama, Ahalya, Shiva, Indra, Dasharatha
- Places: Ganga, Kailasa, Mithila, Himalaya

**Summary:** This chapter covers the journey of Rama, Lakshmana, and Vishwamitra. They cross the Ganga, visit the city of Vishala, and hear the story of Gautama's hermitage and Ahalya's curse and liberation. The chapter also includes the story of Diti's pregnancy and the Maruts, and the narrative of Bhagiratha bringing Ganga to earth.

#### Q1

**Question:** Where did Lord Shiva release the Ganga from his matted locks after hearing Bhagiratha's plea?

**Options:**
- 1. Kanchanaganga
- 2. Kailasa Mountain
- 3. Bindu Sarovara
- 4. Kedarnath

**Correct answer:** Bindu Sarovara

**Key entities:** Shiva, Ganga

#### Q2

**Question:** After crossing the Ganga, Vishwamitra and others traveled north and reached a city. At Rama's request, Vishwamitra described that city. What is its name?

**Options:**
- 1. Kashi
- 2. Avanti
- 3. Dwaraka
- 4. Vishala

**Correct answer:** Vishala

**Key entities:** Ganga, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Diti, with her husband Kashyapa Prajapati's permission, conceived a child capable of killing Indra. Knowing this, Indra entered her womb and cut the fetus into seven pieces. Later, those body parts became deities by Indra's grace. What are they called in the world?

**Answer:** Sapta Maruts

**Key entities:** Indra

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Vishwamitra describe Gautama's hermitage to Rama when asked?

**Answer:** While traveling from Vishala towards Mithila, Vishwamitra and others saw an ancient hermitage. Rama asked whose it was. Vishwamitra said it was the hermitage of the great sage Gautama, once radiant and worshipped by gods. Gautama performed penance there with his wife Ahalya for many years. Once, when Gautama was away, Indra came disguised as Gautama and enjoyed conjugal bliss with Ahalya. Knowing this, Gautama cursed Indra to be without testicles, and told Ahalya to perform penance unseen for years, until Rama, son of Dasharatha, would visit and liberate her. Then Gautama went to the Himalayas to perform penance. Thus Vishwamitra told Rama about Gautama's hermitage.

**Key entities:** Gautama, Rama, Mithila, Ahalya, Indra, Dasharatha, Himalaya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Ahalya's liberation from the curse occur?

**Answer:** After describing Gautama's hermitage, Vishwamitra told Rama to grant liberation to Ahalya. Following Vishwamitra's command, Rama entered the hermitage with Lakshmana. He saw Ahalya, radiant with severe penance. Due to Gautama's curse, she was invisible until Rama's arrival. Upon seeing Rama, she was freed from the curse and became visible to all. Then Ahalya bowed to Rama and Lakshmana and offered them hospitality. Then Gautama appeared and, along with Ahalya, worshipped Rama joyfully. Thereafter, Gautama and Ahalya continued their ascetic life in the hermitage. Then Rama, with Lakshmana, set out for Mithila with Vishwamitra.

**Key entities:** Ahalya, Gautama, Rama, Lakshmana, Mithila

### Chapter 9: Ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 50-56
- Source PDF pages: 24, 25, 26
- Printed page numbers: 28, 29, 30
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Janaka, Ahalya, Gautama, Shiva, Brahma, Shatananda, Sumantra, Jabali, Kushadhvaja
- Places: Mithila, Himalaya

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana, accompanying Vishwamitra, reach Mithila and are honored by King Janaka. They meet the son of Ahalya and Gautama. The chapter recounts Vishwamitra's past: his conflict with Vasishtha over the divine cow Shabala, his defeat, his penance to Shiva, and his subsequent attack on Vasishtha's hermitage, which is thwarted by Vasishtha's brahma power.

#### Q1

**Question:** Rama and Lakshmana, who reached Mithila with Vishwamitra, received the hospitality of King Janaka and there they met the son of Ahalya and Gautama. What is his name?

**Options:**
- 1. Sudhamanu
- 2. Shatananda
- 3. Sumantra
- 4. Jabali

**Correct answer:** Shatananda

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Mithila, Janaka, Ahalya, Gautama, Shatananda

#### Q2

**Question:** In Mithila, who told Rama the past history of Vishwamitra?

**Options:**
- 1. Shatananda
- 2. Janaka
- 3. Kushadhvaja
- 4. Sudhamanu

**Correct answer:** Shatananda

**Key entities:** Mithila, Rama, Shatananda

#### Q3

**Question:** King Vishwamitra came to Vasishtha's hermitage with his retinue, accepted the hospitality of the sage, and was pleased. He then asked Vasishtha for the cow that was the cause of such hospitality. What is the name of that cow?

**Answer:** Shabala

**Key entities:** None listed

#### Q4

**Question:** When Vasishtha refused the cow, what did Vishwamitra do? What happened subsequently?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra, seeing that Vasishtha provided food for him and his retinue merely by his will, was astonished and asked for the wish-fulfilling cow named Shabala, offering a hundred thousand cows in exchange. Vasishtha refused, so Vishwamitra tried to take the cow by force. With Vasishtha's permission, Shabala created thousands of armies from her bellow. Vishwamitra's entire army was destroyed by Shabala's forces. Vishwamitra then mounted his chariot and used various weapons, but Shabala created even more powerful armies from her body. Vishwamitra's hundred sons attacked Vasishtha, but the sage reduced them to ashes with a roar. Thus Vishwamitra's attempt failed.

**Key entities:** None listed

#### Q5

**Question:** After being defeated by Vasishtha, what did Vishwamitra do next?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra, with all his forces including his sons destroyed, became powerless like a snake with its fangs removed. Overcome with despair, he went to his kingdom, handed over the kingdom to his only son who followed the Kshatriya dharma, and went to the Himalayas to perform severe penance to please Shiva. Shiva appeared and granted him a boon: knowledge of the Upanishads and mastery of all weapons used by gods, demons, sages, gandharvas, yakshas, and rakshasas. Puffed up with pride, Vishwamitra went to Vasishtha's hermitage to take revenge. He destroyed the hermitage with his weapons. Vasishtha, angry, stood with his brahma staff, and all of Vishwamitra's weapons became powerless in its shadow. Realizing that Kshatriya strength is nothing compared to brahma power, Vishwamitra renounced his Kshatriya pride and went to practice severe penance.

**Key entities:** Himalaya, Shiva, Brahma

### Chapter 10: Tenth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 57-62
- Source PDF pages: 26, 27, 28
- Printed page numbers: 30, 31, 32
- Key entities: Vasishta, Trishanku, Brahma, Indra, Ambarisha, Agni
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** This chapter narrates the story of Vishwamitra's penance, his conflict with Vasishta, and his assistance to King Trishanku and Shunashepa. It includes Vishwamitra's determination to become a Brahmarishi, his help to Trishanku to ascend to heaven with his physical body, and his rescue of Shunashepa from being a sacrificial animal.

#### Q1

**Question:** Disturbed due to the enmity with Vasishta, Vishwamitra went south with a firm resolve and performed intense penance on Lord Brahma. When the Grandfather (Brahma) appeared, as which rishi did he recognize Vishwamitra?

**Options:**
- 1. As a Brahmarshi
- 2. As a Rajarshi
- 3. As a Devarshi
- 4. As a Maharshi

**Correct answer:** As a Rajarshi

**Key entities:** Vasishta, Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** When King Trishanku, the lord of Ayodhya, requested to perform a sacrifice so that he could go to heaven with his physical body, how did the angry sons of Vasishta curse him, refusing to agree?

**Options:**
- 1. Become a Chandala
- 2. Become an animal form
- 3. Become a stone form
- 4. Become deprived of kingdom

**Correct answer:** Become a Chandala

**Key entities:** Trishanku, Ayodhya, Vasishta

#### Q3

**Question:** Whom did Trishanku, who received the curse from the guru's sons, approach?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra

**Key entities:** Trishanku

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Vishwamitra welcome Trishanku who sought his refuge?

**Answer:** Trishanku, neglected by Vasishta and his sons, sought refuge in Vishwamitra. Vishwamitra, taking in Trishanku who was rejected by his enemy, decided to perform a sacrifice according to his wish. He immediately called his sons and said, 'Trishanku has requested me to enable him to go to heaven with his physical body. We must fulfill his wish and perform the sacrifice. Therefore, gather the necessary materials.' Then he called his disciples and said, 'Invite all the rishis, their disciples, the priests, and the scholars of Vedas and scriptures, telling them it is my command.' Accordingly, everyone came as per Vishwamitra's order. He said, 'Let us all perform the sacrifice and by its power send Trishanku to heaven with his physical body.' They all agreed and performed the sacrifice according to the scriptures. As a result, Trishanku went to heaven with his physical body. There, Lord Indra, saying 'You are unworthy of heaven due to the guru's curse,' threw Trishanku headlong from heaven. Knowing this, Vishwamitra, with his power, stopped Trishanku in the sky, created another heaven, and said, 'Let this heaven be Trishanku's abode, and let all the gods agree to this.' All the gods agreed. Placing Trishanku in the heaven he created, Vishwamitra completed the sacrifice with his officiating priests.

**Key entities:** Trishanku, Vasishta, Indra

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Vishwamitra save Shunashepa, who was going as a sacrificial animal for King Ambarisha?

**Answer:** Once, King Ambarisha of Ayodhya started a sacrifice. Indra stole the sacrificial animal. Then the officiating priest told the king, 'Due to your negligence, the sacrificial animal has been stolen. If you cannot bring back the animal, you may offer cows as a substitute and obtain a human being as a sacrificial animal. Make appropriate efforts.' As part of such efforts, Ambarisha visited Rishi Ruchika and gave him a hundred thousand cows, obtaining his second son Shunashepa as a sacrificial animal. While returning, Shunashepa sought refuge with his maternal uncle Vishwamitra on the way. By the power of the mantra given by that sage, at the time of the sacrifice's conclusion, Shunashepa worshipped Agni and praised Indra and Upendra. Then Lord Indra, pleased, granted long life to Shunashepa and the fruit of the sacrifice to Ambarisha. Thus, by Vishwamitra's instruction, Shunashepa was saved from mortal danger.

**Key entities:** Ambarisha, Ayodhya, Indra, Agni

### Chapter 11: Eleventh Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 63-67
- Source PDF pages: 28, 29, 30, 31
- Printed page numbers: 32, 33, 34, 35
- Key entities: Shiva, Sita, Rama, Menaka, Shatananda, Brahma, Janaka, Lakshmana, Dasharatha
- Places: Ayodhya, Mithila

**Summary:** This chapter continues the story of Vishwamitra's penance and his attainment of Brahmarshi status. It also describes the history of Shiva's bow, Sita's swayamvara, and the breaking of the bow by Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who was the incomparably beautiful apsara who disrupted Vishwamitra's penance at Pushkara Tirtha?

**Options:**
- 1. Punjakasthala
- 2. Urvashi
- 3. Menaka
- 4. Tilottama

**Correct answer:** Menaka

**Key entities:** Menaka

#### Q2

**Question:** While describing the story of Vishwamitra to Rama, Shatananda said that Brahma declared Vishwamitra a Brahmarshi. In which direction was Vishwamitra performing penance when that declaration occurred?

**Options:**
- 1. South
- 2. West
- 3. North
- 4. East

**Correct answer:** East

**Key entities:** Rama, Shatananda, Brahma

#### Q3

**Question:** After being granted Brahmarshihood by Brahma, Vishwamitra said that he would cease his penance if someone called him 'Brahmarshi'.

**Answer:** Vasishtha

**Key entities:** Brahma

#### Q4

**Question:** How did King Janaka explain to Vishwamitra the history of Shiva's bow and the announcement of Sita's swayamvara?

**Answer:** Vishwamitra Maharshi said to King Janaka: 'O king! Your house has the bow of Shiva. These princes of Ayodhya, Rama and Lakshmana, wish to see it. Please show it.' Then Janaka bowed to the sage and said humbly: 'O Brahmarshi! This bow of Shiva was once given by Lord Shiva, who was angered during the destruction of Daksha's sacrifice and later propitiated by the gods. Pleased, Shankara gave this bow to the gods. They entrusted it to Devarata, the sixth in our Nimi dynasty. Since then, this bow has been worshipped in our house. O revered sage! Once, while plowing the earth for a sacrifice, a girl emerged from the furrow. I named her 'Sita' and raised her. Now that my daughter Sita has come of age, I announced that valor itself is the bride-price, and only a valiant man can marry my daughter. Hearing my proclamation, many princes came and displayed their prowess, but none could string Shiva's bow. O Brahmarshi! With your permission, I will show this powerful bow to Rama and Lakshmana. I will give my daughter to whoever strings this bow.' Thus Janaka explained to Vishwamitra.

**Key entities:** Janaka, Shiva, Sita, Ayodhya, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the breaking of Shiva's bow occur during Sita's swayamvara?

**Answer:** By King Janaka's order, his ministers had the chest containing Shiva's bow brought to the assembly hall by strong soldiers. Then the king said to Vishwamitra: 'O guru! Here, I have had Shiva's bow brought. The princes with you may see it.' Then Vishwamitra said: 'My son Rama, look at this bow.' Then that descendant of Raghu approached the chest, saw the bow, and said: 'O guru! I will touch this great bow, lift it, and string it.' Janaka and Vishwamitra agreed. Then, as thousands of onlookers watched, Sri Rama, following the sage's command, grasped the middle of the bow, effortlessly lifted it, and stood it upright. Then that best of men strung the bow and drew it to his ear. Immediately the bow broke with a loud 'Phel' sound. At the sound of the bow breaking, bells jingled. Sita's body thrilled with wonder and joy. Then King Janaka said: 'O sage! I have seen with my own eyes the valor of Sri Rama, son of Dasharatha. I did not imagine such a heroic deed. My daughter Sita, obtaining Sri Rama as her husband, will bring glory to both families.' Then, with the permission of Vishwamitra and Sri Rama, Janaka sent his ministers to Ayodhya to inform King Dasharatha of the details of Sita's swayamvara and invite him to Mithila. Thus the news of the breaking of Shiva's bow reached the citizens of Mithila and Ayodhya, and everyone rejoiced.

**Key entities:** Shiva, Sita, Janaka, Rama, Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Mithila

### Chapter 12: Twelfth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 68-72
- Source PDF pages: 31, 32, 33
- Printed page numbers: 35, 36, 37
- Key entities: Janaka, Dasharatha, Vasishta, Rama, Lakshmana, Bharata, Shatrughna, Sita, Urmila, Shatananda, Brahma, Trishanku, Ambarisha
- Places: Ayodhya, Mithila

**Summary:** King Janaka sends messengers to Ayodhya to invite King Dasaratha for the wedding. Dasaratha arrives with his family. Sage Vasishta narrates the Ikshvaku dynasty lineage, and King Janaka narrates the Videha dynasty lineage. The marriages of Rama, Lakshmana, Bharata, and Shatrughna are arranged with Sita, Urmila, and the daughters of Kushadhwaja.

#### Q1

**Question:** Carrying King Janaka's message, the ministers and messengers traveled day and night and reached Ayodhya in how many days?

**Options:**
- 1. Two days
- 2. Three days
- 3. Four days
- 4. Five days

**Correct answer:** Three days

**Key entities:** Janaka, Ayodhya

#### Q2

**Question:** Janaka summoned Shatananda and ordered him to make arrangements to invite his brother, who ruled Sankashya city, along with his family for the auspicious wedding. What is the name of that brother of King Janaka?

**Options:**
- 1. Maharoma
- 2. Devarata
- 3. Hrasvaroma
- 4. Kushadhwaja

**Correct answer:** Kushadhwaja

**Key entities:** Janaka, Shatananda

#### Q3

**Question:** After everyone was comfortably seated at the wedding altar, through whom did King Dasaratha have his dynasty's lineage narrated?

**Answer:** Through Vasishta

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Vasishta

#### Q4

**Question:** How were the genealogies of the Ikshvaku and Videha royal dynasties described?

**Answer:** After both sides' wedding parties arrived and were seated at the altar, at Dasaratha's request, Vasishta described the Ikshvaku dynasty lineage: Brahma's mind-born son Marichi, his son Kashyapa, Kashyapa's son Vaivasvata Manu, and Manu's son Ikshvaku, who was the first ruler of Ayodhya. Ikshvaku's son Kukṣi, and the lineage continued with Trishanku, Mandhata, Bharata, Sagara, Bhagiratha, Kakutstha, Raghu, Ambarisha, Nahusha, and Yayati. Then Yayati's son Nahusha, Nahusha's son Ajā, and Ajā's son Dasaratha, who had four sons: Rama, Bharata, Lakshmana, and Shatrughna. Then King Janaka said: 'O great sage, our lineage is also renowned. As the bride's father should also declare his lineage, I am describing ours. The famous Nimi was the founder of our dynasty. His son Mithi built Mithila and was the first Janaka. Hence our dynasty is called Janaka. It was sanctified by many famous kings like Devarata, Brihadratha, Haryashva, Kirtirata, Maharoma, and Svarnaroma. My father Hrasvaroma handed over the kingdom to me and retired to the forest.' Thus he described his lineage.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Vasishta, Brahma, Ayodhya, Trishanku, Bharata, Rama, Ambarisha, Lakshmana, Shatrughna, Janaka, Mithila

#### Q5

**Question:** How were the marriages of Lakshmana, Bharata, and Shatrughna decided?

**Answer:** After King Dasaratha arrived at Mithila with his family and retinue at Janaka's invitation, while everyone was joyfully together, Sage Vasishta said to King Janaka: 'O king, it would be excellent if you give your daughters Sita and Urmila in marriage to Rama and Lakshmana, who are born in the Ikshvaku dynasty.' Janaka bowed and agreed. After the genealogies were recited, Vishwamitra said to Janaka: 'O king, both the Ikshvaku and Videha dynasties are incomparably glorious. These marital alliances between the two dynasties are appropriate in every way. I wish to say something: it would be good if you give your brother Kushadhwaja's two daughters in marriage to Bharata and Shatrughna. All of Dasaratha's sons are handsome and youthful, so this alliance will be beneficial for both families.' Hearing Vishwamitra's words with Vasishta's consent, King Janaka humbly folded his hands and said: 'O great sages, may your words, spoken for our welfare, come true. So be it. Let these four valiant princes marry these princesses on the same day.' Thus he gave his consent.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Bharata, Shatrughna, Dasharatha, Mithila, Janaka, Vasishta, Sita, Urmila, Rama

### Chapter 13: Thirteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Bala Kanda
- Sarga range: 73-77
- Source PDF pages: 33, 34, 35, 36
- Printed page numbers: 37, 38, 39, 40
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Vasishta, Parashurama, Vishnu, Dasharatha, Janaka, Shatananda, Urmila, Mandavi, Shrutakirti, Kushadhvaja, Shiva, Narayana
- Places: Himalaya, Ayodhya

**Summary:** The chapter describes the wedding ceremonies of Rama and his brothers with Sita and her sisters, conducted by Sage Vashishta. After the weddings, Sage Vishwamitra departs to the Himalayas. On the return journey to Ayodhya, Parashurama confronts Rama, but Rama strings Vishnu's bow and shoots an arrow that destroys Parashurama's earned merit, causing Parashurama to retreat to Mahendragiri.

#### Q1

**Question:** King Dasharatha came to the wedding pavilion with his sons and all the sages. Then Janaka, bringing his daughters adorned with all ornaments, came to the wedding altar and requested whom to conduct all the wedding rites along with all the sages?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishwamitra
- 2. Shatananda
- 3. Vashishta
- 4. Vamadeva

**Correct answer:** Vashishta

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Janaka, Vasishta

#### Q2

**Question:** After the wedding of Sita and Rama was completed, the next day Sage Vishwamitra blessed all the brides and grooms and went where?

**Options:**
- 1. To the Himalayan regions
- 2. To the Vindhya mountain
- 3. To the Gandhara country
- 4. To Mahendragiri

**Correct answer:** To the Himalayan regions

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** When King Dasharatha set out for Ayodhya with his four sons, four daughters-in-law, and his retinue, which sage blocked their path?

**Answer:** Parashurama

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Parashurama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the weddings of Sita, Urmila, Mandavi, and Shrutakirti take place?

**Answer:** The wedding pavilion was decorated with fragrant flowers and mango festoons. All necessary materials were placed on the altar. With the cooperation of all sages, Sage Vashishta undertook to conduct the wedding ceremony, performing it auspiciously, according to scriptures, and with mantras. King Janaka completed the kanyadana (giving away the bride) for Sita and Urmila, and had his brother Kushadhvaja perform the kanyadana for Mandavi and Shrutakirti. Then, accepting Janaka's words, the four brothers, with Vashishta's approval, took their brides' hands and circumambulated the fire, the altar, King Janaka, and all the sages, bowing to them. Then, following the scriptures and Kalpa Sutras, Sage Vashishta continued the wedding ceremony. The gods in the sky showered flowers on the wedding of the Raghu dynasty. Seeing that auspicious celebration, virtuous men and women told each other that their births were fulfilled. Thus, those radiant newlyweds, holding each other's little fingers and with the knots of their garments tied, circumambulated the fire three times and completed the wedding ceremony. Then the four couples went to their respective lodgings.

**Key entities:** Sita, Urmila, Mandavi, Shrutakirti, Vasishta, Janaka, Kushadhvaja

#### Q5

**Question:** How was the danger in the form of Parashurama that came to Sri Rama while returning to Ayodhya after the wedding celebrations averted?

**Answer:** Dasharatha, who set out for Ayodhya with his four sons and daughters-in-law, bade farewell to King Janaka and others and traveled some distance. Then, Parashurama, carrying an axe on one shoulder and the Vaishnava bow in one hand, came towards them. Vashishta and others bowed to him and had Rama worship him. Then Parashurama said, 'O Rama! I heard that you broke Shiva's bow. I have brought another divine bow. This Vaishnava bow was placed by Narayana with our grandfather Richika. Take this, string it, and demonstrate your strength. Seeing your capability, I will fight a duel with you.' Hearing Parashurama's words, Dasharatha was frightened and prayed with folded hands. Then Rama said, 'O Bhargava! Breaking Shiva's bow was done according to Kshatriya dharma by merely drawing it. The breaking of the bow was only divine will. But you spoke considering me incapable. I do not accept that. See my prowess now.' Saying this, Rama took the Vaishnava bow from Parashurama's hand and strung an arrow. Since the arrow once shot should not go waste, he struck the meritorious worlds that Parashurama had earned through severe penance. Then Parashurama, helpless, realizing that Rama was none other than Maha Vishnu, went to Mahendragiri with the speed of mind. Thereafter, Dasharatha and all others happily reached Ayodhya.

**Key entities:** Parashurama, Rama, Ayodhya, Dasharatha, Janaka, Vasishta, Shiva, Narayana, Vishnu

### Chapter 14: Fourteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-6
- Source PDF pages: 36, 37, 38
- Printed page numbers: 40, 41, 42
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Rama, Vasishta, Sita, Bharata, Yudhajit, Kushadhvaja, Shatananda, Jabali, Sumantra, Narayana
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** King Dasharatha decides to crown Rama as prince regent and seeks the assembly's consent. He assigns the responsibility of the coronation arrangements to Sage Vashishta. Rama and Sita observe a fast and perform rituals. The citizens of Ayodhya celebrate the news of Rama's coronation with great joy.

#### Q1

**Question:** When King Dasharatha intended to crown Rama as prince regent and sought the consent of all in his assembly, Bharata was at his maternal uncle's house. What is the name of Bharata's maternal uncle?

**Options:**
- 1. Siradhvaja
- 2. Kushadhvaja
- 3. Yudhajit
- 4. Shatananda

**Correct answer:** Yudhajit

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Bharata, Yudhajit

#### Q2

**Question:** To whom did Dasharatha entrust the responsibility of conducting Rama's coronation?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishwamitra
- 2. Vashishta
- 3. Jabali
- 4. Jabali

**Correct answer:** Vashishta

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Vasishta

#### Q3

**Question:** King Dasharatha, having summoned Rama through Sumantra, said, 'My son! Tomorrow, on an auspicious asterism, you shall be crowned.' What is the name of that auspicious asterism?

**Answer:** Pushya Nakshatra

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Sumantra

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the fast of Sita and Rama proceed during the coronation?

**Answer:** Dasharatha told Sage Vashishta, 'O great sage! I have told Rama to undertake a fast. You also go and tell Sita to undertake the fast along with Rama.' Accordingly, Vashishta went to Rama's inner apartments and gave the fast initiation to Sita and Rama with mantras. Then Rama's palace was filled with joyous men and women. After Vashishta left, Rama completed his bath and other rituals, and with a steady mind, along with his wife Sita, worshipped Lord Narayana. Then, carrying a vessel containing offerings on his head, he circumambulated the fire and, facing Lord Mahavishnu, performed a homa according to the scriptures into the blazing fire. He then partook of the remaining offerings. Meditating on the supreme deity Mahavishnu, silently and with self-control, both of them lay down on a bed of darbha grass that was nicely spread in that chamber. Thus the fast of Sita and Rama continued.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Dasharatha, Vasishta, Narayana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the citizens of Ayodhya celebrate upon hearing the news of Rama's coronation?

**Answer:** Hearing the auspicious news of Rama's coronation, the citizens and countryfolk were overjoyed. They cleaned all the city streets, sprinkled water, and drew colorful designs. They decorated the city with door arches and garlands, making it resplendent. As the auspicious time for the coronation approached, the men and women in the city chatted in their courtyards and were delighted. Everywhere, people enjoyed the fine performances of actors and actresses, the graceful dance poses of dancers, and the sweet songs of singers. In honor of the great coronation festival, all citizens scattered colorful flowers on the royal roads. They made all the roads fragrant with incense and perfumed ointments. The people, adorned with splendor, praised King Dasharatha. They extolled the great king, the augmenter of the Ikshvaku dynasty, for recognizing his old age and deciding to crown Rama. They said, 'Rama, who knows the good and bad of all people, is going to be our lord. He will be our eternal protector. This fortune that has befallen us is the result of divine grace.' Thus all the people expressed their joy to one another.

**Key entities:** Ayodhya, Rama, Dasharatha

### Chapter 15: Fifteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 7-12
- Source PDF pages: 38, 39, 40
- Printed page numbers: 42, 43, 44
- Key entities: Kaikeyi, Rama, Mandara, Dasharatha, Bharata, Kausalya, Maricha, Subahu
- Places: Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Queen Kaikeyi is informed of Rama's impending coronation by her maid Manthara. She then reminds King Dasharatha of two boons he had promised her during a battle with Shambarasura, demanding that Bharata be crowned instead and Rama be exiled to the forest for fourteen years. Dasharatha is devastated and pleads with her, but she remains adamant.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who first informed Kaikeyi, one of Dasharatha's wives, about the news of Rama's coronation?

**Options:**
- 1. Dasharatha
- 2. Maid Manthara
- 3. Vamadeva
- 4. Kausalya

**Correct answer:** Maid Manthara

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Rama, Mandara

#### Q2

**Question:** During the war with whom did Dasharatha previously give two boons as a pledge to Kaikeyi?

**Options:**
- 1. Shambarasura
- 2. Maricha
- 3. Subahu
- 4. Sunda

**Correct answer:** Shambarasura

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kaikeyi

#### Q3

**Question:** When King Dasharatha entered Kaikeyi's inner palace to inform her of the auspicious coronation news, where was Kaikeyi?

**Answer:** In the anger room (kopagriha), lying on the bare floor

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kaikeyi

#### Q4

**Question:** In what manner and what kind of boons did Kaikeyi ask from King Dasharatha?

**Answer:** Kaikeyi, lying on the bare floor in the anger room, was approached by Dasharatha who pleaded with her. She demanded that he first swear an oath. Then she reminded him of the two boons he had given her during the war with Shambarasura. The first boon: Bharata should be crowned with the preparations made for Rama. The second boon: Rama should wear bark garments, mat his hair, and go to Dandaka forest for fourteen years of exile. Hearing this, Dasharatha became stunned.

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Bharata, Rama, Dandaka Forest

#### Q5

**Question:** How did King Dasharatha lament upon hearing the boons demanded by Kaikeyi?

**Answer:** Dasharatha was stunned, then regained consciousness and lamented, wondering if it was a dream or delusion. He then looked at Kaikeyi as if to burn her with his gaze and said, 'O cruel woman! What harm did Rama do to you? What fault did I commit? How did your mouth utter such a wish? The whole world praises Rama's virtues; what crime did he commit that I should abandon my son? I cannot live without Rama even for a moment. Give up the thought of sending him to the forest, Kaikeyi! I bow at your feet. Have mercy on this helpless man. Do you test my love for Bharata? I will give you the entire earth, but give up your anger towards Rama.' Despite his entreaties, she remained unmoved. Then she said, 'O king, I do not know whether crowning Bharata instead of Rama is righteous or unrighteous. I cannot go against the promise you gave me.' Hearing this, Dasharatha, bowing to his wife, collapsed in anguish.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kaikeyi, Rama, Bharata

### Chapter 16: Sixteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 13-18
- Source PDF pages: 40, 41, 42
- Printed page numbers: 44, 45, 46
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Kaikeyi, Sumantra, Rama, Vasishta, Bharata, Jabali
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** King Dasharatha, bound by his promise to Kaikeyi, is grief-stricken and collapses. At dawn, he sends Sumantra to summon Rama. Meanwhile, Sage Vasishta arrives in Ayodhya with the coronation materials and meets Sumantra. Rama comes to Kaikeyi's palace and learns from her that he must go into exile for fourteen years so that Bharata can be crowned.

#### Q1

**Question:** Seeing Kaikeyi who would not relent, King Dasharatha, overwhelmed with grief that his son would be separated from him, fell down where?

**Options:**
- 1. On a proper seat
- 2. In Kaikeyi's lap
- 3. On a swan-down bed
- 4. On the bare ground

**Correct answer:** On the bare ground

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha

#### Q2

**Question:** Pressed by Kaikeyi, King Dasharatha, bound by the rope of dharma, as dawn broke, sent whom to summon Rama to him?

**Options:**
- 1. Sumantra
- 2. Vasishta
- 3. The chamberlain
- 4. Jabali

**Correct answer:** Sumantra

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Rama, Sumantra

#### Q3

**Question:** Upon his father's summons from Kaikeyi's palace, Rama immediately set out on which vehicle?

**Answer:** Chariot

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sage Vasishta, who was responsible for conducting the coronation, come to the city of Ayodhya? What did the sage do in the city?

**Answer:** As the sun rose and the auspicious moment for the coronation approached, Sage Vasishta, accompanied by his disciples, gathered the coronation materials and set out from the hermitage to the city of Ayodhya. By the time he arrived, the city was beautifully decorated. The people, eager to see Rama's coronation, crowded the streets. The air was fragrant with sandalwood and aloe incense. Then Vasishta, surrounded by disciples, proceeded towards the inner palace. Sumantra came to meet him. Vasishta told Sumantra, 'Inform the king that I am here.' He also showed Sumantra all the materials he had brought for the auspicious coronation ceremony. Sumantra was pleased and, following Vasishta's command, entered the king's palace, proclaiming victory to the king. Not knowing the king's condition, Sumantra greeted him as usual with 'Good morning.' He said, 'Vasishta and others have arrived. You should complete your bath and other rituals and prepare for the coronation ceremony.' Thus, Sumantra, having come as per Vasishta's order, stood near the king.

**Key entities:** Vasishta, Ayodhya, Rama, Sumantra

#### Q5

**Question:** When Rama saw his father in Kaikeyi's palace, what news did he hear from Queen Kaikeyi?

**Answer:** Rama saw King Dasharatha sitting on a golden couch with a withered face, looking dejected, with Kaikeyi beside him. Rama bowed to his father's feet. Then, as the distressed Dasharatha uttered the words 'Father! Rama!', his eyes filled with tears, his throat choked, and he could not see. Seeing this, Rama was bewildered. Rama then bowed to Kaikeyi and asked, 'Mother! Why does our father appear angry like this? Have I committed any offense?' Kaikeyi replied, 'Rama! You are most dear to the king. I cannot bring myself to speak unpleasant words to you. He has given me a promise. That task can only be accomplished by you. If you promise me that you will surely fulfill it regardless of good or bad, then I will explain it fully. The king himself is unable to tell you.' Hearing Kaikeyi's words, Rama said, 'Mother! If it is the king's command, I am ready even to jump into fire. To uphold my father's word, I am ready even to drink deadly poison.' Having bound Rama by his promise, Kaikeyi said, 'Rama! I have now asked for the boons your father promised me long ago. The first is to crown Bharata, and the second is that you go to the forest today and spend fourteen years there. Your father gave me these two boons by promise. You uphold your father's truth.' Hearing his stepmother's words, Rama stood without any agitation.

**Key entities:** Rama, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Bharata

### Chapter 17: Seventeenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 19-24
- Source PDF pages: 42, 43, 44, 45
- Printed page numbers: 46, 47, 48, 49
- Key entities: Rama, Kaikeyi, Kausalya, Lakshmana, Dasharatha, Sumantra, Mandara, Bharata
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** Rama, determined to go to the forest, takes leave from Kaikeyi and then goes to his mother Kausalya. Lakshmana angrily opposes the exile, but Rama pacifies him by emphasizing obedience to parents. Kausalya laments and wants to accompany Rama, but Rama consoles her, urging her to serve King Dasaratha and wait for his return.

#### Q1

**Question:** Ready to renounce the kingdom and go to the forest, Sri Rama told Queen Kaikeyi from whom he would take leave?

**Options:**
- 1. Vasishtha
- 2. Queen Kausalya
- 3. Sumantra
- 4. Lakshmana

**Correct answer:** Queen Kausalya

**Key entities:** Rama, Kaikeyi, Kausalya

#### Q2

**Question:** When Lakshmana expressed his disagreement about Rama's exile, whom did Rama primarily cite as the cause for the kingdom slipping away and his exile?

**Options:**
- 1. Destiny
- 2. Father
- 3. Kaikeyi
- 4. Manthara

**Correct answer:** Destiny

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Before Rama came to Queen Kausalya's palace to inform her about his exile, did Kausalya already know the details of the news?

**Answer:** No

**Key entities:** Rama, Kausalya

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Lakshmana think about the exile? How did Rama pacify his younger brother?

**Answer:** Rama said that his renunciation of the coronation and going to the forest was due to fate alone. Hearing this, Lakshmana was torn between joy at his brother's adherence to dharma and sorrow at his leaving the kingdom. Then, like a wounded serpent, Lakshmana angrily said, 'Brother! Kaikeyi and Dasaratha are both selfish. They will only harm you. They are enemies in the guise of parents. You should not even mentally consent to their wishes. Brother! This is not done by them deliberately. It is not right for you to think it is merely divine. Now we will see which is greater: divine power or human prowess. Even if all the guardians of the directions and the thirty-three crore gods come, they cannot stop Rama's coronation today. Whoever opposes me, strong as I am, will drown in endless sorrow from my fierce manliness. Even destiny cannot save him. O Lord! I am your servant. Command me what I should do to make this earth yours.' Hearing Lakshmana's words, Rama said, 'Brother! Obey the command of your parents with purity of thought, word, and deed. Consider them as me. This is the path of the virtuous.' Thus Sri Rama pacified his younger brother.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Rama, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Queen Kausalya express her anguish before Sri Rama? How did Rama console and convince her?

**Answer:** Knowing Rama's firm resolve to obey his father's command, Queen Kausalya shed continuous tears and said in a choked voice, 'My son! Rama! I cannot live without you before my eyes. If you are determined to go to the forest as per your father's order, take me with you. I will get used to forest life near you and live peacefully.' Seeing his mother lamenting, Rama said, 'Mother! For a woman, her husband is God. The great king now rules over you and me. Bharata is also righteous. Being devoted to dharma, he will be obedient to you and always follow you. This is my firm belief. After I leave Ayodhya, you must take care of the king so that he does not suffer from grief for his son. Do not let him be depressed by this unbearable sorrow; be vigilant and serve him. Spend your time serving your husband and wait patiently until I return after completing my exile.' Hearing Rama's humble words, Kausalya wept profusely and said, 'My son! I do not have the strength to turn you from your firm resolve to go to the forest. Whatever fate decrees will happen. Son! Go carefully!' Then Kausalya gazed at Rama with unwavering attention and lovingly blessed him, wishing him all auspiciousness.

**Key entities:** Kausalya, Rama, Bharata, Ayodhya

### Chapter 18: Eighteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 25-30
- Source PDF pages: 45, 46, 47
- Printed page numbers: 49, 50, 51
- Key entities: Rama, Kausalya, Sita, Vasishta, Sumitra, Tataka, Bharata, Urmila, Shrutakirti, Janaka
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Rama, after receiving blessings from his mother Kausalya, goes to Sita's palace. He informs Sita of his exile to the Dandaka forest due to his father's promise. Rama tries to convince Sita to stay in Ayodhya, but Sita insists on accompanying him, citing her duty as a wife. After a lengthy discussion, Rama agrees to take her with him.

#### Q1

**Question:** After receiving blessings from his mother Kausalya, to whose presence did Rama go?

**Options:**
- 1. To the presence of Vasishta
- 2. To the presence of Sumitra Devi
- 3. To the presence of Vamadeva
- 4. To the presence of Sita Devi

**Correct answer:** To the presence of Sita Devi

**Key entities:** Kausalya, Rama, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** Lord Rama told Sita Devi, 'O Devi! I am strictly following my father's promise and going to which forest?'

**Options:**
- 1. To the Tataka forest region
- 2. To the penance forest
- 3. To the Dandaka forest
- 4. To the Ashoka forest region

**Correct answer:** To the Dandaka forest

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Dandaka Forest

#### Q3

**Question:** Rama tried many ways to make Sita stay in Ayodhya and not accompany him to the forest. Finally, if he refused to take her to the forests, unable to bear separation from Rama, what did she say she would sacrifice?

**Answer:** Her life

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Ayodhya

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama try to prevent Sita from accompanying him to the forest?

**Answer:** After receiving blessings from mother Kausalya, Rama came on foot to Sita's palace. Seeing her husband worried, Sita said, 'Lord! Your face has lost its cheerfulness and is pale. I have never seen such a state before.' To his wife who spoke these distressed words, Rama said, 'Janaki, our venerable father is about to send me to the forests. Therefore, obeying the king's command, I must go to the Dandaka forests. You stay in Ayodhya and serve my parents with humility and affection. Have love for me, be patient with a firm mind. Perform daily worship of gods, observe vows and fasts. From the time Bharata becomes crown prince, he will be the supreme authority. In his rule, you should behave like an ordinary relative. Do not expect more respect than Urmila and Shrutakirti. Behave amicably among others. I, for the sake of fulfilling my father's word, am going to the forests today. You stay in this Ayodhya without causing displeasure to anyone and follow my words.' Thus Rama explained the nuances of dharma to Sita. Rama's words, though spoken, pained Sita, who was naturally soft-spoken. Then she said, 'O noble husband! What is this? You are speaking meaningless words. Never before have such words come from your mouth. O great hero! A wife is half of her husband. Therefore, she is entitled to half the fruits of her husband. The command given to you by the king applies to me as well! Hence, I too must undergo exile along with you.' Thus Sita expressed her firm opinion to Rama.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Kausalya, Dandaka Forest, Ayodhya, Bharata, Urmila, Shrutakirti

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sita reason with dharma to persuade Rama to agree to take her to the forest?

**Answer:** To Janaki, who was ready to accompany him to the forest, Rama said, 'Sita! Do not make hasty sorrowful thoughts. Listen to my words. In the forest there are thorns, stones, no proper paths, no timely food. You, who have enjoyed royal luxuries unknown to the sun, cannot bear the hardships of that forest; the forest is always a abode of sorrow.' Hearing Rama's words, Sita understood that Rama did not wish to take her to the forest and wept. Shedding tears, she said, 'Lord! For any wife, living away from her husband is unbearable. You are my visible god. In this world and the next, I desire your company. As proclaimed by renowned brahmins, after being given in marriage by parents with the pouring of water, I must follow you not only in this world but also in the next. Following the authority of the Vedas, my father Janaka gave me to you with the pouring of water! I am virtuous, devoted to serving my husband, and a partner in your joys and sorrows. O noble husband! During exile, I consider both hardship and happiness equally. Therefore, take me with you. If you do not agree, I will give up my life.' Hearing Sita's words, Rama said, 'O Sita! Whatever it is, you are determined to come with me to the forest. Therefore, follow me and fulfill your duty as a devoted wife.' Thus he agreed.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Janaka

### Chapter 19: Nineteenth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 31-36
- Source PDF pages: 47, 48, 49, 50
- Printed page numbers: 51, 52, 53, 54
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Dasharatha, Kaikeyi, Vasishta, Sumitra, Sumantra, Bharata
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Kosala

**Summary:** Rama, accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, prepares to leave for the forest. He distributes his wealth to the deserving, visits his father Dasharatha, and consoles him. Kaikeyi's cruelty reaches its peak when she opposes sending any comforts with Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Lakshmana realized that Sita and Rama were ready for exile, he convinced his elder brother to let him accompany them to the forest. What did Rama, thus accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, do with all the wealth he possessed?

**Options:**
- 1. He entrusted it to the treasury
- 2. He entrusted it to Vasishta
- 3. He donated it to the deserving
- 4. He entrusted it to his mother and left

**Correct answer:** He donated it to the deserving

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Rama, accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, going to the forest, first came to see whom?

**Options:**
- 1. Dasharatha
- 2. Vasishta
- 3. Kaikeyi
- 4. Sumitra

**Correct answer:** Dasharatha

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Dasharatha

#### Q3

**Question:** Through whom did Rama inform his father that he had come to see him?

**Answer:** Sumantra

**Key entities:** Rama, Sumantra

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama console his grieving father and take leave from him?

**Answer:** Seeing Rama who came to see him, Dasharatha was immersed in an ocean of grief. Then Rama, with folded hands, said, 'O King! You are the lord of us all. Bless me with your cool hands and send me to the Dandaka forests for exile. Lakshmana and Sita wish to follow me to the forests. Despite my many attempts to dissuade them, they do not listen. So please permit them also to come with me. Do not grieve at all for us.' Saying thus, Rama waited for the king's permission. Seeing Rama, Dasharatha said, 'O Rama of the Raghu dynasty! I was deceived because of the boons given to Kaikeyi. Disregard my words and take up the sovereignty of Kosala yourself.' To this Rama replied, 'Father! It is not dharma for me to break your word. Therefore I will go to the forests. After spending fourteen years there, I will return and serve you.' Hearing his son, Dasharatha said, 'My son! O descendant of Raghu! By upholding my word, you are leaving all your relatives and going to the forests to establish me in truth. This is impossible for anyone but you. My son! I cannot turn you from your resolve. But at least stay here until this night ends. I will spend this one day happily seeing you. You may go tomorrow.' Then Rama said, 'Father! Even if I spend this night here, I will not get these royal pleasures tomorrow. So setting aside desires, I wish to go to the forests now. Bless me and send me.' Then Dasharatha said, 'My son! I know well that you are devoted to dharma and truthful. Very well, go now. May you attain happiness in this world and the next!' and blessed him and sent him off.

**Key entities:** Rama, Dasharatha, Dandaka Forest, Lakshmana, Sita, Kaikeyi, Kosala

#### Q5

**Question:** What can be described as the culmination of Kaikeyi's wickedness?

**Answer:** Dasharatha, greatly distressed by his vow, told Sumantra, 'O great minister! Equip the fourfold army and send them with Rama. Send dancers and wrestlers to provide entertainment and joy behind the army. Send various kinds of gold, jewels, ornaments, and clothes sufficient for fourteen years. Send important weapons, carts loaded with food, and forest-dwellers to show the way in the forest as companions for Rama. Sri Rama will hunt wild animals in the forests, drink the honey available there, and not think of royal pleasures. Here Bharata can rule.' Hearing Dasharatha's words, Kaikeyi became afraid and worried. Standing before the king, she said, 'Bharata does not want a kingdom devoid of enjoyments and wealth, a deserted kingdom.' Saying this, with reddened eyes and abandoning shame, Kaikeyi spoke. Seeing Kaikeyi speaking thus, Dasharatha rebuked her, 'Fie! O wicked woman! Do not show me your face.' Even after being publicly rebuked, Kaikeyi was not affected even as much as an ant bite. Such an act of Kaikeyi can be described as the culmination of her wickedness.

**Key entities:** Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Sumantra, Rama, Bharata

### Chapter 20: Twentieth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 37-42
- Source PDF pages: 50, 51, 52
- Printed page numbers: 54, 55, 56
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Dasharatha, Kaikeyi, Sumantra, Jabali, Kausalya, Agni, Bharata
- Places: Ayodhya, Kosala

**Summary:** Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana depart for the forest. Dasharatha laments and curses Kaikeyi. The citizens of Ayodhya grieve for Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Rama said to Dasharatha, 'Father, I have given up all pleasures. Fruits and roots in the forest are my food. If anyone brings me bark garments, I am ready to wear them,' who provided bark garments to Rama and Lakshmana?

**Options:**
- 1. Queen Kaikeyi
- 2. A servant
- 3. Dasharatha
- 4. Sumantra

**Correct answer:** Queen Kaikeyi

**Key entities:** Rama, Dasharatha, Lakshmana, Kaikeyi

#### Q2

**Question:** Whom did Dasharatha order to prepare the chariot to take Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana to the forest?

**Options:**
- 1. The commander
- 2. Sumantra
- 3. Jabali
- 4. The chamberlain

**Correct answer:** Sumantra

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Sumantra

#### Q3

**Question:** Who, following the chariot-borne Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana for some distance, and seeing the deeply distressed and motionless Dasharatha staring in the direction Rama went, said to him, 'O great king! Let us wish that our loved ones return to us. We cannot follow them far, can we?'

**Answer:** The ministers

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Dasharatha

#### Q4

**Question:** How did all the citizens of the city become agitated for Sri Rama?

**Answer:** After the best of men, Sri Rama, left the palace, the lamentations of the palace women became intense. Sri Rama, who never harmed anyone, was the protector of us all. That lord never became angry with anyone, and like his mother Kausalya, he always loved and respected us. Now where has that lord gone? The king, having lost his mind, sent him to the forest and distanced him from us. Thus they cried loudly and wailed. The king, who was already writhing in separation from his son, hearing the terrible lamentations in the palace, sank even deeper in grief. The entire city was overcome with the pain of separation from Rama, and all the daily activities of the citizens came to a halt. All of Rama's friends lost their senses and took to their beds, burdened with sorrow. In this way, all the citizens of the city became agitated.

**Key entities:** Rama, Kausalya

#### Q5

**Question:** After Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana went to the forest, how did Dasharatha lament?

**Answer:** Dasharatha kept looking in that direction until the dust raised by the speed of the chariot wheels of the departing Rama was visible. When even that dust was no longer seen, the king, in anguish, fell to the ground. Then Kausalya immediately grabbed his right shoulder to lift the king. Kaikeyi came and grabbed his left shoulder. Then Dasharatha turned to Kaikeyi and fumed, 'Kaikeyi, do not touch me. Do not show me your face. O wicked woman! I married you with Agni as witness. Because of your excessive evil deed, from today I abandon you. If Bharata becomes the ruler of this vast Kosala kingdom through adharma and rejoices, then after my death, let the offerings of pinda and water he offers not reach me!' Thus the king spoke in grief-stricken anger. Then Kausalya lifted the dust-covered king and went with him to her home. Dasharatha, thinking of his son who had become a sage-like ascetic, lamented. Then the king, like an eclipsed sun, lost his luster. The grief-stricken king writhed in pain. Emaciated by sorrow for his son, the king lay on his bed. Kausalya, herself grief-stricken, said to the king, 'Kaikeyi, with her crooked mind, sent Rama to the forest. If giving the kingdom to Bharata is the main thing, let it be; I agree to that. But even if my son stays here and serves Bharata as a slave, I agree to that. That is better than forest exile! Then my child would be moving before my eyes and staying here!' Thus Kausalya and Dasharatha, thinking of Sri Rama, writhed in pain.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Dasharatha, Kausalya, Kaikeyi, Agni, Bharata, Kosala

### Chapter 21: Twenty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 43-48
- Source PDF pages: 52, 53, 54
- Printed page numbers: 56, 57, 58
- Key entities: Kausalya, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Sumitra, Sumantra, Dasharatha, Kaikeyi
- Places: Ayodhya, Tamasa, Ganga
