**Summary:** Kausalya laments for Rama, and the citizens of Ayodhya follow Rama's chariot. Rama, Lakshmana, and Sita travel to the Tamasa river, where the citizens sleep. Rama decides to leave secretly to avoid their grief, crosses the river, and the citizens return to Ayodhya lamenting.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who consoled Kausalya, who was grieving and emaciated with sorrow for her son, always thinking of Sri Rama, with comforting words?

**Options:**
- 1. Vasishtha
- 2. Sumantra
- 3. Sumitra
- 4. Dasaratha

**Correct answer:** Sumitra

**Key entities:** Kausalya, Rama, Sumitra

#### Q2

**Question:** Who followed Sri Rama's chariot without leaving him?

**Options:**
- 1. Commanders
- 2. Ministers
- 3. Vasishtha and others
- 4. Brahmins and citizens

**Correct answer:** Brahmins and citizens

**Key entities:** Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Desiring to proceed to the forest, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana traveled until evening, stopped at a place, and rested that night on the bank of which river?

**Answer:** Ganga

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ganga

#### Q4

**Question:** How far did the citizens of Ayodhya who followed Sri Rama's chariot go? What happened afterwards?

**Answer:** Despite Rama's protests, the citizens followed him. They traveled some distance with the brahmins and people, reaching the banks of the Tamasa river by evening. Rama told Lakshmana, 'Let us spend our first night of exile here.' Then Rama drank the waters of the Tamasa, and on a bed of leaves arranged by Sumantra and Lakshmana, he lay down with Sita. Lakshmana and Sumantra remained awake that night. All the citizens, exhausted from the journey, fell into a deep sleep. Seeing them asleep, Rama said to Lakshmana, 'Brother, look at these citizens sleeping under the trees. Out of affection for us, they have left their wives and children and followed us here. They are determined to take us back to Ayodhya, even at the cost of their lives. Therefore, before they wake, let us board the chariot and quickly go by a path that no one can detect. Then they will have no chance to follow us and will return to Ayodhya. As princes, it is our duty to remove the people's grief.' According to Rama's words, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana boarded the chariot, and Sumantra drove it, crossing the river by a different ford. Then the citizens who were sleeping under the trees woke up and, not seeing Rama, were stunned with grief and looked around. Searching everywhere but not finding Rama, they lamented, yearning for the sight of Sita and Rama. Afterwards, the citizens traveled back the way they came and reached Ayodhya.

**Key entities:** Ayodhya, Rama, Tamasa, Lakshmana, Sumantra, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the citizens who returned to Ayodhya lament when they met their families?

**Answer:** The citizens who had followed Rama to the forests and returned reached their homes and met their wives and children. Yet they could not overcome their grief. Even when friends came to greet them, no signs of joy appeared on their faces. The women in the houses did not engage in cooking. The women said to their husbands, 'In the present circumstances, this city is not fit for good people to live in. Everyone here is anxious about Rama. If we stay here, we will have no peace. This kingdom is under Kaikeyi's control. Hence, adharma will prevail here. Living in such a place is futile. What use are wealth or children in a kingdom without protection? Kaikeyi, who made the great king a puppet and did such a thing to Rama, will spare no one. As long as Kaikeyi lives, we cannot live happily under her rule. Because of her, the entire kingdom will be destroyed. King Dasaratha, stricken with grief for his son, will not live long. On the day he is gone, our fortunes will be ruined. Therefore, let us go to a place where Kaikeyi's name is not heard.' Thus the citizens of Ayodhya lamented, and the sun set. The city of Ayodhya appeared like a dried-up ocean.

**Key entities:** Ayodhya, Rama, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha

### Chapter 22: Twenty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 49-54
- Source PDF pages: 54, 55, 56, 57
- Printed page numbers: 58, 59, 60, 61
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Guha, Trishanku, Sumantra, Kaikeyi, Bharata, Kausalya, Sumitra
- Places: Tamasa, Ganga, Prayaga, Chitrakuta, Godavari, Kosala, Yamuna, Ayodhya, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana cross the Tamasa river and travel south, reaching the Ganges. They meet Guha, king of Shringaberapura, and later cross the Ganges to Prayaga, where they visit sage Bharadvaja's ashram. Rama discusses his grief with Lakshmana, and they proceed to Chitrakuta.

#### Q1

**Question:** After crossing the Tamasa river and traveling south, which sacred river bank did Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, reach by that evening?

**Options:**
- 1. Godavari
- 2. Krishna River
- 3. Ganges
- 4. Sindhu River

**Correct answer:** Ganges

**Key entities:** Tamasa, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Ganga

#### Q2

**Question:** After crossing the vast borders of Kosala, Rama reached the region of Shringaberapura and wished to rest there. Who was the ruler of that region?

**Options:**
- 1. Guha
- 2. Trishanku
- 3. Kushanabha
- 4. Vishala

**Correct answer:** Guha

**Key entities:** Kosala, Rama, Guha

#### Q3

**Question:** After sending Sumantra back with the chariot, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana crossed the Ganges and reached Prayaga, the confluence of the Ganges and Yamuna. Which sage's ashram did they reach there?

**Answer:** Bharadvaja Maharshi

**Key entities:** Sumantra, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ganga, Prayaga, Yamuna

#### Q4

**Question:** After crossing the Ganges and the populated regions, the noble Rama entered the forests and rested at a place. What topics did he discuss with Lakshmana?

**Answer:** Rama performed evening worship and then spoke to Lakshmana: 'Brother, this is the first night after leaving the populated areas. Let us somehow spend this night here.' They lay on beds of grass. Rama said, 'Lakshmana, the king must be suffering greatly now. Kaikeyi is happy that her wish is fulfilled. No one is there to comfort our father; he is old and separated from us. Seeing this unexpected calamity, I feel that Kaikeyi came to Ayodhya only to send me to the forest, hand the king over to death, and make her son Bharata king. Having gained power, she may become arrogant and forget right and wrong, and trouble mother Kausalya and mother Sumitra for my sake. Therefore, Lakshmana, you should leave at dawn and go to Ayodhya to set things right. I will go to the Dandaka forest with Sita.' Thus Rama grieved for a while. Then Lakshmana consoled him in many ways: 'Brother, if you grieve like this, it pains Sita and me. I cannot live without you. I have no need for anyone but you. I would even reject heaven without you.' After saying this, they slept on the grass bed under a banyan tree, and thus they spent that night.

**Key entities:** Ganga, Rama, Lakshmana, Kaikeyi, Ayodhya, Bharata, Kausalya, Sumitra, Dandaka Forest, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana reach Bharadvaja's ashram? How did the meeting with the sage proceed?

**Answer:** Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, journeyed to see Prayaga, the confluence of the Ganges and Yamuna. As they traveled, Rama said to Lakshmana, 'Brother, I have heard that the ashram of sage Bharadvaja is near Prayaga.' They reached the ashram of sage Bharadvaja by evening. There, Rama met the sage and told him about themselves. Then sage Bharadvaja performed hospitality, providing various fruits, food, and sweet drinks available in the forest, and arranged a dwelling with affection. The sage said, 'O Rama, I have been waiting for your visit for a long time. Today your arrival has fulfilled that. You may stay comfortably at this holy confluence of the Ganges and Yamuna.' Then Rama replied, 'O sage, if I stay here, the people of Kosala will frequently come here. So it is not good for us to stay here. Please tell us of an ashram area inaccessible to people, where we can stay comfortably.' The sage then said, 'Rama, ten kroshas from here is a place called Chitrakuta, which is suitable for you to live.' Rama and his party then traveled along the path shown by the sage.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Prayaga, Ganga, Yamuna, Kosala, Chitrakuta

### Chapter 23: Twenty-Third Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 55-60
- Source PDF pages: 57, 58, 59
- Printed page numbers: 61, 62, 63
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Valmiki, Sumantra, Dasharatha, Kausalya, Atri, Vishvamitra, Guha, Bharata
- Places: Chitrakuta, Yamuna, Ayodhya, Ganga, Godavari, Sarayu, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana travel towards Chitrakuta. Sage Bharadvaja guides them, instructing them to cross the Yamuna river to reach Chitrakuta. They meet Sage Valmiki near Chitrakuta and inform him of their intention to build an ashrama. Lakshmana builds a leaf hut, and Rama performs a Vastu Puja before entering it with Sita. Sumantra returns to Ayodhya and delivers Rama's message to King Dasharatha, who is grief-stricken. Sumantra tries to console Dasharatha and Kausalya.

#### Q1

**Question:** As Rama and his companions were traveling towards Chitrakuta, Sage Bharadvaja accompanied them for some distance and showed them the way, saying, 'If you cross a river, you will reach the Chitrakuta mountain region.' What is the name of that river?

**Options:**
- 1. Ganga
- 2. Yamuna
- 3. Godavari
- 4. Sarayu

**Correct answer:** Yamuna

**Key entities:** Rama, Chitrakuta, Yamuna

#### Q2

**Question:** Rama and his companions reached the Chitrakuta mountain region and visited a sage who lived nearby, telling him that they were going to build an ashrama there. Who was that sage?

**Options:**
- 1. Sage Atri
- 2. Sage Bharadvaja
- 3. Sage Valmiki
- 4. Sage Vishvamitra

**Correct answer:** Sage Valmiki

**Key entities:** Rama, Chitrakuta, Valmiki

#### Q3

**Question:** In the Chitrakuta mountain region, at the spot designated by Rama, Lakshmana built a leaf hut. Then Rama performed a puja, and Rama and Sita entered the leaf hut. What is that puja called?

**Answer:** Vastu Puja

**Key entities:** Chitrakuta, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sumantra, upon reaching Ayodhya, convey Rama's message to Dasharatha?

**Answer:** Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, crossed the Ganga and reached the other shore. Sumantra watched them as long as they were visible, then took leave of Guha and returned to Ayodhya. He entered the royal palace, met the king, and bowed to him. Then the king asked Sumantra, 'My children, who have never known heat, are suffering many hardships in the forest. Where do they sleep? What are their food and activities? Describe all these. By hearing Rama's story, I will be somewhat freed from grief.' As the king spoke, Sumantra, shedding tears and with a choked voice, said, 'O king! Rama, with joined palms, bowed his head to you and said, "Sumantra! Convey my prostrations to the feet of our father, who is a knower of the Self and a great soul. Tell all the mothers in the inner apartments that I have bowed to them and asked about their welfare. Especially convey my salutations to our mother Kausalya. Inform them that we are all well and are practicing dharma with devotion. Convey our welfare news to Bharata. Tell him, as my words, to look upon all mothers with equal vision." After Rama said many such things, Lakshmana said, "Sumantra! What offense did Rama, a prince, commit that he was sent to the forest? Whatever happens, whether brother or father, Rama is everything to me." O king! Sita, however, did not speak to me at all; she was motionless, grieving, crying, and kept looking at the chariot and at me repeatedly.' Thus Sumantra conveyed Rama's message.

**Key entities:** Sumantra, Ayodhya, Rama, Dasharatha, Sita, Lakshmana, Ganga, Guha, Kausalya, Bharata

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sumantra console Dasharatha and Queen Kausalya, who were lamenting with grief for their son?

**Answer:** Having heard Rama's message through Sumantra, Dasharatha said, 'O Sumantra! I now wish to see Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana. But due to my sin, that is not possible for me.' Lamenting thus, he lost consciousness. Then Kausalya, trembling and weak, fell to the ground. After some time, she said, 'Sumantra! Without Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana, I cannot live even for a moment. Therefore, take me to the place where they are.' Hearing Kausalya's pitiful words, Sumantra grieved for a long time. Then Sumantra said, 'Mother! Raghava Rama is staying peacefully in the Dandaka forest without any worry. So do not worry about what will happen to Rama. Give up the grief caused by separation from him. Lakshmana, who is self-controlled and knows dharma, is constantly serving Rama in the forest. Sita is always receiving love and affection from her husband. Mother Kausalya! Do not worry at all about Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana.' Thus Sumantra tried to console Dasharatha and Kausalya with appropriate words, but they, emaciated by the grief of separation from their son, continued to lament, crying 'Rama! Rama!' and suffering.

**Key entities:** Sumantra, Dasharatha, Kausalya, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Dandaka Forest

### Chapter 24: Twenty-Fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 61-66
- Source PDF pages: 59, 60, 61, 62
- Printed page numbers: 63, 64, 65, 66
- Key entities: Kausalya, Rama, Dasharatha, Vasishta, Sumitra, Kaikeyi
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** Kausalya, unable to bear separation from Rama, speaks harshly to Dasaratha, who is pained. She repents. Dasaratha consoles her and recounts a curse from his youth that he will die of grief for his son. He dies at midnight, remembering Rama. The queens and palace women lament. Vasistha and ministers preserve the king's body in an oil-filled trough, postponing cremation until the sons return.

#### Q1

**Question:** Seeing her husband pained by her harsh words spoken due to inability to bear separation from Sri Rama, how did Kausalya behave?

**Options:**
- 1. She repented
- 2. She became irritated
- 3. She was surprised
- 4. She justified herself

**Correct answer:** She repented

**Key entities:** Rama, Kausalya

#### Q2

**Question:** Consoling Kausalya, Dasaratha told her in detail about a curse that befell him as a result of an incident in his youth. What did he say the curse was?

**Options:**
- 1. You will be deprived of your kingdom
- 2. You will be deprived of heaven
- 3. You will die of grief for your son
- 4. You will be deprived of righteousness

**Correct answer:** You will die of grief for your son

**Key entities:** Kausalya, Dasharatha

#### Q3

**Question:** When King Dasaratha, late at night past midnight, said 'Alas, Kausalya! Sumitra! My senses are failing moment by moment,' and left this world, whom did he remember as he gave up his life?

**Answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kausalya, Sumitra, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the queens and palace women lament upon the death of King Dasaratha?

**Answer:** By sunrise, all the attendants came eagerly to serve the king. Since Dasaratha had not come out of the bedchamber, they suspected something and looked inside, realizing the king's heartbeat had stopped. Kausalya and Sumitra, immersed in grief until late night, were in deep sleep and did not realize. Upon learning of the king's death, the palace women raised their voices and wept piteously. Awakened by their cries, Kausalya and Sumitra quickly woke up. Seeing the king, they cried 'Alas! Lord of our lives!' and fell to the ground. Overwhelmed with grief, Kausalya rolled on the ground, her body covered with dust and lustreless. Then Kaikeyi and all of Dasaratha's wives, overcome with sorrow, wept and fell unconscious. With the lamentations of all the queens including Kausalya, the entire palace resounded with weeping. The king's death filled the mansion with fear, agitation, and distressed attendants. Thus the queens and attendants lamented the death of King Dasaratha.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Kausalya, Sumitra, Kaikeyi

#### Q5

**Question:** How was King Dasaratha's mortal body preserved? Then how did the people of Ayodhya and the queens grieve?

**Answer:** Kausalya, taking the head of the lifeless King Dasaratha onto her lap, lamented in various ways. She said, 'What use is life without the king? I will also perform self-immolation with the king.' She wept falling on her husband's body. Then the maids took her away. Then Vasistha, consulting with all the ministers, not wishing to perform the cremation rites without the sons present, preserved the king's mortal body in a trough filled with oil. Afterwards, they managed all state affairs. Seeing the king's body placed in the oil trough, the palace women and all servants wept profusely. 'Alas! O King! You who were grieving for Sri Rama, have now left us and gone to heaven. We have all become orphans. How can we live before Kaikeyi?' Thus all the queens grieved, falling and rolling on the ground. With the king's death, neither the palace women nor the city people cleaned their homes and courtyards, so the city became lustreless. They all abstained from food that day and became pale. Then the sun set. All the residents of Ayodhya lost their peace of mind.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Kausalya, Vasishta, Rama, Kaikeyi

### Chapter 25: Twenty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 67-72
- Source PDF pages: 62, 63, 64
- Printed page numbers: 66, 67, 68
- Key entities: Bharata, Shatrughna, Kaikeyi, Markandeya, Kausalya, Yudhajit, Dasharatha, Rama, Lakshmana
- Places: Ayodhya, Kosala

**Summary:** The sages entrust the responsibility of ruling the kingdom to Vasishtha. Vasishtha sends messengers to bring Bharata and Shatrughna back to Ayodhya. The messengers travel to Girivrajapura, the capital of Kekaya, and inform Bharata. Bharata, along with Shatrughna and a fourfold army, travels for seven days and reaches Ayodhya on the eighth day. Upon entering the city, he learns of his father's death from his mother Kaikeyi, who urges him to rule the kingdom.

#### Q1

**Question:** To whom did the sages like Markandeya entrust the responsibility of thinking about the kingdom, saying that a kingdom without a king should not exist?

**Options:**
- 1. Kausalya Devi
- 2. Vamadeva
- 3. The commander-in-chief
- 4. Vasishtha

**Correct answer:** Vasishtha

**Key entities:** Markandeya

#### Q2

**Question:** When Vasishtha sent messengers to bring Bharata and Shatrughna to Ayodhya, what did he tell them as the name of the city where Bharata's maternal uncle lived?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishala Nagara
- 2. Hastinapura
- 3. Girivrajapura
- 4. Dwaraka

**Correct answer:** Girivrajapura

**Key entities:** Bharata, Shatrughna, Ayodhya

#### Q3

**Question:** Having received the messengers' message, Bharata, accompanied by Shatrughna and a fourfold army, traveled without delay and reached Ayodhya in how many days?

**Answer:** Eight days

**Key entities:** Bharata, Shatrughna, Ayodhya

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the messengers sent by Vasishtha's order reach the Kekaya kingdom? How did Bharata's journey towards Ayodhya proceed?

**Answer:** The messengers sent by Vasishtha's order traveled for several days and reached Girivrajapura, the capital city of the Kekaya king. There, they met Bharata and Shatrughna, who were spending time comfortably in the royal house of Yudhajit. Then Bharata asked the messengers, 'Is our father, King Dasharatha, well? Are the great souls Rama and Lakshmana and our three mothers well? Has no calamity befallen our mother Kaikeyi? Did she send any message?' The messengers replied, 'O best of men! All are well. Depart immediately.' Hearing the messengers' words, Bharata said, 'Alright, the messengers are urging me to travel to Ayodhya. With your permission, I will proceed to Ayodhya.' Thus, he requested his maternal grandfather and, obtaining permission from him and all others there, Bharata set out for Ayodhya with a fourfold army. Crossing mountains, forests, rivers, cities, and villages, he traveled for seven days and entered the Kosala kingdom on the eighth day at sunrise, and saw Ayodhya. Thus, Bharata's journey to Ayodhya proceeded.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ayodhya, Shatrughna, Yudhajit, Dasharatha, Rama, Lakshmana, Kaikeyi, Kosala

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Bharata, upon entering the city of Ayodhya, learn about his father's death?

**Answer:** Upon entering Ayodhya, Bharata went to the royal palace but did not see his father. So he went to his mother Kaikeyi's chamber. Seeing Bharata, who had been at his grandfather's house until now, Kaikeyi rose from her seat with unbounded joy. Immediately, Bharata bowed at his mother's feet. Then Kaikeyi said, 'My son! Bharata! You have come from your grandfather's house, haven't you? Are your grandfather and maternal uncle all well there?' and asked about the welfare of everyone there. Then Bharata said, 'Mother! I went to father's house to see him. He was not there. Is he in the house of my elder mother Kausalya?' To Bharata's question, his mother replied, 'My son! Your father, a great soul, a treasure for virtuous men, has attained the supreme goal that all beings attain.' Hearing his mother's words about his father's death, he was overcome with terrible grief for his father and lamented with pitiful words, 'Oh father! Have you left me?' and fell to the ground, rolling. Then Kaikeyi lifted her son and consoled him. Bharata sobbed for a long time with overwhelming grief. Later, composing himself, he asked, 'Mother! What was the disease that caused the death of our noble father?' Then his mother told him the entire story and said, 'O son! Abandon your grief and sorrow, and with courage, rule this Kosala kingdom without thorns.' Hearing her words, Bharata became stunned.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ayodhya, Kaikeyi, Kausalya, Kosala

### Chapter 26: Twenty-Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 73-78
- Source PDF pages: 64, 65, 66, 67
- Printed page numbers: 68, 69, 70, 71
- Key entities: Bharata, Kaikeyi, Rama, Dasharatha, Sumantra, Kausalya, Vasishta, Mandara
- Places: Sarayu

**Summary:** Bharata learns from Kaikeyi that she is the cause of Rama's exile and Dasaratha's death. He rebukes her and declares he will make Rama king. Sumantra and ministers arrive. Bharata faints and later goes with Satrughna to Kausalya. Vasistha advises Bharata to perform the funeral rites. The funeral of Dasaratha is described in detail. Satrughna attacks Manthara but is stopped by Bharata.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Bharata learned that his mother was the main cause of Sri Rama's exile and his father's death, he rebuked her in many ways and said, 'Listen to what I am going to do for this wicked deed of yours.' What did Bharata tell his mother?

**Options:**
- 1. You rule this kingdom yourself
- 2. I will crown Satrughna
- 3. I will make Sri Rama the king
- 4. I will hand over this kingdom to Vasistha

**Correct answer:** I will make Sri Rama the king

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Learning of Bharata's arrival, Sumantra and other ministers came to Kaikeyi's palace. Bharata had already lost consciousness and did not regain it for a long time. Then, with whom did Bharata go along with Satrughna?

**Options:**
- 1. To Vasistha
- 2. To mother Kausalya
- 3. To the assembly of citizens and countrymen
- 4. To the chief servant

**Correct answer:** To mother Kausalya

**Key entities:** Bharata, Sumantra, Kaikeyi, Kausalya

#### Q3

**Question:** While Bharata was overcome with grief, who told him, 'O prince! This is not the time for grief. The king's funeral rites must be performed so that he may attain the highest realms.'?

**Answer:** Vasistha

**Key entities:** Bharata, Vasishta

#### Q4

**Question:** How were the funeral and post-funeral rites of King Dasaratha performed?

**Answer:** Following the advice of Sage Vasistha, Bharata composed his mind to perform the funeral rites for his father. Then Dasaratha's body was taken down from the oil vat. Seeing their lifeless father, Bharata and Satrughna wept for a long time. Then Vasistha told the princes to perform the funeral rites without worry. As per the guru's words, Bharata urged the priests, chaplains, and teachers. Attendants placed the king's coffin on a palanquin and took it to the cremation ground. There, on the pyre, they placed aloe, sandalwood, frankincense sticks, pine, padmaka, and deodar wood, and sprinkled various fragrant substances. Then, while the priests chanted Vedic mantras, Bharata lit the fire. Then Kausalya and other queens came to the cremation ground with maids. After the cremation was complete, they bathed in the Sarayu river and offered libations. Then for ten days, Bharata slept on the ground, suppressing his grief, and performed the rites. On the eleventh day, Bharata purified himself and performed the purificatory rites. On the twelfth day, he completed the sapindikarana and other shraddha rites, and gave abundant food donations so that the king might attain the highest realms. They also donated gold ornaments, thousands of cows, and various goods and vehicles. Thus Bharata and Satrughna completed King Dasaratha's funeral rites.

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Vasishta, Bharata, Kausalya, Sarayu

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Satrughna attempt to punish Manthara?

**Answer:** After completing all the post-funeral rites of King Dasaratha, while Bharata was thinking of going to Sri Rama, Satrughna was also there. At that time, Manthara, adorned with ornaments all over her body, stood at the eastern gate in joy. Seeing her, some gatekeepers caught her and brought her to Satrughna, saying, 'O prince! This Manthara is the root cause of all these calamities. Do as you wish with this sinful woman.' Then Satrughna, learning everything, said to the attendants, 'She must suffer the consequences of her wickedness towards us,' and grabbed Manthara tightly. The hunchback screamed in fear. Satrughna dragged her and threw her to the ground. Hearing Manthara's screams in fear of her life, Kaikeyi came to rescue her. Satrughna defied her, and Kaikeyi, frightened, sought refuge with Bharata. Then Bharata, seeing his mother who had come to him and seeing Satrughna in a rage, said, 'I should kill her, but I stopped because our brother Sri Rama would not look at the face of a mother-killer. Similarly, if we kill this hunchback, our brother would not even look at us, calling us women-killers. So release her as well.' Following Bharata's words, Satrughna released Manthara. Kaikeyi took the terrified Manthara to her palace.

**Key entities:** Mandara, Dasharatha, Bharata, Rama, Kaikeyi

### Chapter 27: Twenty-Seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 79-84
- Source PDF pages: 67, 68, 69
- Printed page numbers: 71, 72, 73
- Key entities: Dasharatha, Bharata, Rama, Guha, Atri, Kausalya, Sumantra, Kaikeyi, Valmiki, Lakshmana, Sumitra
- Places: Ganga, Ayodhya

**Summary:** After King Dasharatha's funeral, Bharata is urged to become king but decides to bring Rama back. He sets out with a large entourage including queens and citizens, reaches the Ganges, and meets Guha, the Nishada king, who welcomes them.

#### Q1

**Question:** On the fourteenth day after performing King Dasharatha's funeral rites, who told Bharata in the morning, 'O prince! At present, you alone are fit to be king by law'?

**Options:**
- 1. Vasishtha
- 2. Kausalya
- 3. Citizens
- 4. Ministers

**Correct answer:** Atri Maharshi

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Bharata, Atri

#### Q2

**Question:** At whose summons did Sumantra and other ministers convene a full assembly?

**Options:**
- 1. Kausalya
- 2. Kaikeyi
- 3. Vasishtha
- 4. Bharata

**Correct answer:** Question Guha tells about Sri Rama, saying, 'O prince! Your elder brother Sri Rama is under this tree...'

**Key entities:** Sumantra, Guha, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** In the full assembly after King Dasharatha's funeral, who decided and said that Sri Rama alone is fit to be king, and that we should go with the fourfold army and invite him back?

**Answer:** Valmiki Maharshi

**Key entities:** Dasharatha, Rama, Valmiki

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Bharata's journey with his retinue proceed up to the Ganges River in search of Sri Rama?

**Answer:** Eager to see Rama and Lakshmana, Bharata set out with Kausalya, Sumitra, and Kaikeyi in suitable vehicles. Along with the fourfold army, the citizens of Ayodhya of all professions followed Bharata. Thus the entire city of Ayodhya moved. The soldiers joyfully traveled far on horses, elephants, and chariots, reaching the banks of the Ganges near Shringaberipura. That city was the residence of Guha, a friend of Sri Rama. Seeing the Ganges with its sacred waters and noticing his army somewhat tired, Bharata told the ministers, 'As you wish, halt our army here. Tomorrow we will cross the Ganges. I will offer libations of Ganges water to our father.' Bharata did so. By Bharata's order, Sumantra and others stopped the army and stationed them in various places. Then Bharata, thinking of a way to bring the great-souled Sri Rama, spent the night there.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ganga, Rama, Lakshmana, Kausalya, Sumitra, Kaikeyi, Ayodhya, Guha, Sumantra

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Guha, seeing Bharata encamped on the Ganges bank, greet and honor him?

**Answer:** Guha, the Nishada king, seeing Bharata's army and the Kovidara flag flying on the chariots, thought, 'This is the army of the Ikshvaku kings. It seems Bharata has set out to permanently seize the kingdom and eliminate Sri Rama.' He considered, 'If Bharata intends to bring joy to Sri Rama, we will safely cross the Ganges with this army.' He instructed his men and took some food items to Bharata. There he first met Sumantra and learned the truth, becoming happy. Then Guha bowed to Bharata and said, 'Lord! Had we known of your arrival earlier, we would have welcomed and honored you. We are all your servants. We wish to offer you fruits, roots, meat, and various forest grains.' Bharata replied, 'Brother! You are a great friend of my elder brother Sri Rama. Your wish is good. Your devotion, sincerity, and kind words have satisfied me. Just get us across the Ganges.' Then Guha said, 'Prince! I know all these forest paths. I and my people will ferry you across the Ganges and accompany you. Be carefree and accept our hospitality today with your army. Tomorrow we can cross the Ganges.' Bharata agreed. That night everyone rested there.

**Key entities:** Guha, Bharata, Ganga, Rama, Sumantra

### Chapter 28: Twenty-Eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 85-90
- Source PDF pages: 69, 70, 71, 72
- Printed page numbers: 73, 74, 75, 76
- Key entities: Bharata, Guha, Rama, Atri, Valmiki, Gautama, Shatrughna, Kausalya, Dasharatha, Sita, Lakshmana
- Places: Ganga, Chitrakuta

**Summary:** Bharata and his army cross the Ganga with Guha's help and reach the hermitage of Sage Bharadvaja. Bharata seeks guidance to find Rama, and the sage directs him to Chitrakuta.

#### Q1

**Question:** During the intimate conversation between Bharata and Guha, which sage's hermitage did Bharata ask Guha to guide them to?

**Options:**
- 1. Sage Atri
- 2. Sage Bharadvaja
- 3. Sage Valmiki
- 4. Sage Gautama

**Correct answer:** Sage Bharadvaja

**Key entities:** Bharata, Guha

#### Q2

**Question:** While telling about Rama, Guha said, 'O prince! Your elder brother Rama slept that night under this very tree on a bed of grass.' What is the name of that tree?

**Options:**
- 1. Gara tree
- 2. Banyan tree
- 3. Ragi tree
- 4. Medi tree

**Correct answer:** Gara tree

**Key entities:** Rama, Guha

#### Q3

**Question:** With what means did Guha transport Bharata's four-fold army across the Ganga?

**Answer:** Boats

**Key entities:** Guha, Bharata, Ganga

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Bharata, along with his retinue, cross the Ganga and reach Sage Bharadvaja's hermitage?

**Answer:** Bharata and Shatrughna slept at the very spot where Rama had slept on the Ganga bank. Waking before sunrise, they boarded the five hundred boats arranged by Guha, along with the preceptors led by Vasishtha, the royal women led by Kausalya, soldiers, relatives, friends, and all supplies. Some people shouted loudly about their belongings and boarded the boats hastily. The overcrowded boats were mostly filled with women; some boats were limited to horses, others to carts and oxen. Gradually, some boats went to the opposite shore and returned. Then, auspicious elephants were loaded onto some boats. Some crossed the Ganga on boats, others by swimming. The army, purified by bathing in the river, along with Bharata and others, reached near Bharadvaja's hermitage after some time. Bharata left his army at a distance and went on foot to the sage with Vasishtha and other priests. The hermitage of Sage Bharadvaja looked charming with its leaf huts.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ganga, Shatrughna, Rama, Guha, Kausalya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Bharata and others see Sage Bharadvaja and speak with him?

**Answer:** Seeing Sage Bharadvaja from a distance, Bharata stopped all those following him and walked ahead with the priest Vasishtha in front. The great ascetic, seeing Vasishtha, rose from his seat and came forward. Then Bharata and Vasishtha introduced their gotra names and bowed. Sage Bharadvaja then offered arghya and padya to Bharata and Vasishtha and worshipped them. He inquired about their welfare and recognized Bharata as Dasharatha's son. Then he asked Bharata, 'Your elder brother Rama has been sent to the forest, has he not? What is the reason for your coming here?' Bharata, shedding tears, explained everything. Then Sage Bharadvaja said, 'O best of men! Your goal and your resolve are all good. I know the truth of your mind. May it become firm in you! May your fame spread throughout the earth! The righteous Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, is living in the regions of Chitrakuta mountain. Therefore, O Bharata! You may go to your elder brother Rama tomorrow. Today, stay here with your ministers and retinue. This is my wish.' Then Bharata said, 'O lord of sages! I bow to your command,' and decided to stay at the hermitage for that night.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Dasharatha, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Chitrakuta

### Chapter 29: Twenty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 91-96
- Source PDF pages: 72, 73, 74
- Printed page numbers: 76, 77, 78
- Key entities: Bharata, Rama, Bharadwaja, Sita, Lakshmana, Brahma, Kubera
- Places: Chitrakuta, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Bharata, eager to see Rama, arrives at Chitrakuta with his army. Sage Bharadwaja hosts them and directs them to Chitrakuta. Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana are enjoying the natural beauty of Chitrakuta and the Mandakini river. Lakshmana spots Bharata's approaching army and suspects hostile intentions, but Rama remains calm.

#### Q1

**Question:** Having decided to offer hospitality to Bharata and his entire retinue, Sage Bharadwaja entered the fire-sanctuary, performed achamana, and whom did he first invite?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishvakarma
- 2. Brahma
- 3. Parashakti
- 4. Annapurna Devi

**Correct answer:** Vishvakarma

**Key entities:** Bharata, Bharadwaja

#### Q2

**Question:** Taking leave from Sage Bharadwaja, with a desire to see Rama, Bharata approached the sage and asked, 'O great one! Where is my elder brother? How far is that place from here?' What distance did Sage Bharadwaja say Chitrakuta, where Rama was, is from there?

**Options:**
- 1. Five yojanas
- 2. Four and a half yojanas
- 3. Three and a half yojanas
- 4. Two yojanas

**Correct answer:** Three and a half yojanas

**Key entities:** Bharadwaja, Rama, Bharata, Chitrakuta

#### Q3

**Question:** With a desire to see Rama, Bharata, along with his army, was walking on the slopes of Chitrakuta mountain according to the signs given by Sage Bharadwaja. Some servants came and showed a sign to Bharata, saying Rama might be there. What could that sign be?

**Answer:** Smoke

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Chitrakuta, Bharadwaja

#### Q4

**Question:** When Bharata went to the Chitrakuta region with all his people, how were Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana at that time?

**Answer:** Sita, Lakshmana, and Rama had begun their forest exile about a month ago. Gradually, Rama was enjoying the natural beauties of Chitrakuta, showing the wonderful mountain splendors to Sita and delighting in them himself. Then Rama said to his wife, 'O beautiful one! Although kingship is far from me, and friends who wish me well are not near, my mind, absorbed in enjoying the charming sights of these Chitrakuta mountains, is not troubled by those matters. Sita! By performing forest exile, I have repaid my father's debt by ruling that land. At the same time, I have done good to my brother Bharata. I have obtained both these results. By happily spending these fourteen years following the rules of forest exile, our family's fame and prestige will increase further.' Thus describing the splendors of the region to Sita, he once went with her to the banks of the Mandakini river. Showing her that river with its sacred waters, he said, 'Sita! This bank of the Mandakini river, with its sandbanks, swans, cranes, and blooming lotuses, is very delightful. The trees on both sides, laden with fruits and flowers, make this place rival Kubera's Saugandhika lake.' Speaking thus, with Sita as his companion, Rama roamed the Chitrakuta mountain regions and the banks of the Mandakini river.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Chitrakuta, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Kubera

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana recognize the arrival of Bharata and others?

**Answer:** While Rama was sitting on a level ground near the leaf-hut, the sounds of Bharata's approaching army and the dust raised by their feet suddenly appeared. Meanwhile, the elephants and wild animals in the forest, frightened by the tumultuous noise of the great army, fled from their herds. Then Rama, hearing the sounds made by the movement of the army, looked at Lakshmana and said, 'O Saumitri! It seems some prince is coming this way, look.' As soon as his elder brother spoke, Lakshmana climbed a nearby tall tree and looked in all directions. He saw a great army towards the north. Observing the army with its four divisions and the banners flying on the chariots, he said, 'Brother! Bharata is coming here with his army. You take up your bow and arrows and be ready. He, having been crowned in Ayodhya, is coming here to kill you in order to remove you as an obstacle to his rule. O elder brother! We have endured many insults until now. I have been controlling the fire of anger within me. Now his death at my hands is certain. I do not consider killing Bharata a sin.' Thus Lakshmana was overcome with anger. At that time, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana were in that state.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Bharata, Ayodhya, Sita

### Chapter 30: Thirtieth Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 97-102
- Source PDF pages: 74, 75, 76, 77
- Printed page numbers: 78, 79, 80, 81
- Key entities: Bharata, Lakshmana, Rama, Shatrughna, Dasharatha, Indra, Brahma, Sita, Sumantra
- Places: Chitrakuta, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Bharata arrives at Chitrakuta with his army. Lakshmana, seeing the army, suspects Bharata's intentions and urges Rama to prepare for battle. Rama rebukes Lakshmana, stating he would not desire any position unrighteously. Bharata, leaving his army, approaches Rama's hermitage on foot. He climbs a tree to locate Rama. Upon meeting, Bharata and Shatrughna prostrate at Rama's feet. Rama, wearing bark garments and a deer skin, raises Bharata and embraces him. They discuss their father Dasharatha's death. Rama performs water oblations and pinda offerings for his father at the Mandakini river.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Lakshmana said, 'Bharata is coming with his army. We should be ready with weapons in hand,' what position did Rama say he would not desire unrighteously?

**Options:**
- 1. Even the position of a king
- 2. Even the position of Indra
- 3. Even the position of a Lokapala
- 4. Even the position of Brahma

**Correct answer:** Even the position of Indra

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Bharata, Rama, Indra

#### Q2

**Question:** When Bharata came to the Chitrakuta region, he halted all his armies at one place, and walking ahead on foot to find Rama's whereabouts, he climbed a tree and looked. What is the name of that tree?

**Options:**
- 1. Maddi tree
- 2. Deodar tree
- 3. Chandrag tree
- 4. Nara-epi tree

**Correct answer:** Maddi tree

**Key entities:** Bharata, Chitrakuta, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** When Bharata and Shatrughna saw Rama in the leaf hut and prostrated at his feet, Rama was wearing bark garments. What was he wearing as an upper garment?

**Answer:** Deer skin

**Key entities:** Bharata, Shatrughna, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the meeting of Rama and Bharata take place?

**Answer:** Bharata, wearing bark cloth, with matted hair, prostrated on the ground. Rama lifted him, embraced him, seated him beside him, and asked, 'My son Bharata! Where is our father? Why have you come here instead of serving him?' Then Rama asked about the welfare of the gurus and mothers. Later, he spoke to Bharata about many royal duties. Hearing Rama's words, Bharata said, 'Brother! Serving you is my supreme duty. When I am separated from that, what use are other royal duties? Elder brother, no matter how many sons a king has, the eldest son alone is worthy of the kingdom. This is the eternal tradition in our dynasty. You, being the eldest son, should come to Ayodhya with me and be crowned. Our father, King Dasharatha, died when I was in the Kekaya kingdom, as soon as you left for the forest. Unable to bear your departure to the forest, the king ascended to heaven. I and Shatrughna performed the funeral rites for father. You are as dear as life to our father. He gave up his life thinking of you. The elders say that if a beloved son offers sesame and water oblations, the ancestors attain eternal worlds.' Thus Rama and Bharata discussed the news of their father's death.

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Ayodhya, Dasharatha, Shatrughna

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama offer pinda and water oblations to his father?

**Answer:** Hearing the sorrowful news of his father's death from Bharata, Rama became motionless. On hearing that heart-rending news, Rama lost consciousness and fell to the ground. Then Sita, Lakshmana, Bharata, and Shatrughna performed soothing ministrations. Gradually regaining consciousness, he wept and lamented piteously. Rama said, 'Sita, your father-in-law, who cherished you with great affection, has gone to heaven. Lakshmana! We have become fatherless.' As Rama spoke, the four brothers shed continuous tears. Then Bharata said, 'Brother! Perform water oblations for our father.' Then Rama consoled the weeping Janaki and said, 'Lakshmana! Bring the paste of garcinia seeds, a cloth, and an upper garment. Let us go to offer oblations to our father.' Taking Sita, with Lakshmana and Sumantra following, they went to the Mandakini river. After bathing in the sacred waters and completing rituals, Rama and Lakshmana offered water oblations, saying, 'Father! May these waters bring you satisfaction!' Then Rama offered sesame water oblations and pinda to his father. Afterwards, Rama returned to the leaf hut. Hearing the sounds of lamentation from the leaf hut area, the soldiers realized that Bharata had met Rama, and they all came in the direction of the sounds and saw Rama. Rama welcomed all who came to him.

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Sita, Lakshmana, Shatrughna, Sumantra

### Chapter 31: Thirty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 103-108
- Source PDF pages: 77, 78, 79
- Printed page numbers: 81, 82, 83
- Key entities: Bharata, Rama, Jabali, Kausalya, Guha, Indra, Kubera, Brahma, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Sita, Lakshmana
- Places: Ayodhya, Kosala

**Summary:** Bharata, accompanied by Vasishtha, arrives at Rama's hermitage and pleads with Rama to return to Ayodhya and accept the throne. Rama refuses, citing his duty to uphold his father's promise. Bharata is grief-stricken upon seeing the rice balls offered by Rama for his father's rites. Rama explains the importance of filial duty and recounts the story of King Gaya. Minister Jabali presents an atheistic argument to persuade Rama, but Rama remains steadfast.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who came to the leaf hut with Sage Vasishtha, and later, upon seeing the rice balls placed by Sri Rama for the ancestral rites near the Mandakini River, grieved excessively?

**Options:**
- 1. Jabali
- 2. Guha
- 3. Bharata
- 4. Kausalya

**Correct answer:** Kausalya

**Key entities:** Rama, Kausalya

#### Q2

**Question:** When Bharata prayed to his elder brother Sri Rama to return to Ayodhya and accept the kingdom, Rama told Bharata that upholding the father's word is our dharma. To whom did Rama compare their father?

**Options:**
- 1. Indra
- 2. Kubera
- 3. Brahma
- 4. Ishvara

**Correct answer:** Indra

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama, Ayodhya, Indra

#### Q3

**Question:** Even though Bharata pleaded greatly, Rama declared that he would adhere only to the fulfillment of his father's word. Referring to a king who, in ancient times, performed a sacrifice at Gaya Kshetra for the manes and declared that only a son who delivers his parents from Put (hell) is a true son, which king did Rama mention to Bharata?

**Answer:** Gaya

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** With what reasoning did Rama explain to Bharata that making their father truthful is our duty?

**Answer:** Bharata prayerfully requested Sri Rama to return to Ayodhya and be crowned. Then Sri Rama said, 'Brother Bharata! You were born to Kaikeyi from the king of kings, Dasharatha. All the words you have spoken are appropriate to your stature. Younger brother! In the past, when our father married your mother, he had promised your grandfather that the son born to Kaikeyi would be given the kingdom. Later, in the war between gods and demons, your mother rendered service, and the king was pleased and promised her two boons. Accordingly, your mother made the king swear an oath and asked for two boons: that you be crowned king and that I be sent to the forest. The king agreed. What fault is there in your mother? The king commanded me. I came to the forest with Sita and Lakshmana. You too should respect father's word and be crowned immediately. Follow my words and free the king from his debt to Kaikeyi. Do not cause him to attain hell.' Thus Sri Rama exhorted Bharata in many ways that it is proper for him to bear the burden of the kingdom.

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Ayodhya, Kaikeyi, Dasharatha, Sita, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** What kind of argument did Jabali, one of Dasharatha's ministers, present to convince Sri Rama?

**Answer:** While the righteous Sri Rama was thus consoling Bharata, Jabali, one of Dasharatha's ministers, came forward and said, 'O Rama of the Raghu dynasty! The things you said are fine. But you are wise and mentally strong. Do not let such futile thoughts come to your mind like an ignorant person. In this world, who is a relative to whom? All bonds among humans are momentary. Therefore, good people should not develop attachment to those relationships. O best among men! This forest life is very difficult. It is not proper for someone like you to abandon the wealth inherited from your father and choose such a difficult path. O wise one! Do not think that a father's word cannot be disobeyed. Enjoy the immediate benefit of the kingdom that is present before you. Do not believe in unseen otherworldly benefits. O Rama! The pleasures of this world alone are real; there is no afterlife. Follow the authority of those who teach this. Accept this Kosala kingdom as Bharata is pleading.' Thus Jabali presented his atheistic argument to Sri Rama.

**Key entities:** Jabali, Dasharatha, Rama, Bharata, Kosala

### Chapter 32: Thirty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Ayodhya Kanda
- Sarga range: 109-114
- Source PDF pages: 79, 80, 81, 82
- Printed page numbers: 83, 84, 85, 86
- Key entities: Jabali, Rama, Vasishta, Bharata, Kausalya, Guha, Sumantra, Shatrughna, Lakshmana, Dasharatha, Kaikeyi
- Places: Ayodhya, Chitrakuta, Yamuna, Ganga

**Summary:** Jabali's atheistic arguments are refuted by Rama, who upholds truth. Vasistha also advises Rama to return to Ayodhya. Bharata threatens a hunger strike, and Rama gives his sandals to Bharata. Bharata returns to Ayodhya with the sandals, passing through various places, and laments the desolate state of the city.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who pacified Rama by saying that Jabali is not an atheist, but spoke thus only to persuade him to return to Ayodhya, while Rama was condemning Jabali's atheism and extolling the excellence of truth?

**Options:**
- 1. Vasistha
- 2. Kausalya
- 3. Bharadvaja Maharshi
- 4. Guha

**Correct answer:** Vasistha

**Key entities:** Rama, Jabali, Ayodhya, Vasishta

#### Q2

**Question:** When Rama did not agree to return to Ayodhya despite Vasistha's advice, Bharata said he would spread darbha grass before Rama and sit on it on a hunger strike. Whom did he ask to bring the darbha grass?

**Options:**
- 1. Shatrughna
- 2. Jabali
- 3. Lakshmana
- 4. Sumantra

**Correct answer:** Sumantra

**Key entities:** Rama, Ayodhya, Vasishta, Bharata, Sumantra

#### Q3

**Question:** Upon Bharata's request, Rama gave his sandals. Bharata then bowed to the sandals, took them, placed them on the howdah of an elephant, and carried them away. What was the name of that elephant?

**Answer:** Shatrunjaya

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Bharata return to the city of Ayodhya?

**Answer:** Bharata took the sandals from the elephant howdah, placed them on his head, and with Shatrughna, mothers, gurus, ministers, citizens, and the entire army, took leave of Rama and set out for Ayodhya. He reached the hermitage of Bharadvaja Maharshi near Chitrakuta, bowed to the sage, narrated all that happened in the presence of Rama at Chitrakuta, took leave, and proceeded towards Ayodhya. The great army with four divisions, along with palanquins, carts, and other vehicles, followed Bharata. They traveled some distance, crossed the Yamuna river, then saw the holy Ganga. With the help of Guha, they crossed the Ganga and reached Shringaberipura. Bidding farewell to Guha, they left Shringaberipura and after some distance saw Ayodhya. Seeing the city bereft of his father and brothers, Bharata said to the charioteer Sumantra, 'Sumantra! This Ayodhya is desolate and has lost its charm. There is no joy among the people here.' Thus Bharata entered Ayodhya.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ayodhya, Shatrughna, Rama, Chitrakuta, Yamuna, Ganga, Guha, Sumantra

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Bharata suffer upon seeing the miserable condition of Ayodhya city?

**Answer:** When Bharata entered Ayodhya, the city was devoid of splendor. Due to the death of King Dasaratha and Rama's exile to the forest, Ayodhya was grief-stricken, dejected, lustreless, and bereft of beauty. Like the sky when clouds cover the moon and stars, Ayodhya had become pale. Ayodhya was shattered by the force of Kaikeyi's boons. Seated in his chariot as he went through the royal streets, Bharata said to Sumantra, 'Previously, when I walked through the streets of Ayodhya, the sounds of veenas, flutes, mridangams, and cymbals were heard. The city was fragrant with sandalwood, aloe, musk, and flowers. Now none of that exists. The shouts of palanquin bearers, the neighing of horses, the trumpeting of elephants, and the sound of chariot wheels were heard, but now they are absent. All the splendor and glory of this Ayodhya have gone to the forests with my brother Rama. There is nothing we can do but wait for the day when Rama returns from the forest.' Speaking thus in many ways, Bharata entered the royal palace. Seeing the inner apartments empty, Bharata shed tears.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ayodhya, Dasharatha, Rama, Kaikeyi, Sumantra

### Chapter 33: Thirty-Third Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 115-119
- Source PDF pages: 82, 83, 84, 85
- Printed page numbers: 86, 87, 88, 89
- Key entities: Bharata, Rama, Khara, Atri, Sita, Lakshmana, Maricha, Ravana, Subahu, Kausalya, Janaka, Shiva, Dasharatha
- Places: Chitrakuta, Dandaka Forest, Ayodhya, Mithila

**Summary:** Bharata decides to stay in Nandigrama during Rama's exile. Rama learns from sages that the demon Khara is troubling them. Rama leaves Chitrakuta and reaches the hermitage of Sage Atri. Sita narrates her marriage story to Anasuya. Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana leave Atri's hermitage and enter the Dandaka forest.

#### Q1

**Question:** Bharata, placing all his mothers in the inner apartments, grief-stricken, told his guru Vasishtha, 'O Guru! I cannot stay in Ayodhya without Rama. So I will go to a village near here and stay there for these fourteen years.' What is the name of that village?

**Options:**
- 1. Shringaberipura
- 2. Nandigrama
- 3. Vaishali
- 4. Karusha

**Correct answer:** Nandigrama

**Key entities:** Bharata, Ayodhya, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Rama lived for some time in the Chitrakuta region. One day, Rama noticed that the hermitage dwellers in that area were planning to leave the region. He asked a great sage the reason. The sage replied, 'The torment of demons has increased in this area. One of them is very powerful. Rama! You too come with us, go far away, and build hermitages.' What is the name of that powerful demon?

**Options:**
- 1. Maricha
- 2. Ravana
- 3. Subahu
- 4. Khara

**Correct answer:** Khara

**Key entities:** Rama, Chitrakuta, Khara

#### Q3

**Question:** After all the sages left those hermitage sites, Rama thought in various ways. He remembered that Bharata, Kausalya, and all his people had met him here. Haunted by those memories, he decided to leave that place. Traveling some distance, he reached the hermitage of a great sage. Whose hermitage was that?

**Answer:** Atri Maharshi's hermitage

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Kausalya, Atri

#### Q4

**Question:** To whom and in what manner did Sita narrate her marriage story?

**Answer:** From the Chitrakuta mountain region, Rama along with Sita and Lakshmana reached the hermitage of Sage Atri. After bowing to the sage and introducing himself, the sage welcomed Rama like his own son. Then Sage Atri introduced Sita to his wife Anasuya. Anasuya greatly welcomed and honored Sita. In the course of conversation, Anasuya taught Sita many duties of a devoted wife. At Anasuya's request, Sita narrated her marriage story: 'O mother! King Janaka, the lord of Mithila, is my father. While plowing the earth for a sacrifice to obtain children, I emerged from a furrow in a casket. King Janaka took me in his arms and raised me with great affection, saying 'She is my daughter.' When I came of age, my father announced a swayamvara: 'I will give my daughter to him who strings the bow of Shiva that has been in our lineage since the time of Devarata.' Princes from various countries came but could not string it and returned. Then Rama, the elder of Rama and Lakshmana who came with Sage Vishwamitra, strung the bow and won me. Then my father invited King Dasharatha, my father-in-law, and celebrated my marriage with Rama with great pomp.' Thus Sita narrated her marriage story to Anasuya.

**Key entities:** Sita, Chitrakuta, Rama, Lakshmana, Atri, Janaka, Mithila, Shiva, Dasharatha

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama leave the hermitage of Sage Atri and enter the Dandaka forest?

**Answer:** Hearing Sita's marriage story, Anasuya rejoiced and said, 'O Sita! Adorn yourself now with these divine garments and ornaments I have given you. I wish to see you thus adorned and be happy.' Sita wore those garments, ornaments, and garlands and bowed to Anasuya. Then Sita went before Rama. Seeing Sita adorned with the gifts given by Anasuya out of love, Rama was very pleased. Rama and Lakshmana rejoiced that Sita had received honors not given to any human. Then Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana accepted the hospitality offered by the ascetics, spent the night there. Rising at dawn, they took leave of the ascetics and asked for the path to Dandaka forest. Following the path they indicated, Rama, the subduer of enemies, along with Sita and Lakshmana, entered the dense Dandaka forest like the sun in a cloud bank.

**Key entities:** Rama, Atri, Dandaka Forest, Sita, Lakshmana

### Chapter 34: Thirty-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-6
- Source PDF pages: 85, 86, 87
- Printed page numbers: 89, 90, 91
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Viradha, Brahma, Indra, Kabandha, Maricha, Dushana, Atri
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Kailasa

**Summary:** Rama, Sita, and Lakshmana enter the Dandaka forest, visit hermitages, encounter the demon Viradha, and then proceed to Sage Sharabhanga's ashrama where the sage attains liberation. Rama then reassures the sages and heads to Sage Sutikshna's ashrama.

#### Q1

**Question:** Sri Rama entered the Dandaka forest, which is impossible for ordinary people to step into. There he saw many hermitages. The chanting of the Vedas during sacrificial rituals echoed throughout the place. Therefore, which world is it comparable to?

**Options:**
- 1. Indra's world
- 2. Brahma's world
- 3. Vaikuntha
- 4. Kailasa

**Correct answer:** Brahma's world

**Key entities:** Rama, Dandaka Forest, Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana received hospitality from the sages, spent the night in the hermitage, and at sunrise took leave and proceeded. After going some distance, they saw a demon. What was his name?

**Options:**
- 1. Kabandha
- 2. Maricha
- 3. Viradha
- 4. Dushana

**Correct answer:** Viradha

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Viradha

#### Q3

**Question:** Viradha, who was fatally struck by Rama and Lakshmana, said that in his previous birth he was a Gandharva. By being slain by you, I have been freed from a curse. What was Viradha's name in his previous birth?

**Answer:** Tumburu

**Key entities:** Viradha, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q4

**Question:** After Sri Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, came to Sharabhanga's ashrama, what happened there?

**Answer:** Leaving Atri Maharshi's ashrama, Sri Rama walked quickly and reached the area of Sharabhanga Maharshi's ashrama by evening. From outside the ashrama, Sri Rama saw a wondrous person beside Sharabhanga Maharshi. Sri Rama realized that divine person was Indra. Then Rama told Lakshmana, 'Brother! You and your sister-in-law stay here; I will go inside and find out who that divine person is,' and entered the ashrama. Seeing this, Indra told Sharabhanga Maharshi, 'O sage! Sri Rama is coming here. I should not be seen by him now; there is still some time for that.' Then Indra left. Then Sri Rama, along with Sita and Lakshmana, had the darshan of Sharabhanga Maharshi. The sage welcomed them cordially and performed hospitality. Then Sharabhanga Maharshi asked Sri Rama to stay in his ashrama that day. Then Rama said, 'O sage! Please tell us a suitable place in this forest for us to live.' The sage replied, 'O Rama! The greatly radiant sage Sutikshna is nearby. You may meet him and arrange your residence according to his suggestion.' Then the sage said, 'O Rama! I knew beforehand that you would come here. I was waiting to give up this body after your darshan. Now, having seen you, I am fulfilled.' Then that sage established the fire, chanted the Brahma Veda mantras, and entered the fire. The fire consumed his body. Rama witnessed that scene.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Atri, Indra, Brahma

#### Q5

**Question:** From Sharabhanga's ashrama, where did Rama go and in what manner?

**Answer:** After Sharabhanga Maharshi passed away, all the sages in the ashrama came to Sri Rama and said, 'O Sri Rama! We are distressed and beseech you. We are unable to bear the torments of the cruel demons in this region. We seek refuge in you. Protect us from those demons.' To them, Rama said, 'O great souls! I entered this forest for the purpose of exile. But it seems that I entered this forest under the pretext of fulfilling my father's command, in order to eradicate the harm the demons are causing you. My coming to this forest is providential for the accomplishment of your purpose. Therefore, my exile will be greatly fruitful. We consider it our duty to destroy the demons who are enemies of the ascetics. From now on, you will see the valor of us brothers.' Thus Sri Rama gave assurance to those ascetics and, accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, set out for the ashrama of Sage Sutikshna.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lakshmana

### Chapter 35: Thirty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 7-11
- Source PDF pages: 87, 88, 89, 90
- Printed page numbers: 91, 92, 93, 94
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Agastya, Atri, Jatayu, Yama
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Chitrakuta

**Summary:** Rama, accompanied by Sita and Lakshmana, visits the hermitage of Sage Sutikshna. After receiving hospitality, Rama asks for a suitable place to stay. Sutikshna advises them to stay in his hermitage. They then travel through the Dandaka forest, visiting various hermitages, including that of Sage Mandakarni and Sage Sudarshana, and eventually reach the hermitage of Sage Agastya. Along the way, Rama recounts the story of Vatapi and Ilvala to Lakshmana.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Rama arrived at Sage Sutikshna's hermitage and accepted the hospitality, what did Sage Sutikshna say when Rama asked for a suitable place to live?

**Options:**
- 1. He told them to go to Atri's hermitage.
- 2. He told them to stay in his own hermitage.
- 3. He told them to go to Sharabhanga's hermitage.
- 4. He told them to go to Chitrakuta.

**Correct answer:** He told them to stay in his own hermitage.

**Key entities:** Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Who imparted some beneficial words to Rama as he left Sage Sutikshna's hermitage and traveled through the Dandaka forest?

**Options:**
- 1. Sita
- 2. Lakshmana
- 3. The sages
- 4. Jatayu

**Correct answer:** Sita

**Key entities:** Rama, Dandaka Forest, Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** While walking through the beautiful forest hermitages, what did Rama say to Sita that he would not abandon as long as life was in his body?

**Answer:** The vow he made

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** After leaving Sage Sutikshna's hermitage, which hermitages did Sita and Rama visit?

**Answer:** During their journey through the Dandaka forest, Rama, along with his followers, walked forward observing the mountain slopes, rivers, and forest beauty. After traveling some distance, they saw a beautiful lake. The place seemed very charming, and Rama heard melodious music. Wondering about the music in a place with no human movement, he asked the sage Dharmabhrita who was following him. The sage replied, 'O Rama! This lake was created by the sage Mandakarni through his penance. To disturb his intense penance, the gods sent apsaras, but the sage, using his power, built a house inside this lake and lives there. Their songs and dances are the sounds we hear now.' Hearing this, Rama examined the hermitage area and thought it suitable for their stay. He stayed there happily with Sita and Lakshmana, receiving the sages' worship. Thus, Rama spent ten years living comfortably in various hermitages. One day, he returned to Sage Sutikshna's hermitage with all his followers. After meeting the sage and receiving his hospitality, he learned the path to Sage Agastya's hermitage from him. On the way, he visited the hermitage of Sage Sudarshana, Agastya's brother, and following the path shown by him, reached Sage Agastya's hermitage.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Dandaka Forest, Lakshmana, Agastya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama narrate the story of Vatapi and Ilvala to his brother Lakshmana?

**Answer:** While going to Sage Sudarshana's hermitage with all his followers, Rama told his brother on the way, 'Lakshmana! Once upon a time, two brothers named Vatapi and Ilvala used to kill ascetics with their magical powers. Vatapi would become a goat, and after killing it, they would cook it appropriately for a shraddha ceremony. Ilvala, disguised as a Brahmin, would invite Brahmins for the shraddha and serve them the meat of the goat Vatapi. After the ascetics finished eating, Ilvala would call out, 'O Vatapi, come out!' Vatapi would then tear open the ascetics' stomachs and come out, and both brothers would eat the flesh of the dead Brahmins. Knowing this, Sage Agastya one day went to Vatapi's house for a shraddha meal. After the meal, Ilvala called, 'O Vatapi, come out!' Then Agastya said, 'Where is Vatapi now? He has been digested and has gone to Yama's abode.' Enraged, Ilvala attacked Agastya, but Agastya, with a roar of anger, burned him to ashes. Thus, Sage Agastya saved the ascetics from the torment of Vatapi and Ilvala.' Speaking thus about Agastya, Rama and Lakshmana continued their journey.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Agastya, Yama

### Chapter 36: Thirty-Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 12-17
- Source PDF pages: 90, 91, 92
- Printed page numbers: 94, 95, 96
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Agastya, Jatayu, Surpanakha, Ravana, Indra, Khara, Dushana
- Places: Panchavati, Chitrakuta, Godavari

**Summary:** Rama, Lakshmana, and Sita arrive at Sage Agastya's hermitage. Agastya directs them to Panchavati as a suitable dwelling. On the way, the bird Jatayu meets them and offers to accompany them. In Panchavati, Lakshmana builds a beautiful leaf hut. The demoness Shurpanakha enters the hut and propositions Rama, threatening Sita and Lakshmana.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Sri Rama came to Agastya's hermitage, through whom did he inform Sage Agastya of their arrival?

**Options:**
- 1. The Dharmabhrita who came with him
- 2. Sita Devi
- 3. That hermitage dweller
- 4. Lakshmana

**Correct answer:** Lakshmana

**Key entities:** Rama, Agastya, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** As requested by Sri Rama, what is the name of the place suitable for them to reside, as told by Agastya?

**Options:**
- 1. Panchavati
- 2. Chitrakuta
- 3. Badarikavana
- 4. Siddhashrama

**Correct answer:** Panchavati

**Key entities:** Rama, Agastya, Panchavati

#### Q3

**Question:** As per Agastya's instruction, while Rama and others were proceeding on the path to establish their dwelling, a bird appeared in the middle of the way, introduced itself, and said 'I will be with you.' What is the name of that bird?

**Answer:** Jatayu

**Key entities:** Agastya, Rama, Jatayu

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama and others set up the leaf hut in Panchavati and reside there?

**Answer:** After entering the Panchavati region, Rama said to Lakshmana, 'We have come to the place suggested by Sage Agastya. This place is very beautiful. Choose a level area where we have water, fruits, flowers, and where firewood and darbha grass are available without shortage for fire rituals.' Lakshmana surveyed the entire area and identified a place with all facilities that pleased him. He showed that place to his elder brother and with his permission, on the banks of the Godavari river, he built walls with the mud he dug. He erected beautiful, strong bamboo poles as pillars, placed long bamboo poles on them, spread tender jammi branches on those poles, tied them firmly with strong palm fiber, covered them with darbha grass, reeds, and crow bamboo leaves, and fashioned the leaf hut strongly and beautifully. Then he leveled the ground well and made it charming. Afterwards, Lakshmana went to the Godavari river, bathed, collected flowers and fruits, and returned. Then he showed the leaf hut to Sita and Rama. Sri Rama was pleased, performed Vastu puja for the hut, and entered it with Sita and Lakshmana. In that Panchavati region, Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana lived peacefully in the leaf hut for some time.

**Key entities:** Rama, Panchavati, Lakshmana, Agastya, Godavari, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the demoness named Shurpanakha, who entered the leaf hut area, behave?

**Answer:** While Sita, Rama, and Lakshmana were living happily in the leaf hut, performing their daily duties, by fate the demoness Shurpanakha came to that place. She was Ravana's sister. Seeing Sri Rama, who shone like the god of love and with the splendor of Indra, she became overcome with lust. Then the repulsive-looking Shurpanakha said, 'O handsome one! You are in the guise of an ascetic. You are accompanied by your wife and bear a bow and arrows. Why have you come to this region, which is the abode of demons?' Then Sri Rama told his story. Then Rama asked, 'I think you are a demoness. Who are you?' She replied, 'My name is Shurpanakha. Ravana, the lord of demons, is my brother. He is a great hero. Khara, Dushana, and others who roam this region are also my brothers. They are immensely powerful. I possess many powers and abilities. Seeing your wonderful form, I have become lustful. I desire to have you as my husband. What need do you have with Sita? Her form is ugly. I will eat this human woman. I will do the same to your brother. They will not be obstacles for us. O handsome one! Then we two can roam happily in these forests and on mountain peaks.' Thus the demoness Shurpanakha, who entered the leaf hut area, behaved with intoxicated eyes.

**Key entities:** Surpanakha, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ravana, Indra, Khara, Dushana

### Chapter 37: Thirty-Seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 18-23
- Source PDF pages: 92, 93, 94, 95
- Printed page numbers: 96, 97, 98, 99
- Key entities: Surpanakha, Lakshmana, Khara, Rama, Maricha, Subahu, Dushana, Trishira
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Shurpanakha, after being disfigured by Lakshmana, seeks refuge with her brother Khara. Khara sends fourteen thousand rakshasa warriors to attack Rama, but Rama kills them all. Shurpanakha returns to Khara, who then prepares for battle with his army, ignoring ominous signs.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Rama stopped Shurpanakha with a roar and told Lakshmana, 'This woman is evil-natured. Why jest with her? Disfigure her,' Lakshmana immediately cut off her nose and ears. Bleeding and wailing, whom did she approach?

**Options:**
- 1. Maricha
- 2. Subahu
- 3. Khara
- 4. Sundudunu

**Correct answer:** Khara

**Key entities:** Rama, Surpanakha, Lakshmana, Khara

#### Q2

**Question:** Hearing Shurpanakha's words, how many rakshasa warriors did Khara send against Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Twelve
- 2. Ten thousand
- 3. Fourteen thousand
- 4. Fourteen

**Correct answer:** Fourteen

**Key entities:** Surpanakha, Khara, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Seeing that Rama had killed the fourteen warriors sent by Khara, Shurpanakha wept and wailed and went again to whom?

**Answer:** Khara

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Surpanakha

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Khara behave upon hearing Shurpanakha's words?

**Answer:** Seeing Shurpanakha return to him as if it heralded the destruction of all rakshasas, Khara said, 'Shurpanakha! Why are you crying? The fourteen warriors I sent with you were equal to me. What happened to such warriors?' Shurpanakha replied, 'O brother! Rama has killed all the warriors you sent. Moreover, if you do not kill that Rama who cut off my nose and ears today, I will give up my life before you. It is not enough to boast that you are a hero. Kill that mere human Rama.' Fainting, she fell. Khara said, 'Sister! Because of this irreparable insult to you, anger surges in me. Rama is a mere human and short-lived. Before my prowess, he is nothing. I will kill not only him but also his brother. Calm down and wipe your tears.' Then Khara called his commander Dushana and ordered, 'O Dushana! Prepare my chariot immediately. Gather all weapons. I, skilled in warfare, will lead. Command all our troops to be battle-ready and march.' Thus Khara commanded his commander and became battle-ready.

**Key entities:** Khara, Surpanakha, Rama, Dushana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Khara, along with all his men, become battle-ready and advance against Rama?

**Answer:** Fourteen thousand fearsome rakshasa warriors, holding various weapons like iron clubs, broadswords, and tridents, followed Khara. Khara's horses yoked to his chariot sped along a smooth royal road, yet suddenly the chariot seemed to stumble. In the dark sky, a halo formed around the sun. On the tall flag atop the chariot, a large vulture circled and perched on it. Many such inauspicious omens appeared to Khara. But disregarding them, Khara told his men, 'Even though these great portents befall, I, a courageous one, do not heed them at all. I will surely destroy the arrogant Rama and his brother with my fierce arrows. I have never known defeat in my previous battles. May it be so now!' Hearing Khara's words, all his followers rejoiced. Around Khara's chariot, twelve commanders followed, including the chief commanders Sthulaksha, Pramadhi, Trishira, and Mahakapala. Thus the rakshasa army, filled with battle fervor, rapidly approached the princes Rama and Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Khara, Rama, Trishira, Lakshmana

### Chapter 38: Thirty-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 24-29
- Source PDF pages: 95, 96, 97
- Printed page numbers: 99, 100, 101
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Khara, Agastya, Dushana, Trishira, Dasharatha, Yama
- Places: Godavari, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Rama instructs Lakshmana to take Sita to a cave for safety as Khara approaches with his army. Rama uses the Gandharva astra to create countless arrows. After killing fourteen thousand demons, only Khara remains. A fierce battle ensues between Rama and Khara, with harsh words exchanged. Rama uses the Vaishnava bow given by Agastya.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Rama saw Khara coming with his army, he told Lakshmana to take the responsibility of protecting his sister-in-law and take her to which place?

**Options:**
- 1. To the shade of a tree
- 2. Into the leaf hut
- 3. Into a mountain cave
- 4. To the Godavari region

**Correct answer:** Into a mountain cave

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** When the demons started the battle and raged with many weapons, Rama released an astra. By its effect, thousands of arrows spread in all directions. What is the name of that astra released by Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Agneyastra
- 2. Varunastra
- 3. Aindrastra
- 4. Gandharvastra

**Correct answer:** Gandharvastra

**Key entities:** Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** When fourteen thousand soldiers and commanders were killed by the enemy-destroying Rama, who was the last one remaining?

**Answer:** Khara

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the battle between Rama and Khara take place?

**Answer:** Seeing Dushana and Trishira fall on the battlefield, Khara was somewhat afraid seeing Rama's prowess. Besides Trishira and Dushana, seeing that Rama alone had destroyed the invincible vast army of fourteen thousand demons before his eyes, all his pride subsided. Regaining courage, Khara rushed at Rama. Khara drew his powerful bow and shot arrows at Rama. Mounted on his chariot, Khara displayed his archery skills in various ways. Then the descendant of Raghu covered the sky with his unerring arrows that emitted sparks. The sky became filled with the sharp arrows shot by Rama and Khara. Seeing that despite having destroyed the vast demon army, Rama remained steadfast with great valor in battle, Khara thought, 'This descendant of Raghu is immensely powerful.' Like a locust that, not knowing its own destruction, rushes into fire, Khara rushed at Rama. Then Rama took the Vaishnava bow given by Sage Agastya and rushed at Khara. Thus the battle between Rama and Khara continued.

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Dushana, Trishira, Agastya

#### Q5

**Question:** During the battle, how did Rama and Khara speak harshly to each other?

**Answer:** Seeing Khara, who had lost his chariot and held a mace, Rama said, 'O night-wanderer! You, who had elephants, horses, chariots, and infantry, committed terrible deeds. All the worlds abhor your evil deeds. One who causes fear to all beings, who torments, who engages in sinful acts, even if he is the lord of the three worlds, cannot escape death. What then of a lowly one like you? Even the most compassionate, when faced with a serpent that comes at them, will not refrain from killing it. What did you gain by killing the ascetics who lived righteously in this Dandaka forest, minding their own business? Sinners who perform evil deeds, even if they obtain wealth, soon perish. O demon! To take the lives of those who plot evil against humanity and engage in terrible sinful acts, King Dasaratha sent me to this Dandaka forest.' Thus Rama spoke. Then Khara said, 'O son of Dasaratha! Having killed ordinary soldiers in battle, you boast about yourself like a great hero. Is what you did really a battle? Self-praise is a sign of your inferiority. Do you not see me standing before you in this battlefield, holding a mace, like a steadfast mountain? I alone, like Yama who takes away your life, am enough to take your life.' Saying this, Khara hurled the mace from his shoulder at Rama. Rama shattered the weapon with his arrow. Thus Khara and Rama spoke harshly and began to fight.

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Dandaka Forest, Dasharatha, Yama

### Chapter 39: Thirty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 30-35
- Source PDF pages: 97, 98, 99, 100
- Printed page numbers: 101, 102, 103, 104
- Key entities: Rama, Khara, Dushana, Ravana, Maricha, Surpanakha, Sita, Trishira, Subahu, Lakshmana
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Lanka

**Summary:** Rama kills Khara, Dushana, and fourteen thousand demons. Akampana informs Ravana of their deaths. Enraged, Ravana seeks Maricha's help. Shurpanakha incites Ravana by describing Sita's beauty and her own disfigurement. Ravana decides to abduct Sita and goes to Maricha's hermitage to seek his assistance.

#### Q1

**Question:** In how many ghatikas did Sri Rama slay Khara, Dushana, and the fourteen thousand demons?

**Options:**
- 1. Five ghatikas
- 2. Seven ghatikas
- 3. Two ghatikas
- 4. Three ghatikas

**Correct answer:** Three ghatikas

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara, Dushana

#### Q2

**Question:** Who first informed Ravana of the death of Khara and all their people?

**Options:**
- 1. Akampana
- 2. Dushana
- 3. Trishira
- 4. Subahu

**Correct answer:** Akampana

**Key entities:** Ravana, Khara

#### Q3

**Question:** Enraged by Akampana's words, Ravana came to Dandaka forest and sought support from whom in Janasthana to kill Sri Rama?

**Answer:** Maricha

**Key entities:** Ravana, Dandaka Forest, Rama, Maricha

#### Q4

**Question:** Ravana was somewhat pacified by Maricha's advice. How did Shurpanakha again provoke him and send him against Rama?

**Answer:** Ravana went to Maricha to seek his cooperation for abducting Sita. Maricha said, 'O Ravana! War with Sri Rama is not proper for you. He who sent you after telling you about Sita and Rama is not your well-wisher. Listen to me. Give up this idea and go to Lanka and live happily.' Ravana agreed and returned to Lanka. In Lanka, Shurpanakha came fearfully to Ravana seated in court. She displayed her disfigured form caused by Lakshmana in Dandaka forest and spoke to her brother Ravana: 'O Ravana! Without anyone to oppose you, you are an autocrat, immersed in sensual pleasures and intoxicated. A situation even fearful to hear has arisen. O brother!
