Knowing that countless of our demon warriors have died a terrible death in the battlefield of Janasthana, how can you be indifferent towards the enemy? Ravana! The truth is that among the beauties of gods, gandharvas, yakshas, kinnaras, and humans, there is none as beautiful as her. She is Rama's wife, Sita Devi. She is worthy of being your wife. Thinking thus, I was trying in that direction when Rama's brother Lakshmana disfigured me like this. To pacify the souls of Khara, Dushana and other demons, you must kill Rama and Lakshmana. Then you can enjoy the helpless Sita as you wish.' Hearing Shurpanakha's words, Ravana discussed with his ministers in court and decided his course of action.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Maricha, Surpanakha, Rama, Sita, Lanka, Lakshmana, Dandaka Forest, Khara, Dushana

#### Q5

**Question:** Having come to a firm decision regarding the abduction of Sita, what did Ravana do?

**Answer:** Ravana went from the court to his inner palace, thoroughly considered the feasibility of abducting Sita, compared his strength with Rama's, and finally decided on the abduction. Then he went to the stable and told the charioteer to prepare the chariot. As per the king's order, the charioteer prepared a golden chariot yoked with donkeys having demonic forms. Ravana mounted it, came to the seashore, and traveled through the sky on a chariot that moved at his will. Traveling thus, Ravana saw a beautiful and peaceful hermitage. There he saw a demon named Maricha, wearing a black deer skin, with matted hair, and observing dietary restrictions. Then Maricha offered hospitality to the arriving Ravana and worshipped him with various luxuries. Maricha personally arranged food for Ravana. Then Maricha asked, 'O king of demons! Is everyone in Lanka well? Why have you come here alone so suddenly?' Then Ravana explained to him the necessity of abducting Sita.

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Rama, Maricha, Lanka

### Chapter 40: Fortieth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 36-41
- Source PDF pages: 100, 101, 102
- Printed page numbers: 104, 105, 106
- Key entities: Ravana, Maricha, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Ravana seeks Maricha's help to abduct Sita. He orders Maricha to take the form of a golden deer to lure Rama away. Maricha warns Ravana about Rama's prowess and the dangers of the plan, but Ravana threatens him into compliance.

#### Q1

**Question:** Ravana asked Maricha to cooperate in the abduction of Sita. What form did he tell Maricha to assume and wander near Sita?

**Options:**
- 1. Elephant
- 2. Horse
- 3. Deer (buck)
- 4. Dog

**Correct answer:** Deer (buck)

**Key entities:** Ravana, Maricha, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** Advising Ravana, what did Maricha primarily say about Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Fickle
- 2. Lowly
- 3. Embodiment of dharma
- 4. Coward

**Correct answer:** Embodiment of dharma

**Key entities:** Ravana, Maricha, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** Maricha told Ravana about his past experience where Rama showed unparalleled valor. Where did that incident take place?

**Answer:** Siddhashrama

**Key entities:** Maricha, Ravana, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana bring Maricha under his control to make him obey his words?

**Answer:** Despite Maricha's warnings about Rama's strength, Ravana refused to listen. He said, 'O Maricha! I need your help for the task I have planned. I did not ask you whether it is good or bad. Listen to what you must do. O Maricha! Transform into a strange golden deer with white spots like silver and wander near Rama's hermitage. Freely roaming thus, tempt Sita. Then Vaidehi, seeing the magical deer, will ask Rama to bring it to her immediately. Rama will come to catch you as per her wish. You lead him far away. Then, imitating Rama's voice, cry out loudly, 'Ha Sita! Ha Lakshmana!' Hearing those words, Sita will grieve and urge Lakshmana to go. Once Lakshmana leaves, I will easily take Vaidehi away. O Maricha! This is the only task you need to do for me. After that, you may go as you please. Thus, without fighting Rama, I will deceive him and go to Lanka with Sita. If you do not do as I say, I will kill you right now. Even if you are unwilling, I will make you do this task. If you assume the form of an animal, you might survive by fate. But if you oppose me, your life will end now. Consider which of the two you choose.' Thus Ravana threatened Maricha and brought him to his side.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Maricha, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Lanka

#### Q5

**Question:** In how many ways did Maricha tell Ravana that the task he intended to do was not good?

**Answer:** Maricha, criticizing Ravana's arrogant command, said, 'O night-ranger! If you abduct Sita like this, you will be destroyed along with your main army. Who is the wicked one who gave you this disastrous advice? O king! Who is that sinner who cannot bear your happiness? Who are your weak demon enemies who, unable to confront you directly, desire your death at the hands of the stronger Rama? O Ravana! Who is waiting for your harm by planting this evil thought in your head? Even if someone intends to harm you due to your own fault, you alone will suffer the consequences. O Ravana! Soon after Rama kills me, he will kill you too. Dying at Rama's hands, I will give up my life seeing that great soul. You, having abducted Sita, will die along with your relatives, friends, and retinue. If the abduction happens as per your plan, neither you nor I nor the demons will survive. Lanka will cease to exist. O Ravana! I speak for your good, yet you do not listen. When one's end is near, he does not heed a friend's words. You are behaving likewise.' Thus Maricha advised Ravana in many ways.

**Key entities:** Maricha, Ravana, Sita, Rama, Lanka

### Chapter 41: Forty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 42-47
- Source PDF pages: 102, 103, 104, 105
- Printed page numbers: 106, 107, 108, 109
- Key entities: Maricha, Ravana, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Kabandha, Viradha
- Places: Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Maricha, under Ravana's orders, goes to Rama's hermitage in Dandaka forest. He takes the form of a golden deer to lure Rama away. Lakshmana suspects it is Maricha's illusion. Rama pursues the deer and shoots it; Maricha cries out in Rama's voice. Sita hears the cry and forces Lakshmana to go to Rama's aid. After Lakshmana leaves, Ravana approaches Sita in the guise of a sage and tries to abduct her.

#### Q1

**Question:** By which trees did Maricha, who came on Ravana's chariot, identify Sri Rama's hermitage in Dandaka forest?

**Options:**
- 1. Sandalwood trees
- 2. Maddi trees
- 3. Jammi trees
- 4. Banana trees

**Correct answer:** Banana trees

**Key entities:** Maricha, Ravana, Rama, Dandaka Forest

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing the illusory deer wandering near their hermitage, Lakshmana told his elder brother that this is not an ordinary deer. Which demon's illusion is this?

**Options:**
- 1. Kabandha
- 2. Viradha
- 3. Maricha
- 4. Akampana

**Correct answer:** Maricha

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Maricha

#### Q3

**Question:** Armed with bow and arrows, Rama followed the illusory deer far away. There, struck by Rama's arrow, Maricha in deer form cried out in what manner?

**Answer:** Ha! Sita! Ha! Lakshmana!

**Key entities:** Rama, Maricha, Sita, Lakshmana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana get the opportunity to approach Sita?

**Answer:** The cry of Maricha in deer form, struck by Rama's arrow, resembled Rama's voice. Hearing it, Sita concluded that Rama was in danger and told Lakshmana, 'That cry is your brother's. Since hearing it, my mind is not at peace. My life is leaving me. So Lakshmana! Run immediately to protect him.' Even as Sita spoke thus, Lakshmana stayed there as per his brother's order. Then Janaki angrily said, 'O Saumitri! You pretend love for your brother. In truth, you have no love for him. You are his enemy. Even in such danger, you do not go to him. Actually, you desire me and are trying to harm Rama. Truly, you have no love for your brother.' Speaking these unbearable words, Sita, trembling with fear, thought her husband was in danger. Lakshmana said, 'Mother! No one among gods, demons, nagas, gandharvas, or humans can defeat Sri Rama. There is no doubt.' Though Lakshmana consoled Sita in many ways, hurt by her stubbornness and harsh words, he bowed to her, reluctantly left, and went to Rama. As soon as Lakshmana left, Ravana, who was waiting for the opportunity, appeared before Sita in the guise of a sage.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Maricha, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** When Ravana, in the guise of a sage, went to Sita in the leaf hut, what happened there?

**Answer:** Ravana entered the hermitage in the guise of a sage when Rama and Lakshmana were absent. Reciting Vedic mantras appropriately for a sage's appearance, he saw Vaidehi, Rama's wife. Overcome with desire, he said to Sita, 'O woman! Who are you? I have never seen a jewel of a woman like you, a mass of beauty.' Praising her in many ways, he said, 'O young lady! Why are you in this place where shape-shifting demons roam? O auspicious one! What is your name? Whose are you? Why are you staying in this Dandaka forest?' Though Ravana spoke thus, Sita, anxious that her husband Rama had not yet returned, listened absent-mindedly. Because of his ascetic guise, she honored him with hospitality. Ravana, however, was thinking of abducting her. Then, at Ravana's request, Sita told him her entire story. Afterwards, she asked, 'O best of brahmins! Who are you? What is the reason for your wandering in this Dandaka forest?' To that, Ravana said in a harsh voice, 'O Sita! I am Ravana, the king of demons. I have brought many beautiful women. If you accept me as your husband, you will become my chief queen. All my wives will serve you. Thousands of maids will serve you.' Sita scorned him. Then Ravana explained to her about the demon race and his own valor.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Dandaka Forest

### Chapter 42: Forty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 48-53
- Source PDF pages: 105, 106, 107
- Printed page numbers: 109, 110, 111
- Key entities: Ravana, Sita, Jatayu, Kubera, Sampati, Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Ravana abducts Sita after defeating Jatayu. He boasts of his prowess, takes Sita through the sky, and Sita rebukes him harshly. The chapter covers Ravana's abduction, Jatayu's intervention, and Sita's lament.

#### Q1

**Question:** Ravana, while telling Sita about his prowess, said that he is the brother of Kubera, but after fighting with that Kubera, what did he conquer and take possession of?

**Options:**
- 1. Divine chariot
- 2. Kubera's wife
- 3. Pushpaka Vimana
- 4. Diamond throne

**Correct answer:** Pushpaka Vimana

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Kubera

#### Q2

**Question:** When Ravana was forcibly abducting Sita, who obstructed him?

**Options:**
- 1. Forest deities
- 2. Jatayu
- 3. Sampati
- 4. Anjaneya

**Correct answer:** Jatayu

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Jatayu

#### Q3

**Question:** During the battle between Ravana and Jatayu, Jatayu's blow destroyed Ravana's chariot, charioteer, and the donkeys with distorted faces yoked to the chariot. For what reason did Ravana notice that Jatayu was somewhat fatigued?

**Answer:** Old age

**Key entities:** Ravana, Jatayu

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana forcibly take Sita away?

**Answer:** Seeing Jatayu fall near the hermitage, Ravana approached Sita. She embraced the dying Jatayu and wept. When Ravana came towards her, Sita cried out 'Rama! Lakshmana!' and, frightened, hugged a tree tightly, weeping 'Rama! Protect me! Protect me!'. Then Ravana grabbed the weeping Sita by her hair and dragged her. Seeing the insult to Sita at Ravana's hands, nature was plunged into darkness. The rakshasa king took Janaki, who was crying 'Rama! Lakshmana! Protect me!', and flew into the sky. The auspicious Sita's ornaments and anklets, struck by the wind, fell one by one here and there. All the flowers from her braid scattered on the ground. Thus Sita, with unbearable grief, wept loudly in a pitiful voice, crying 'Rama! Lakshmana!' and repeatedly looked down at the ground. Seeing Sita like that, the forest deities trembled. Her hair was disheveled, the tilak on her forehead was smeared. Ravana abducted that chaste wife because his death was near.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Jatayu, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** While Ravana was abducting her towards Lanka city, how did Sita speak harshly?

**Answer:** Sita, angry at Ravana who was taking her through the sky, wept bitterly and lamented helplessly, saying: 'O vile Ravana! You came when Rama and Lakshmana were absent and are fleeing with me like a thief. Aren't you ashamed to do such a deed? O wicked one! Desiring to abduct me, fearing my husband, you sent him away from me in the form of a magical deer and are abducting me. What hero are you? You killed Jatayu, who was a friend of my father-in-law. Is killing an old bird heroism? O lowest of rakshasas! You did not defeat Raghuvira in battle and bring me here. From this, your prowess is evident. O lowly one! You abducted the wife of a man when he was absent. Aren't you ashamed to do such a despicable deed? Though devoid of prowess, you boast of being a great hero. By thus harming the great Rama, you will surely die like one who has drunk poison. You are abducting the wife of Rama, who alone, without his brother, killed fourteen thousand demons. Will Rama spare the one who abducted his wife? Your death is near.' Thus Janaki, overcome with fear and grief, spoke many harsh words. Yet Ravana, disregarding her, continued on his way.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Lanka, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Jatayu

### Chapter 43: Forty-Third Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 54-58
- Source PDF pages: 107, 108, 109, 110
- Printed page numbers: 111, 112, 113, 114
- Key entities: Rama, Maricha, Sita, Lakshmana, Ravana, Vibhishana
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Rama returns to the hermitage after killing Maricha, only to find Sita missing. He laments and questions Lakshmana about leaving her alone. The chapter also covers Sita's abduction by Ravana, her dropping of ornaments for the monkeys, and Ravana's threats.

#### Q1

**Question:** Sita, abducted by Ravana, tore her garment, tied her ornaments in a bundle, and dropped it among the foremost monkeys on a mountain peak. How many foremost monkeys were there?

**Options:**
- 1. Eight
- 2. Seven
- 3. Six
- 4. Five

**Correct answer:** Five

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana

#### Q2

**Question:** When Ravana brought Sita through the sky to Lanka, where did he first place her?

**Options:**
- 1. In the Ashoka grove
- 2. In the Pushpaka chariot
- 3. In his inner palace
- 4. In Vibhishana's house

**Correct answer:** In his inner palace

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Lanka

#### Q3

**Question:** Ravana showed his wealth and splendor, but Sita did not accept him as her husband. So he placed her in the Ashoka grove, set a deadline, and threatened to kill her after it expired. How many months was the deadline?

**Answer:** Twelve months

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Ashoka Grove

#### Q4

**Question:** What happened after Sri Rama killed Maricha?

**Answer:** Maricha, in the form of a deer, led Rama far away. Rama killed the shape-shifting Maricha and started back to the hermitage. Then a jackal behind him howled hideously. Hearing it, Rama's body trembled, suspecting some calamity. Maricha had imitated Rama's voice crying 'Ha Sita! Ha Lakshmana!' Thinking of the inauspicious jackal's cry, Rama hurried back. Meanwhile, Lakshmana, with a dejected face, met him. Rama grasped Lakshmana's left hand and, expressing anguish, rebuked him: 'Lakshmana! How could you leave Sita alone in this forest, the abode of demons? You have made a great mistake. The demons here might have killed her or eaten her. Lakshmana! Will we ever see Sita alive? The demon in deer form lured me far away. Finally I killed him.' Saying this, Rama walked quickly with Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Rama, Maricha, Sita, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana reach the hermitage?

**Answer:** Rama, agitated, said to Lakshmana: 'Lakshmana! Where did you leave Sita? I cannot live without her. Is she still alive? Due to your carelessness, has that noble woman fallen into the hands of demons? The wicked demon imitated my voice crying 'Alas! Lakshmana!' and you might have been frightened. Because of that fear, Vaidehi might also have been scared and sent you to me.' Thus speaking in various ways, Rama lamented about Sita and walked quickly to the hermitage. Having walked a long distance, Rama was very tired. Due to hunger and thirst, his face was withered and pale. In that state, he rebuked Lakshmana with anguish, sighing deeply, and reached the hermitage. Not finding Sita anywhere, they searched inside the leaf hut and the surrounding areas. The result was empty. Rama, stunned, began to suffer greatly.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

### Chapter 44: Forty-Fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 59-64
- Source PDF pages: 110, 111, 112
- Printed page numbers: 114, 115, 116
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Janaka, Vayu
- Places: Ayodhya, Godavari

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana return to the hermitage to find Sita missing. Rama is overwhelmed with grief and searches desperately, while Lakshmana tries to console him. They follow clues including scattered flowers, footprints, and signs of a struggle, deducing that Sita was abducted by a rakshasa.

#### Q1

**Question:** When asked by his brother why he left Sita alone in the hermitage, Lakshmana replied: 'Brother! I had to come because my sister-in-law scolded me with words my ears could not bear and my mouth could not utter.' Then Rama said: 'Whatever it is, brother! I see some bad omens. Therefore something terrible must have happened.' What is one of those bad omens?

**Options:**
- 1. My right shoulder twitched
- 2. My right eye twitched
- 2. My left leg twitched
- 4. My left eye twitched

**Correct answer:** My left eye twitched

**Key entities:** Sita, Lakshmana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** When Rama and Lakshmana came to the hermitage, they could not find any trace of Sita. They looked here and there. Rama's eyes turned red with the weight of grief. Searching for Sita, asking every tree, bush, bank, mountain, valley, and river 'Where is my Sita? Where is my Sita?', how did Rama appear at that time?

**Options:**
- 1. He appeared like a madman
- 2. He appeared like a great hero
- 3. He appeared like a great king
- 4. He appeared like a forest-dweller

**Correct answer:** He appeared like a madman

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** Despite Lakshmana's attempts to console Rama over the pain of not finding Sita, Rama remained inconsolable. He said to Lakshmana: 'I came to the forests with Sita. If I return to Ayodhya without Sita, and the people there ask where Sita is, what shall I reply?' He lamented, especially asking: 'If [who] confronts me and asks where Sita is, what shall I say?'

**Answer:** King Janaka

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Rama, Sita, Ayodhya, Janaka

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama suffer, remembering Sita in various ways?

**Answer:** Rama, overwhelmed with grief and separation from Sita, lamented: 'Lakshmana! There is no one more unfortunate than me on this earth. An endless series of sorrows haunts me, tearing my heart and mind. Brother! The noble Sita is timid. Someone must have forcibly abducted her through the sky. How frightened my Janaki must have been! My virtuous wife, who would not even bear the touch of another man, might have been killed by rakshasas who drank her blood. At that time, she must have looked for my help without blinking. Lakshmana! Your sister-in-law used to sit with me on this stone slab and converse charmingly about many things. She loved this Godavari river very much, but she never went to the river without me. O Sun god! You are the witness to all actions. You know everything in the world. O Wind god! Nothing happens without your knowledge. Please tell me where my Sita is.' Thus Rama lamented in despair, while Lakshmana said, 'Brother! Give up grief. Do not lose hope. Be courageous. Let us search with enthusiasm.' But even as his brother spoke, Rama lost his courage and sank into endless sorrow.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Godavari, Vayu

#### Q5

**Question:** What did Rama and Lakshmana discuss as they began the search for Sita?

**Answer:** Rama, grieving and sorrowing for Sita, said: 'Lakshmana! Let us search along this riverbank and in the region of Prashravana Hill. Sita may be found. The strong animals are looking at me as if they want to tell me something.' Then he asked the animals, 'Where is my Sita?' Immediately, the animals looked towards the southern sky and ran in that direction. Seeing this, Lakshmana said, 'They are showing us the direction Sita went. Brother! Let us travel in the south-westerly direction. In that direction, which is the abode of rakshasas, our sister-in-law may be found.' As the two brothers walked in that direction, they saw scattered flowers along the way. Rama recognized them as the ones Sita had worn. Further on, they saw large footprints of a rakshasa and footprints of Sita. Going further, they saw bloodstains, a broken bow, a chariot, a charioteer, and deformed donkeys. Seeing this, they concluded that two rakshasas must have seen Sita, quarreled over eating her, and fought. Rama said, 'Lakshmana! None of the gods tried to protect my Sita. If they do not return my Sita to me now, they will experience my wrath.' And Rama, enraged, took up his bow.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

### Chapter 45: Forty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 65-70
- Source PDF pages: 112, 113, 114, 115
- Printed page numbers: 116, 117, 118, 119
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Jatayu, Ravana, Kabandha, Sugriva
- Places: Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana continue searching for Sita. They find signs of a struggle and meet the dying bird Jatayu, who tells them Ravana abducted Sita southward. They perform Jatayu's funeral rites. Later, they encounter the demon Kabandha, who seizes them. Lakshmana cuts off his arms, and Kabandha reveals his story and advises them to seek Sugriva's help.

#### Q1

**Question:** Lakshmana, consoling Rama who was mentally emaciated due to separation from Sita, said: 'Brother! This entire area is crushed by the pressure of chariot wheel rims. Based on the war signs here, how many people might have fought here?' What did Lakshmana tell Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Two
- 2. One alone
- 2. A great army
- 4. Three

**Correct answer:** One alone

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Rama, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** While Rama was grieving and lamenting for Sita, Lakshmana pacified him, informed him of his duty, and they walked forward a distance. There they saw Jatayu in his final moments. Jatayu told Rama that Ravana had abducted Sita and had thrown him down like this when he tried to stop him. The king of birds then gave up his life. What did Rama and Lakshmana do with Jatayu's body?

**Options:**
- 1. Buried it in the ground
- 2. Left it there and went away
- 3. Performed cremation rites
- 4. Hung it from a tree

**Correct answer:** Performed cremation rites

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Jatayu, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** How and in which direction did Jatayu tell Rama that Ravana took Janaki Devi?

**Answer:** Through the sky, towards the south.

**Key entities:** Jatayu, Rama, Ravana, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the demon named Kabandha appear to Rama and Lakshmana as they were going in search of Sita?

**Answer:** Rama and Lakshmana, both armed with bows and arrows, traveled southwest searching for Sita. They crossed the Dandaka forest, entered the Krauncha forest, and after traveling three yojanas, they came to a place between Matanga ashrama and Krauncha forest. There they saw a mountain cave. From there, they walked forward and entered a dense forest. Then they heard a great noise that made the forest tremble. Walking in the direction of the sound, they saw a demon of grotesque form. His two arms extended far away, and with such arms he was dragging even cruel beasts. That Kabandha stood blocking their path, caught both of them, and pulled them close. Then Rama said, 'Brother! No matter how much we search, Sita is not found. Now even our lives are in danger. For anyone, the influence of time cannot be overcome. Lakshmana! Even the valiant, the strong, and those skilled in archery become subject to time and suffer hardships. It is not difficult for the divine to control even the greatest.' Thus speaking to Lakshmana, Rama steadied his mind.

**Key entities:** Kabandha, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Dandaka Forest

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana finish off Kabandha?

**Answer:** Seeing the princes caught in his arms, Kabandha said, 'O princes! Seeing that I am hungry, that god himself has sent you as my food. There is no use thinking further.' Hearing the demon speaking thus, Lakshmana said, 'Brother! There is no need for weapons to kill this demon. Cut off that arm with the sword in your hand. I will cut off this arm with the sword in my hand.' Then Lakshmana cut off the arm that held him. When both his arms were cut off, Kabandha roared, making the earth and sky tremble. That demon, wallowing in a pool of blood, sorrowfully asked, 'Sirs! Who are you?' Then Lakshmana replied, 'We are of the Ikshvaku dynasty. This one, endowed with divine power, is Sri Rama. I am his younger brother, Lakshmana. Due to certain reasons, a demon abducted Sri Rama's wife. Searching for her, we have come here. Now, who are you?' When Saumitri asked, Kabandha said, 'O best of men! My fortune has ripened, and I have obtained your sight. By my good fortune, you have cut off my arms. Because I behaved disrespectfully, I was cursed and obtained this grotesque form.' Then Kabandha narrated his entire story to Rama and Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Kabandha

### Chapter 46: Forty-Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Aranya Kanda
- Sarga range: 71-75
- Source PDF pages: 115, 116, 117, 118
- Printed page numbers: 119, 120, 121, 122
- Key entities: Kabandha, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Shabari, Atri, Vali, Hanuman, Angada, Sita
- Places: Rishyamuka

**Summary:** Kabandha tells his story to Rama and Lakshmana, revealing the sage who cursed him. After gaining a divine form, he advises them to seek Sugriva's help. Rama and Lakshmana journey towards Rishyamuka Mountain, meeting the ascetic Shabari at Matanga's hermitage, who is blessed by Rama and attains liberation. They then proceed to Pampa Lake and Rishyamuka.

#### Q1

**Question:** While telling his story to Rama and Lakshmana, Kabandha revealed which great sage cursed him to get this deformed form?

**Options:**
- 1. Sharabhanga
- 2. Matanga Maharshi
- 3. Sthulashira
- 4. Atri Maharshi

**Correct answer:** Sthulashira

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Kabandha

#### Q2

**Question:** After obtaining a divine body, whom did Kabandha advise Rama and Lakshmana to take refuge in for their mission to succeed?

**Options:**
- 1. Vali
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Angada
- 4. Sugriva

**Correct answer:** Sugriva

**Key entities:** Kabandha, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva

#### Q3

**Question:** As instructed by Kabandha, Rama and Lakshmana traveled towards Rishyamuka Mountain. On the way, they saw an old female ascetic at Matanga Maharshi's hermitage. What was her name?

**Answer:** Shabari

**Key entities:** Kabandha, Rama, Lakshmana, Rishyamuka, Shabari

#### Q4

**Question:** While coming to meet Sugriva, whom did Rama and Lakshmana bless and how at Matanga's hermitage on the way?

**Answer:** Following the path told by Kabandha, Rama and Lakshmana both started walking westwards through that forest. After traveling some distance, they spent the night on a mountain peak there, and the next morning reached the western shore of Pampa Lake. Then they reached the hermitage, which was lush with trees, and met Shabari there. That Shabari, who had attained yogic perfection, seeing Rama and Lakshmana, folded her hands and bowed at their feet. Then Shabari worshipped both brothers with offerings of arghya and padya and presented fruits and flowers. Then Rama said, 'O ascetic! Is there any hindrance to your penance? Are you fulfilled in your service to your guru?' To Rama's words, Shabari replied, 'O Lord Ramachandra! By seeing you with my own eyes, my penance is fulfilled. All the sages I served, while going to heaven, said that Sri Rama will come to this sacred hermitage with Lakshmana. Honor him. By his sight, you will attain the highest worlds. O holy man! With your permission, I will abandon this body. My gurus are holy men; I will go to the worlds they went to. Please permit me.' According to Shabari's wish, Rama said, 'O Shabari! I am pleased with your worship. You may go as you wish.' Then, with Rama's permission, Shabari, in a state of yogic meditation, left her body and went to the eternal worlds. Then Rama and Lakshmana performed the fire rites for the devout Shabari's earthly body and continued their journey from there.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Kabandha, Shabari

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana's journey from Shabari's hermitage to the Rishyamuka Mountain region proceed?

**Answer:** Near Shabari's hermitage, both Rama and Lakshmana bathed in the Saptasagara Tirtha and offered libations to the ancestors. Then Rama said, 'Brother! With this, all our inauspiciousness has perished. My mind has found some relief. It feels that only good will happen to us now. Lakshmana! Let us now go along the shore of Pampa Lake. Rishyamuka Mountain is nearby. There Sugriva lives, fearing his brother Vali. That foremost of vanaras can help us in the search for Sita.' As Rama was speaking, Lakshmana said, 'Brother! My mind is also eager for that. So we must go quickly.' Thus both brothers started walking along the shore of Pampa Lake. Then Rama said, 'Brother! As Kabandha told us, Rishyamuka Mountain is in this Pampa Lake region. Lakshmana! In this state, without Sita Devi by my side, how can I live?' Remembering Sita Devi and grieving, Rama was consoled by Lakshmana, and together they walked along Pampa Lake.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Shabari, Rishyamuka, Sugriva, Vali, Sita, Kabandha

### Chapter 47: Forty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-6
- Source PDF pages: 118, 119, 120
- Printed page numbers: 122, 123, 124
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Sugriva, Hanuman, Ravana, Vali
- Places: Rishyamuka

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana search for Sita on Rishyamuka Mountain. Sugriva sends Hanuman to ascertain their intentions. Hanuman meets them, learns their story, and brings Sugriva. Rama and Sugriva form a friendship with fire as witness. Sugriva shows Rama the bundle of jewels dropped by Sita when she was abducted by Ravana.

#### Q1

**Question:** As Sri Rama, along with Lakshmana, traversed all forests, streams, and mountain caves searching for Sita, and walked on Rishyamuka Mountain, who among the monkeys was the first to be afraid upon seeing those bow-bearing Rama and Lakshmana?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Mainda
- 3. Dvivida
- 4. Sugriva

**Correct answer:** Sugriva

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Rishyamuka, Sugriva

#### Q2

**Question:** Sugriva sent Hanuman to find out who Rama and Lakshmana were and their true intentions, and in what form did he ask him to go?

**Options:**
- 1. Human form
- 2. Monkey form
- 3. Rakshasa form
- 4. As a Gandharva

**Correct answer:** Human form

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q3

**Question:** Hanuman met Rama and Lakshmana, spoke to them sweetly, and told them about Sugriva's story: that our lord Sugriva was driven from his kingdom by his elder brother Vali, and that Vali also took Sugriva's wife under his control. What is the name of Sugriva's wife?

**Answer:** Ruma

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Vali

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the friendship between Rama and Sugriva take place?

**Answer:** When Hanuman brought Rama and Lakshmana to Rishyamuka Mountain, Sugriva had gone to nearby Malaya Mountain. Then Hanuman went to Sugriva, brought the monkey king, and on the way told him all he knew about Rama and Lakshmana. He brought him to Rishyamuka Mountain and presented him to Rama and Lakshmana. Then Maruti (Hanuman) said to Sugriva, 'Lord! These Rama and Lakshmana are princes of the Ikshvaku dynasty. They are renowned for their righteous conduct. While living in exile to fulfill their father's command, Ravana abducted Rama's wife. Therefore, he has come here seeking your help.' Hearing Hanuman's words, Sugriva rejoiced, and with the sight of Rama, all his fear vanished. He said, 'Lord! It is indeed my fortune that a great soul like you has come seeking the friendship of a monkey like me. Here I extend my hand of friendship.' Then Rama accepted Sugriva's hand, and embracing him, honored that pure friendship. Then Hanuman brought strong sami branches, kindled a fire, and worshipped it with flowers. Rama and Sugriva, holding each other's hands, circumambulated the fire and became friends with fire as witness. Hanuman arranged suitable seats for Rama and Lakshmana and made them sit.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Hanuman, Lakshmana, Rishyamuka, Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sugriva and others show the bundle of Sita's jewels to Rama and Lakshmana?

**Answer:** Sugriva consoled Sri Rama, saying, 'O mighty-armed one! You will soon be free from the grief of separation from your wife. O Rama! One day I saw a cruel rakshasa carrying away a woman. In my opinion, she might be Sita. Because she was crying loudly with a choked voice, 'Rama! Rama! Lakshmana!', and seeing me, she dropped a bundle tied in her garment. At that time, I was on the mountain with my four ministers. Later, I took that bundle of jewels and kept it safely.' Then Sugriva went into a mountain cave, brought the hidden bundle of jewels, and placed it before Sri Rama. When Sri Rama tried to open that sacred bundle, his eyes filled with tears, and he appeared dim and unclear like the moon covered by frost. Rama lamented, 'Alas! My beloved!' and losing courage, fell to the ground. After some time, he regained composure, pressed the ornaments to his heart, and sighed like a snake hissing in an anthill. Then Sri Rama looked at Saumitri (Lakshmana) and wept for a long time. Then Rama asked Lakshmana to look at the ornaments. With a sorrowful face, Lakshmana looked at the ornaments and said, 'Brother! I do not recognize these armlets and earrings, but because I daily bow to our elder sister-in-law's feet, I recognize these anklets as hers.' Thus, seeing the jewels shown by Sugriva, Rama and Lakshmana confirmed that they belonged to Sita.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana

### Chapter 48: Forty-Eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 7-12
- Source PDF pages: 120, 121, 122, 123
- Printed page numbers: 124, 125, 126, 127
- Key entities: Sugriva, Rama, Vali, Hanuman, Angada, Tara, Jambavan, Nila, Nala, Indra
- Places: Rishyamuka, Kishkindha

**Summary:** Sugriva narrates his story to Rama, describing Vali's persecution and his own survival with the help of Hanuman and others. He explains Vali's valor, the curse of sage Matanga, and the first battle between Vali and Sugriva where Rama hesitated to shoot Vali due to their resemblance.

#### Q1

**Question:** Sugriva, while telling his story to Sri Rama, said that he has survived till now the torments inflicted by his brother Vali due to whose support?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman and others
- 2. Angada and others
- 3. Tara
- 4. Jambavan and others

**Correct answer:** Hanuman and others

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Vali, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** Sugriva, while telling his story to Sri Rama, said that the father of Vali and Sugriva is who?

**Options:**
- 1. Kesari
- 2. Nila
- 3. Riksharajas
- 4. Nala

**Correct answer:** Riksharajas

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Vali

#### Q3

**Question:** Sugriva tells Rama: 'Rama! An old enemy of my brother Vali, a demon, challenged us to a fight at midnight. We both went. Seeing us, that demon ran far and entered a mountain cave.' Who was that demon who entered the cave?

**Answer:** Mayavi

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Vali

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sugriva describe his brother's valor to Sri Rama?

**Answer:** O descendant of Raghu! My brother Vali is greatly valorous. Once, a demon named Dundubhi, assuming the form of a buffalo, came to fight Vali. To face that mighty demon, Vali, born from a part of Indra, wore the garland given by Indra. Whoever wears that garland gains the strength of the opponent. Remembering this, Vali fought Dundubhi. The battle was fierce, and Vali killed Dundubhi. When Vali threw the corpse, drops of blood from Dundubhi's mouth fell on sage Matanga's hermitage. Seeing the blood stains on himself, sage Matanga learned the matter and cursed: 'Vali, who has defiled this hermitage with blood stains, shall not live in this Rishyamuka forest. If he does, death is certain. Not only Vali, but his followers must leave this area within a day. If not, they will turn into stone for thousands of years.' Therefore, from then on, Vali and his followers stopped coming to this mountain region. O Rama! That day my brother threw Dundubhi's elephant-like carcass, which lies here. Observe it.' Thus Sugriva described his brother Vali's valor to Rama.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Vali, Indra, Rishyamuka

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the battle between Vali and Sugriva take place?

**Answer:** Having learned of Vali's valor through Sugriva, to instill confidence in Sugriva, Rama strung his bow and shot a sharp arrow, felling seven crooked sala trees. Seeing that, Sugriva was amazed at Rama's prowess and archery skill and bowed at Rama's feet. He said, 'Lord! No one can stand against you in battle. Therefore, kill Vali now.' Then Rama said, 'Sugriva! Now go to Kishkindha and challenge Vali, who torments you, to battle.' According to Rama's words, Sugriva stood outside Kishkindha city, roared terribly, and challenged Vali to the battlefield. Rama stood hidden behind dense bushes in the forest. The mighty Vali, hearing his brother Sugriva's roar, came out of the city in anger and haste. Then the two of them struck each other in the battlefield with thunderbolt-like palm blows and diamond-like fist punches. Then Rama, the bow-bearer, seeing those two heroes who resembled each other like the Ashvini deities, could not distinguish Sugriva from Vali and did not shoot the fatal arrow. Sugriva, severely beaten by Vali, and not seeing his protector Raghava, ran towards Rishyamuka mountain. Thus the battle between Vali and Sugriva took place.

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Rama, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka

### Chapter 49: Forty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 13-18
- Source PDF pages: 123, 124, 125
- Printed page numbers: 127, 128, 129
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Vali, Tara, Nila, Angada
- Places: Kishkindha, Ganga

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana help Sugriva in his battle against Vali. Rama shoots Vali from hiding, and Vali falls. Vali rebukes Rama for his unfair attack, and Rama justifies his action based on dharma and the Ikshvaku kings' authority over all beings in Jambudvipa.

#### Q1

**Question:** Since Vali and Sugriva looked alike, what did Lakshmana adorn Sugriva with, on Rama's suggestion, to identify him?

**Options:**
- 1. Helmet
- 2. Tying a waistband
- 3. Armlets
- 4. A garland of flowers around the neck

**Correct answer:** A garland of flowers around the neck

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** When Sugriva went to Kishkindha a second time, roared, and challenged Vali to battle, who tried to stop Vali from going to war?

**Options:**
- 1. Ruma
- 2. Tara
- 3. Nila
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Tara

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Kishkindha, Vali, Tara

#### Q3

**Question:** While Vali and Sugriva were fighting, from where did Rama shoot Vali with an arrow?

**Answer:** From behind a tree

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Vali, fallen on the battlefield, rebuke Rama?

**Answer:** While Vali and Sugriva were fighting fiercely, gradually Sugriva's strength began to wane. Noticing this, Rama released an arrow like a venomous serpent. It struck Vali's chest. Due to its force, Vali fell to the ground. Vali's body was drenched with blood flowing from him. Vali lay unconscious. Then Vali opened his eyes and looked straight. Rama and Lakshmana approached him with affection. Then Vali saw the mighty Rama and Lakshmana. Then he said humbly to Rama: 'O Lord! You are the son of a great king. You have learned all the scriptures of dharma. You were born in an excellent lineage. You are truthful and valiant. Yet, while I was fighting with someone else, why did you strike my chest? I came to war even though Tara forbade me, believing you to be of noble lineage. I have never seen you before. You have suffered no harm from me. Therefore, I fully trusted that you, a righteous one, would not strike me while I was fighting with others. But your mind seems to have gone astray. I have never done any harm to your country or to you. Why do you seek to kill me, who is innocent? I am a monkey living in the forest, eating fruits and roots. I have never fought against you. My bones, skin, and flesh are of no use to you. I could not imagine that you would show your prowess against innocent ones like me. If you think this act of yours is proper, give me an answer.' Thus Vali, wounded and thirsty, with dry mouth, kept looking at Rama.

**Key entities:** Vali, Rama, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Tara

#### Q5

**Question:** What did Rama reply to Vali's rebuke?

**Answer:** After Vali, struck by Rama's arrow, rebuked the best of the Raghus, he looked like a sun without splendor. Then Rama said: 'O Vali! Not knowing dharma, artha, kama, and worldly customs, you are blaming me out of ignorance. This land with mountains, forests, and groves is part of Jambudvipa. All of it is under the control of the Ikshvaku lords. We, the princes of that lineage, have full authority to restrain or favor the animals, birds, and humans here. We certainly punish those who deviate from the path of dharma. You are completely selfish and addicted to pleasures. Abandoning the royal dharma, you have engaged in adharma. An elder brother, father, and teacher who imparts knowledge—these three are equal to a father. You have cast such dharma into the Ganges. Your younger brother's wife Ruma is like a daughter-in-law to you. A daughter-in-law is like a daughter. While your brother is alive, you, overcome by lust, committed a sinful act with Ruma, who is like a daughter. Therefore, I had to pronounce the death sentence upon you. Your brother Sugriva was ready to help me. I promised to restore his wife and kingdom to him at that time. Fulfilling that is my dharma, isn't it? Hence, I had to impose the appropriate punishment on you. You can understand this well. Kings, while hunting, set traps, spread nets, and shoot from hiding behind trees. None of these are adharma. Therefore, what I did is also in accordance with dharma.' Thus Rama explained to Vali.

**Key entities:** Rama, Vali, Ganga, Sugriva

### Chapter 50: Fiftieth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 19-24
- Source PDF pages: 125, 126, 127, 128
- Printed page numbers: 129, 130, 131, 132
- Key entities: Tara, Vali, Rama, Angada, Sugriva, Hanuman
- Places: Kishkindha

**Summary:** Tara, learning that Vali has fallen in battle from Rama's arrow, comes to the battlefield with Angada and laments over Vali's unconscious body. Sugriva is moved to sorrow. Hanuman tries to console Tara. Vali, in his dying moments, calls Sugriva, entrusts Angada to him, and gives him a divine golden necklace. Vali advises Sugriva to rule the kingdom, care for Angada, heed Tara's counsel, and faithfully execute Rama's mission. He then dies. Rama consoles both Sugriva and Tara, urging them to accept fate and look forward to Angada's future as crown prince.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Tara, having learned that Vali had fallen in the battlefield from Rama's arrow, came to the battlefield with Angada and saw Vali lying unconscious, she fell to the ground with a heartbroken lamentation. What was Sugriva's mental state upon seeing this?

**Options:**
- 1. He rejoiced
- 2. He became sorrowful
- 3. He burned with enmity
- 4. He laughed to himself

**Correct answer:** He became sorrowful

**Key entities:** Tara, Vali, Rama, Angada, Sugriva

#### Q2

**Question:** While Tara was weeping over her husband Vali, who lay like a tree cut at the root, who tried to console her?

**Options:**
- 1. Sugriva
- 2. Ruma
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Tara, Vali, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** Vali, in his dying state, breathing heavily, called Sugriva, entrusted Angada to him, and said, 'Son Sugriva! Take this while I am still alive.' What did he give?

**Answer:** A divine golden necklace

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Angada

#### Q4

**Question:** What were the last words Vali spoke to Sugriva?

**Answer:** Vali, with his last breath, looked around and called Sugriva close. He said, 'Brother! Do not consider me guilty for taking your wife and driving you out of Kishkindha. This is all the play of fate. I did it out of pride and ignorance. Destiny did not write that we brothers should live together happily. So we acted contrary to that. I am about to leave this body and go to the other world. Therefore, accept this monkey kingdom. Sugriva! Listen to my words in this final hour. Be crowned king of this kingdom. Brother! Consider my son Angada, who is dear as my life, as your own son from now on; embrace and protect him. Brother! My wife Tara is very perceptive; she can foresee dangers and give advice. Whatever Tara says, follow her words without doubt. Brother! Carry out Rama's mission without any hesitation. If you do not, the arrow that killed me will be waiting to punish you. Sugriva! While I am still alive, wear this divine golden necklace. Otherwise, after my death, its invincible power will be lost.' Hearing Vali's words, Sugriva's enmity vanished and he did as his brother said. Then Vali told Angada, 'Son! Behave as your uncle has said,' and gave up his life.

**Key entities:** Vali, Sugriva, Kishkindha, Angada, Tara, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Rama console Tara and Sugriva?

**Answer:** Seeing Tara immersed in sorrow, shedding continuous tears, Sugriva was moved. He came to Rama and said, 'Lord! You have fulfilled your promise. I have obtained the kingdom. But I have no interest in royal pleasures; indeed, I have become averse to life itself.' Rama consoled Sugriva. Then Rama noticed Tara looking at him repeatedly. To remove her grief, the Lord looked at her with compassion. When Rama approached her, the chief ministers helped her sit up. She thought, 'He who killed my husband with a single arrow,' and looked at Rama with the intention of speaking harsh words. But seeing his divine and auspicious form, her intense anger subsided. She said, 'O Rama! You are beyond time and place. You have incarnated to protect dharma. Therefore, kill me with the same arrow that killed my husband. I will go to his side. A wife is half the body of her husband. Without me, my husband cannot be happy even in heaven. Half of my body has gone with that arrow. Now grant release to this remaining half.' As she spoke thus, Rama consoled her, saying, 'O heroic wife! Do not give in to despair. No one can escape fate. Your son Angada will soon become crown prince. Thus you will attain happiness.' Thus Rama wisely consoled Tara.

**Key entities:** Rama, Tara, Sugriva, Angada

### Chapter 51: Fifty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 25-29
- Source PDF pages: 128, 129, 130
- Printed page numbers: 132, 133, 134
- Key entities: Vali, Sugriva, Tara, Angada, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Hanuman, Nila
- Places: Kishkindha

**Summary:** After Vali's death, Sugriva, Tara, and Angada mourn. Rama and Lakshmana console them and advise performing funeral rites. Rama then orders Sugriva's coronation as king of Kishkindha. Sugriva is crowned, and Rama tells him to spend the rainy season on Prashravana Hill and prepare for war. Rama and Lakshmana reside on Prashravana Hill, enduring the rains while Rama pines for Sita. At the onset of autumn, Hanuman reminds Sugriva of his promise to Rama, urging him to begin the search for Sita. Sugriva then orders Nila to assemble the monkey army.

#### Q1

**Question:** While Sugriva, Tara, and Angada were grieving for Vali's death, Rama and Lakshmana consoled them, saying that no matter how much you lament for the dead Vali, his soul will not find peace. Therefore, what kind of rites did he ask to perform for that corpse?

**Options:**
- 1. Perform cremation rites
- 2. Bury it in the ground
- 3. Leave this corpse and go
- 4. Throw it as food for wild animals

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Tara, Angada, Vali, Rama, Lakshmana, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** After performing the last rites for Vali, whom did Sri Rama order to be crowned as king of Kishkindha?

**Options:**
- 1. Angada
- 2. Tara
- 3. Sugriva
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Tara

**Key entities:** Vali, Rama, Kishkindha, Tara

#### Q3

**Question:** After the coronation, Rama said to Sugriva, 'Friend! This is the rainy season starting from the month of Shravana for four months. It is not a suitable time for war. Therefore, in the meantime, you gather the army. During this time, where did Rama say they would reside?

**Answer:** Nila

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Nila

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama and Lakshmana spend their time on Prashravana Hill?

**Answer:** After Sugriva became lord of the monkeys, he came to Sri Rama, took his blessings, and left. Then Rama and Lakshmana reached Prashravana Hill. On that hill, along with wild animals, bears, monkeys, langurs, and wild cats roamed. There, bushes and creepers spread widely, and great trees grew lushly. Pure water reservoirs were abundant. Along with Lakshmana, Sri Rama decided to reside in a spacious cave on the hilltop and began to stay there. Then Rama said, 'Brother! We told Sugriva that we would start the search for Sita in autumn. We have to stay here until the rainy season ends. The sounds of musical instruments from the monkeys dancing with great joy are heard. Sugriva has obtained kingship. He has his wife. He is happy with relatives and wealth.' Thinking thus, Rama and Lakshmana tried to live happily on Prashravana Hill with the fruits and flowers available there. But because Rama's wife Sita was abducted and far away, remembering her, these comforts and beauties could not give him any happiness. Seeing his brother suffering thus, Lakshmana was distressed. In that state, Saumitri tried to console his brother. 'Brother! Suppressing anger and pain, let us wait until autumn. Let us endure these four months until the rainy season ends, not let our enthusiasm diminish, and both of us reside in this forest.' Thus both of them spent time on that Prashravana Hill.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** At the onset of autumn, how did Hanuman suggest to Sugriva regarding Rama's task?

**Answer:** Observing the end of the rainy season and the onset of autumn, Hanuman realized that this was the right time for the search for Sita. He immediately went to Sugriva and said, 'Lord! You have obtained kingship. Fame and prestige have come. According to the promise given to your friend, you must accomplish their task. For those who act righteously by providing timely help to friends, kingdom, fame, and valor increase. Otherwise, those who delay and neglect will face adverse results. Lord! According to the promise you made, you must fulfill Sri Rama's task. Lord! Sri Rama is our supreme friend. It is only by his grace that we are enjoying these pleasures. Therefore, you should immediately try to repay him. Order the monkey chiefs to search for Sita.' Hearing these timely and appropriate gentle words from Hanuman, the valiant Sugriva ordered a commander named Nila to assemble the entire monkey army from all directions.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sugriva, Rama, Sita, Nila

### Chapter 52: Fifty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 30-35
- Source PDF pages: 130, 131, 132, 133
- Printed page numbers: 134, 135, 136, 137
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Sita, Tara, Angada, Hanuman, Nila, Ravana
- Places: Kishkindha, Lanka

**Summary:** Rama sends Lakshmana to remind Sugriva of his promise to search for Sita. Lakshmana enters Kishkindha, and Tara pacifies his anger. Lakshmana rebukes Sugriva for his negligence, and Tara explains Sugriva's preparations for the search.

#### Q1

**Question:** With the rainy season over and autumn beginning, a favorable environment for searching for Sita has arisen, but Sugriva is not making efforts in that direction. Rama said, 'Lakshmana, go and remind him.' In what manner did Rama instruct Lakshmana to behave there?

**Options:**
- 1. Speak harshly
- 2. Speak gently
- 3. Beg
- 4. Speak threateningly

**Correct answer:** Speak gently

**Key entities:** Sita, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** Who informed Sugriva that Lakshmana had arrived at the entrance of Kishkindha as per Rama's suggestion?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Tara
- 3. Nila
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Lakshmana, Kishkindha, Rama, Angada

#### Q3

**Question:** As per Sugriva's order, Angada brought Lakshmana to Sugriva's inner palace in Kishkindha. Who recognized the intensity of anger on Lakshmana's face and tried to pacify him?

**Answer:** Tara

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Angada, Lakshmana, Kishkindha, Tara

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Lakshmana rebuke Sugriva after entering Sugriva's palace?

**Answer:** Upon entering the inner palace, Lakshmana saw Tara. She spoke to him, saying, 'O prince, you are greatly valorous. What is the use of being angry with a weak person? Moreover, you are peace personified. I know the valor of Lord Rama. O Lakshmana, Sugriva, the lord of the monkeys, is like a brother to you. Therefore, forgive him with compassion. Though Sugriva is now addicted to pleasures, he has already given appropriate orders to accomplish your task.' Saying thus, Tara led Lakshmana to Sugriva. There, Lakshmana saw Sugriva adorned with divine garments and garlands, surrounded by beautiful women, seated on a golden throne. Seeing Lakshmana, Sugriva hurriedly rose and stood near him. Then Lakshmana said, 'O king of monkeys! One who receives help from a friend and does not reciprocate is an ingrate and deserves death; moreover, he is as good as dead among all people. Sugriva! Rama can accomplish any task effortlessly. If you forget the favor done by that lord, today his sharp arrows will send you to your brother. Remember that these pleasures you enjoy are obtained by Rama's grace.' Thus Lakshmana severely rebuked Sugriva.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Sugriva, Tara, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** Seeing Lakshmana's intensity, how did Tara pacify him?

**Answer:** Seeing Lakshmana rebuking Sugriva severely, Tara said, 'O brother of Rama! Sugriva is your friend, the king of monkeys. It is not righteous for a great soul like you to utter such harsh words. This Sugriva is not an ingrate, not a deceiver, not a liar, nor crooked. Rama has done a task impossible for others on the battlefield. Sugriva has not forgotten that. It is because of Lord Rama that Sugriva has obtained this monkey kingdom and all pleasures. O lord! Food, sleep, fear, and marital pleasure are natural bodily functions of living beings. Without knowing the true facts, it is not righteous to act hastily like an ordinary person and become angry. O Lakshmana! This lord of monkeys can surely kill Ravana in battle and deliver Sita to Rama. But Sugriva alone cannot confront Ravana, who is surrounded by countless demon warriors in Lanka. Therefore, to gather countless monkey warriors to help him in battle, Sugriva has already sent many monkey chiefs in all directions. He is waiting for their arrival and has not moved from this city. O Saumitri! Crores of monkey, bear, and langur warriors should have already arrived here. Please have mercy on us and give up your anger. The redness in your eyes is causing us anxiety.' Thus Tara pacified Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Tara, Sugriva, Rama, Ravana, Sita, Lanka

### Chapter 53: Fifty-third Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 36-41
- Source PDF pages: 133, 134, 135
- Printed page numbers: 137, 138, 139
- Key entities: Lakshmana, Tara, Sugriva, Rama, Sita, Ravana, Angada, Hanuman, Nila, Sushena, Jambavan
- Places: Kishkindha, Lanka

**Summary:** Lakshmana calms down after Tara's words and tells Sugriva to meet Rama. Sugriva, delighted, sends messengers to hasten the arrival of monkey warriors from all directions. He then goes with Lakshmana to meet Rama. Rama advises Sugriva on the next steps: first ascertain Sita's whereabouts and Ravana's location. Sugriva dispatches search parties to the four directions, appointing leaders for each. For the south, he sends Angada as leader with many prominent monkeys, including Hanuman, and gives detailed instructions about the terrain and a one-month deadline.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Tara and Sugriva's words, Lakshmana became calm and happy, and told Sugriva to go see Rama. Sugriva, delighted, had already sent some to bring the monkey warriors from the four corners of the earth quickly to Kishkindha. Whom did he order to send others to hurry them and bring them here?

**Options:**
- 1. Tara
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Angada
- 4. Nila

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Tara, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Rama, Kishkindha, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** Following Lakshmana's suggestion, Sugriva set out with royal honors to meet Rama. What did Lakshmana and Sugriva ride?

**Options:**
- 1. Elephant
- 2. Horse
- 3. Palanquin
- 4. Chariot

**Correct answer:** Palanquin

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Sugriva, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** While Rama was happily speaking with Sugriva who came to see him, monkeys, bears, and heroes from the four directions arrived in crores. Among them was Tara's father. What is his name?

**Answer:** Sushena

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Tara, Sushena

#### Q4

**Question:** When Sugriva showed his entire army to Rama, how did Rama advise Sugriva about the duty to be performed?

**Answer:** While Rama and Sugriva were talking on Prashravana mountain, an immense monkey army arrived and stationed themselves in various areas. Sugriva realized this and said to Rama: 'Lord! Powerful monkey chiefs have come and are standing in suitable places. They are all immensely strong like rutting elephants, can change form at will, and are equal to demons. This entire army is yours and under your control. Command them as you wish.' Hearing this, Rama looked at Sugriva with affection and said: 'O wise one! Until now, we need to know whether Sita is alive or not, and the place where Ravana is. First, we must learn Sita's whereabouts and Ravana's location. Then we will discuss and decide the proper course of action. O monkey king! The search for Sita is not possible by me or Lakshmana. You are the one who can accomplish this task. Its success lies in your hands. There is no doubt about it. So think appropriately and command your followers.' After Rama spoke thus wisely, Sugriva called his army chief Vinata and ordered him to go east with a suitable army, search for Rama's wife Sita, and return within a month. Thus Sugriva sent capable leaders to all four directions for the search of Sita.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Sita, Ravana, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** For the search of Sita, whom did Sugriva send to the south, in what manner, and with what instructions?

**Answer:** For the search of Sita, Sugriva sent thoroughly tested monkeys to the southern direction. Among them were Nila, Hanuman, Jambavan, Suhotra, Sharari, Sharagulma, Gaja, Gavaksha, Gavaya, Sushena, Rishabha, Mainda, Dvivida, Vijaya, Gandhamadana, Ulkamukha, Asanga, and other monkey heroes. He appointed Angada as their leader and sent them south. In that direction, notably, Ravana-ruled Lanka is located. Sugriva described in detail some places that are extremely difficult to access, as well as the rivers, mountains, cities, and regions they would encounter. He set a deadline of one month and said: 'Whoever finds Sita and returns within this deadline will be most dear to me and will enjoy pleasures equal to mine. Even if he has many faults, he will be my most beloved and dear as life itself. Therefore, O friends! You possess unparalleled strength and valor. Now begin the effort suitable for Rama's task.' Thus Sugriva spoke to Angada and others and sent them to the south.

**Key entities:** Sita, Sugriva, Nila, Hanuman, Jambavan, Sushena, Angada, Ravana, Lanka, Rama

### Chapter 54: Fifty-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 42-47
- Source PDF pages: 135, 136, 137, 138
- Printed page numbers: 139, 140, 141, 142
- Key entities: Sugriva, Sita, Rama, Vali, Angada, Hanuman, Sushena, Nala, Jambavan
- Places: Lanka, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka

**Summary:** Sugriva dispatches monkey warriors in all directions to search for Sita, describing the geographical features of each direction. He gives a month's deadline and promises great rewards for success. Rama asks Sugriva how he knows the entire earth, and Sugriva narrates his past wanderings while fleeing from Vali. The monkey troops return unsuccessful except for the southern group led by Angada, which includes Hanuman, who is expected to find Sita in Lanka.

#### Q1

**Question:** Sugriva, describing the mountains, rivers, cities, and countries in the western direction for the search of Sita, under whose leadership did he send the monkey warriors?

**Options:**
- 1. Shatavali
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Nala
- 4. Sushena

**Correct answer:** Sushena

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Sita, Sushena

#### Q2

**Question:** To search for Rama's wife Sita, Sugriva described all the mountains, rivers, forests, forts, countries, and cities in the northern direction and made whom the leader to send the monkey warriors?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Gavaya
- 3. Shatavali
- 4. Vijaya

**Correct answer:** Shatavali

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Sugriva

#### Q3

**Question:** Among the warriors going to the southern direction, Rama called Hanuman and gave him which object as his token?

**Answer:** Ring (Anguleeyakam)

**Key entities:** Rama, Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** When Rama asked Sugriva, 'How do you know all these details of the earth?', how did Sugriva answer the lord?

**Answer:** After the monkey warriors left in all directions as per Sugriva's command, Rama asked Sugriva, 'How do you know all this earth?' Then the monkey king said, 'O Lord! My elder brother Vali chased a demon named Dundubhi, who had the form of a buffalo, and entered a cave. I waited outside the cave for my brother. After a long time, my brother did not come out. Then blood started flowing from the cave entrance. Fearing it was my brother's blood and that the demon might come out and kill me, I closed the cave entrance with a large boulder, gave up hope of my brother's life, thought the demon also died in the cave, and returned to Kishkindha. Immediately, the citizens of Kishkindha made me king. Meanwhile, my brother, who had killed Dundubhi, returned to Kishkindha. Seeing Vali, I fearfully and respectfully handed over the kingdom to him. But Vali became angry and tried to kill me. Then I fled with my ministers. Thus I first went east. My brother did not leave me; he kept chasing me. In this way, I went in all directions. Finally, I went to Rishyamuka mountain, and knowing that Vali would not come due to a curse, I started living there. O best of men! Thus I have traveled and seen the entire earth in all directions.' Thus Sugriva told Lord Ramachandra.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Vali, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka

#### Q5

**Question:** Which monkey chiefs returned after searching for Sita as per Sugriva's command? What information did they convey to Sugriva?

**Answer:** All the monkey troops went to various places as per Sugriva's command to search for Sita. They thoroughly searched lakes, riverbanks, bowers, forests full of trees and creepers, desert places where no grass grew, places difficult to cross due to rivers, hills, valleys, cities, villages, mountains, and dense forests. Thus they searched all day, gathered at designated places at night, ate fruits available there to satisfy their hunger, and searched for Mother Janaki for a month. Not finding any trace of her, they returned disappointed to Prashravana hill and met the monkey king Sugriva. Then they all said, 'O monkey king! As you commanded, we searched every inch in the directions we went, even in inaccessible places. But our efforts did not bear fruit. We could not find any trace of Mother Sita. O great king! Hanuman, who went south under the leadership of Angada, will surely find Sita's trace. Because in that direction lies the city of Lanka. Therefore, that great soul will bring us the good news of Mother's whereabouts.' Thus the monkey warriors told Sugriva.

**Key entities:** Sita, Sugriva, Hanuman, Angada, Lanka

### Chapter 55: Fifty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 48-53
- Source PDF pages: 138, 139, 140
- Printed page numbers: 142, 143, 144
- Key entities: Angada, Sita, Hanuman, Simhika, Brahma, Rama, Dasharatha, Ravana, Sugriva
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** The monkey warriors led by Angada begin their search for Sita from the Vindhya mountain region. Exhausted and thirsty, they enter a cave called Rkshabila, where they meet the ascetic Svayamprabha. She explains that the cave was created by the demon architect Maya for his pleasure with the apsara Hema. After they refresh themselves, Svayamprabha uses her ascetic power to transport them to the southern seashore.

#### Q1

**Question:** From which mountain region did the monkey warriors, led by Angada, first begin their search for Sita in the southern direction?

**Options:**
- 1. From the Vindhya mountain region
- 2. From the Gandhamadana region
- 3. From the Himalayan region
- 4. From the Satpura mountain

**Correct answer:** From the Vindhya mountain region

**Key entities:** Angada, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** While searching for Sita, Hanuman and other prominent monkeys became very thirsty and tired, and entered a cave called Rkshabila. There they saw a radiant yogini. What is her name?

**Options:**
- 1. Sabari
- 2. Vedavati
- 3. Svayamprabha
- 4. Simhika

**Correct answer:** Svayamprabha

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** When Maruti, seeing the splendor in Rkshabila, asked the ascetic there, 'Mother! Who created this forest?', what did she answer?

**Answer:** The demon architect Maya

**Key entities:** Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** In Rkshabila, how did the ascetic respond to Hanuman's doubts, and how did Hanuman reply to her questions?

**Answer:** Led by Angada, the monkey warriors searching for Sita became hungry and thirsty. Seeing birds with wet wings emerging from a cave, they thought water might be inside and entered the difficult cave with patience. After some distance, they saw a vast place with buildings, sweet roots and fruits, and pure water. There, an ascetic wearing deerskin was present. Hanuman humbly asked, 'Mother, who are you? Whose is this radiant place? We entered this cave unable to bear hunger and thirst.' The ascetic replied, 'Long ago, the demon architect Maya performed penance to Brahma here. Later, by the grace of the Grandfather, he acquired the science of architecture. He created this place for his enjoyment and became attached to the apsara Hema. Hema entrusted me with protecting these forests. Without hesitation, partake of this food and water.' Then the monkeys joyfully satisfied their hunger and thirst. Later, the ascetic revealed her name as Svayamprabha and asked Hanuman about their purpose. Maruti said, 'Mother! Sri Rama, the eldest son of Dasaratha who ruled Ayodhya, was in exile when the demon Ravana abducted his wife Sita. We have come here searching for Sita.' Thus, Svayamprabha and Hanuman exchanged their stories.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Angada, Sita, Brahma, Rama, Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did all the monkey warriors reach the seashore from Rkshabila?

**Answer:** Hanuman said to the ascetic Svayamprabha, 'O righteous lady! We all seek refuge in you. The deadline set by our king Sugriva has ended in this cave. We have a great task to accomplish, but circumstances are unfavorable. We are trapped here.' Hearing Hanuman's words, Svayamprabha said, 'O monkeys! It is difficult for those who enter this cave to come out alive. But by the power of my penance performed with discipline, I will deliver you from this cave. All of you close your eyes.' Then they all covered their eyes with both hands. When they opened their eyes again, they were all near the southern seashore. Then Svayamprabha said, 'May you be blessed! I am going to my abode,' and departed. All the prominent monkeys, hearing the roar of the ocean, rested in the shade of great trees there.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sugriva

### Chapter 56: Fifty-sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 53-57
- Source PDF pages: 140, 141, 142, 143
- Printed page numbers: 144, 145, 146, 147
- Key entities: Angada, Sugriva, Hanuman, Sampati, Jatayu, Rama, Sita, Tara, Jambavan, Vali, Dasharatha, Lakshmana, Ravana
- Places: Ayodhya, Dandaka Forest, Rishyamuka, Kishkindha

**Summary:** The monkeys, having emerged from the cave, sit despondently on the seashore. Angada suggests they perform prayopavesha (fast unto death) rather than face Sugriva empty-handed. Hanuman tries to dissuade him. Nearby, the vulture king Sampati hears Angada mention Jatayu's death and asks for details. Angada narrates the story of Rama, Sita's abduction, Jatayu's death, and their search for Sita.

#### Q1

**Question:** One of those sitting sorrowfully on the seashore said, 'If we go before Sugriva empty-handed without finding Sita's trace, he will sentence us to death. Rather than going there and dying, it is better for us to perform prayopavesha here.' Who said this?

**Options:**
- 1. Tara
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Angada
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Sita, Angada

#### Q2

**Question:** To Angada, who was contemplating prayopavesha, someone said, 'O young prince! Come with us, complete the search for Sita, and even if the deadline is exceeded, if we go to the king, he will welcome us. Therefore, let us think only about the search for Sita.' Who said this?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Suhotra
- 3. Gavaya
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Angada, Sita, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** Despite Maruti trying in many ways, Angada did not turn his mind away from prayopavesha. While he was remembering Rama and recounting his forest exile, Jatayu's death, and Sita's abduction, which bird nearby asked for details about Jatayu's death?

**Answer:** Sampati

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Angada, Rama, Jatayu, Sita, Sampati

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sampati learn the news of his younger brother's death?

**Answer:** Sampati, the vulture king, was sitting on a mountain peak near the monkeys who were preparing for prayopavesha. He thought that if all the monkeys died, he could eat them one by one. Meanwhile, Angada spoke about Jatayu's death, saying that Jatayu fought the demon to protect Sita and died. Hearing this, Sampati loudly asked who was speaking about his brother Jatayu's death and requested the monkeys to lower him from the peak and tell him the details.

**Key entities:** Sampati, Angada, Jatayu, Sita

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Angada explain the news of Jatayu's death and their search for Sita to Sampati?

**Answer:** At Sampati's request, Angada went to him and said, 'O king of birds! In the past, there was a monkey king named Rksharajas who had two sons, Vali and Sugriva. I am Angada, son of Vali. The eldest son of King Dasaratha of Ayodhya, Sri Rama, came to the forest with his wife Sita and brother Lakshmana to fulfill his father's word. While living in Dandaka forest, they became friends with Jatayu, who was a friend of Dasaratha. When the demon Ravana tried to abduct Sita in the absence of Rama and Lakshmana, Jatayu intervened and was killed by Ravana. Rama and Lakshmana, searching for Sita, befriended Sugriva on Rishyamuka mountain. Sugriva told Rama of the injustice done by my father Vali, and Rama killed Vali, making Sugriva king of Kishkindha. Because of Rama's great favor to Sugriva, we, obeying our king Sugriva's command, are searching for Sita and have come here.' Thus Angada explained the news of Jatayu's death and the reason for their arrival.

**Key entities:** Angada, Jatayu, Sita, Sampati, Vali, Sugriva, Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Rama, Lakshmana, Dandaka Forest, Ravana, Rishyamuka, Kishkindha

### Chapter 57: Fifty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 58-62
- Source PDF pages: 143, 144, 145
- Printed page numbers: 147, 148, 149
- Key entities: Sampati, Sita, Ravana, Jatayu, Rama, Angada, Vayu, Dasharatha, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Sampati tells the monkeys about Sita's abduction by Ravana, describes Lanka's distance, recounts his own story of losing his wings while protecting Jatayu, and relates the prophecy of sage Nishakara that his wings will regrow after he informs the monkeys about Sita.

#### Q1

**Question:** Sampati said, 'I will cooperate in Rama's work. O monkeys! I saw Ravana abducting a beautiful woman. Ravana's residence is the city of Lanka. How far did Sampati say Lanka is from here?'

**Options:**
- 1. 70 yojanas
- 2. 90 yojanas
- 3. 100 yojanas
- 4. 80 yojanas

**Correct answer:** 100 yojanas

**Key entities:** Sampati, Rama, Ravana, Lanka

#### Q2

**Question:** Sampati, while narrating the abduction of Sita, said that one day in those times, when his son had gone in search of food, he saw a wicked man abducting a woman. What is the name of Sampati's son?

**Options:**
- 1. Anuru
- 2. Suparshva
- 3. Vainateya
- 4. Jatayu

**Correct answer:** Suparshva

**Key entities:** Sampati, Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** Sampati, while telling Angada and other monkeys about Sita, said, 'Once, my wings were burnt by the sun's heat, and I fell in the Vindhya mountain region. There I took refuge with a great sage who comforted me.' What is the name of that sage?

**Answer:** Nishakara Maharshi

**Key entities:** Sampati, Angada, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sampati explain to sage Nishakara the reason for his wings being burnt?

**Answer:** Sampati, whose wings were scorched by the sun's heat, went to the Vindhya mountain region and met the great sage Nishakara. The sage asked, 'O Sampati! You two are brothers and can assume any form at will. I have seen you before. How did this happen to you, who are equal to Vayu?' Then Sampati replied, 'O sage! We two brothers, proud of our strength, wanting to test our prowess, competed and flew into the sky. As we flew, looking down, the cities, mountains, rivers, and oceans appeared very small. Then our bodies sweated from the sun's heat. We were afraid. Our senses and mind lost control. Directions became unclear. Then Jatayu, without telling me, began to fall down. Seeing the situation, to support my brother, I came near him and covered Jatayu with my wings. Thus he was protected from the hot rays of the sun, but my wings were burnt and I fell to the ground. I thought Jatayu would have fallen in the Dandaka forest. I fell in this Vindhya mountain region. My brother became distant.' Thus Sampati narrated his story to sage Nishakara.

**Key entities:** Sampati, Vayu, Jatayu, Dandaka Forest

#### Q5

**Question:** How did sage Nishakara console Sampati?

**Answer:** Seeing Sampati weeping before him, sage Nishakara, with his yogic vision, said, 'O Sampati! Do not grieve. Your burnt wings will grow back. Likewise, your eyesight will be restored. Your diminished life force, strength, and valor will revive. I have foreseen with my divine vision a great event that will happen in the future. Sri Rama, the eldest son of King Dasharatha of the Ikshvaku dynasty, will come to the Dandaka forest with his wife and brother to fulfill his father's words. A demon named Ravana will abduct Rama's wife. Neither gods nor demons can do anything to Ravana. That Ravana will be slain by Sri Rama. Good will come to all creatures. Searching for Sita, monkeys will come to you. Then you should inform them about Rama's wife. Until then, do not leave this place. Wait for the right time and circumstances. As soon as you tell the monkeys about Sita, your wings will grow back. O Sampati! I wish to see Rama and Lakshmana, but my body will not last until then. So I must give up this body.' Thus Sampati told the monkey chiefs about the prophecy of sage Nishakara.

**Key entities:** Sampati, Rama, Dasharatha, Dandaka Forest, Ravana, Sita, Lakshmana

### Chapter 58: Fifty-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Kishkindha Kanda
- Sarga range: 63-67
- Source PDF pages: 145, 146, 147, 148
- Printed page numbers: 149, 150, 151, 152
- Key entities: Sampati, Angada, Jambavan, Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Nila, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Vayu, Indra
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Sampati's wings grow back as predicted by sage Nishakara, and he encourages the monkeys. The monkeys spend the night and in the morning, Angada asks who can leap the hundred-yojana ocean. Jambavan recounts Hanuman's birth and powers, motivating him to undertake the leap. Hanuman resolves to cross the ocean, expands his form, and prepares to leap from Mahendragiri.

#### Q1

**Question:** While the monkey chiefs were watching, Sampati's wings grew back. Then Sampati, looking at his wings with delight, said, 'O monkeys! As sage Nishakara said, my wings have grown. In the same way, you will also find the trace of Mother Sita.' What color were Sampati's wings that grew back?

**Options:**
- 1. White
- 2. Green
- 3. Blue
- 4. Red

**Correct answer:** Red

**Key entities:** Sampati, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** After Sampati encouraged the monkey chiefs and left, they all spent the night there, woke up in the morning, and asked, 'O monkey chiefs! Who among you can leap this hundred-yojana ocean and accomplish Rama's task? Give me your assurance.' Who asked this?

**Options:**
- 1. Angada
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Jambavan
- 4. Nila

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Sampati, Rama, Angada

#### Q3

**Question:** As part of declaring their abilities in the ocean leap, how many yojanas did Jambavan say he could go?

**Answer:** Ninety yojanas

**Key entities:** Jambavan

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Jambavan motivate Hanuman for the ocean leap?
