**Answer:** Observing the monkey army of many lakhs sunk in despair, Jambavan decided to inspire Hanuman and said, 'O Anjaneya! You are incomparable among all monkeys. You know all the scriptures. O son of Vayu! In your splendor, strength, and valor, you are in no way inferior to Sugriva or Rama and Lakshmana. O Hanuman! The foremost of apsaras, 'Punjakasthala', due to a curse, was born on earth as Anjana Devi. She became the wife of the monkey chief Kesari. Being a shape-shifter, she assumed a human form adorned with all ornaments and was sporting on a mountain peak when Vayu, captivated by her beauty and youth, embraced her. Anjana Devi was frightened by the unexpected turn. Then Vayu said, 'O beautiful one! Even though I embraced you, no blemish will come to you. Do not fear. You will give birth to a greatly valiant and intelligent being.' So saying, he left. Then your mother gave birth to you. When you, thinking the rising sun to be a fruit, went towards it, Indra stopped you. Angered by this, Vayu caused all the worlds to become still. Then all the gods, pleased, gave you many boons. Therefore, O Hanuman! Among all here, you alone are fit for the ocean leap. So, arise at once.' Thus Jambavan motivated Hanuman.

**Key entities:** Jambavan, Hanuman, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Vayu, Indra

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Hanuman become determined for the ocean leap?

**Answer:** To immediately cross the ocean of a hundred yojanas, Maruti gathered his valor within and began to increase his wondrous form. Seeing that great hero, the entire monkey army shed their sorrow and praised Hanuman. They shouted loudly and were filled with joy and wonder. Then Hanuman, pleased with the monkeys' praise, raised his tail, further augmented his strength, and grew. Then the form of that great being was wonderful. Then Anjaneya said, 'I will leap this ocean, reach Lanka, and see Mother Sita. May you all rejoice! I am confident that I can leap even thousands of yojanas.' As the splendid and mighty monkey chief Hanuman spoke, all the monkeys gazed at him with joy and wonder. Then Maruti said to Jambavan, 'This ordinary ground cannot bear my foot for leaping. Therefore, I will place my foot on Mahendragiri and leap the ocean from there.' So he climbed Mahendragiri and, with focused mind, began to think of Lanka.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Sita, Jambavan

### Chapter 59: Fifty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-5
- Source PDF pages: 148, 149, 150
- Printed page numbers: 152, 153, 154
- Key entities: Hanuman, Mainaka, Surasa, Simhika, Sita, Garuda, Brahma, Ravana, Rama
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Hanuman leaps from Mahendragiri towards Lanka. The ocean offers him rest via Mount Mainaka. The gods send Surasa to test him, and a shadow-grabber named Simhika tries to stop him. Hanuman defeats Lankini, the guardian deity of Lanka, and enters the city in a tiny form. He searches for Sita throughout Lanka but does not find her.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Hanuman set out southward from Mahendragiri, flying like Garuda, the ocean, wishing to give some rest to the son of Marut who was going for the sake of the Ikshvaku dynasty, which mountain inside him did he command to come out and provide shelter to Hanuman?

**Options:**
- 1. Vidya mountain
- 2. Sheshachala mountain
- 3. Mainaka mountain
- 4. Meru mountain

**Correct answer:** Mainaka mountain

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Garuda, Mainaka

#### Q2

**Question:** The gods, wishing to test Hanuman's strength, ordered whom to obstruct his path?

**Options:**
- 1. Diti
- 2. Atidhi
- 3. Naga-mata Surasa
- 4. Kaliya

**Correct answer:** Naga-mata Surasa

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Surasa

#### Q3

**Question:** As Hanuman was proceeding towards Lanka, a grotesque shadow-catcher in the ocean grabbed his shadow and pulled him back, trying to stop his speed. What is her name?

**Answer:** Simhika

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Simhika

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Anjaneya enter Lanka?

**Answer:** The mighty Hanuman, having leaped over the ocean impossible for others, fixed his gaze on the city of Lanka situated on Trikuta mountain. While roaming on that mountain, various trees showered flowers on him. Without any fatigue from crossing the ocean, the son of the wind wandered here and there, seeing the forests and groves, and observed the city of Lanka on the mountain. Then Hanuman thought for a moment: first I must know whether Sita is alive or not. In this Lanka guarded by extremely cruel and powerful demons, entering in this form is not advisable; it is better to reduce his form and enter at night. So he waited for some time. When darkness fell, the city of Lanka shone with the light of house lamps and moonlight, and Maruti saw it. Then the foremost of monkeys, Maruti, while entering Lanka, was seen by the guardian deity of Lanka, Lankini, who stood before him and said, 'Who are you? Why have you come to this city of Lanka? Tell the truth before you lose your life at my hands.' Seeing Lankini standing in a grotesque form, he said, 'I came to see the beautiful city of Lanka.' 'O evil-minded one! Without defeating me you cannot enter Lanka,' said Lankini and struck Maruti hard. Immediately Hanuman clenched his fist and struck her with his left fist. Struck by that blow, Lankini fell to the ground and said, 'O foremost of monkeys! As Brahma said long ago, Lanka will be destroyed by the one who strikes me.' And she gave way for Maruti to enter Lanka. Thus Maruti entered Lanka.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Sita, Brahma

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Maruti search for Sita in Lanka?

**Answer:** The greatly radiant Hanuman assumed a tiny form and, instead of entering through the main gate, jumped over the rampart and entered Lanka placing his left foot first, as if placing his left foot on the enemy's head. The foremost of monkeys proceeded along the royal road adorned with flowering trees on both sides. From the houses various sounds of musical instruments were heard. Skilled in accomplishing his master's task, Maruti looked at every house and moved forward. Thousands of demons guarded Ravana's palace, and Hanuman secretly entered Ravana's inner apartments which were in the midst of a very tight security cordon. Due to the rising of the autumn moon, darkness disappeared and people rejoiced. The night-wanderers delighted in eating meat. Men and women, having given up quarrels, reveled in the pleasures of love. Some were playing the veena strings. Others of good conduct were enjoying the comforts of bed with their husbands. The wise Hanuman examined every house in search of Sita. Though he searched many places, he could not find any trace of Sita, the righteous wife of Rama. Thus Hanuman continued searching for Sita.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Lanka, Ravana, Rama

### Chapter 60: Sixtieth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 6-11
- Source PDF pages: 150, 151, 152, 153
- Printed page numbers: 154, 155, 156, 157
- Key entities: Hanuman, Ravana, Sita, Mandodari, Brahma, Prahasta, Virupaksha, Kubera, Varuna, Vali, Indra, Rama
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Hanuman secretly enters Ravana's inner palace in search of Sita. He observes the grandeur of the palace, the guards, and the sleeping women, including Ravana. He briefly mistakes Mandodari for Sita but quickly corrects himself and continues his search.

#### Q1

**Question:** Hanuman thought that Ravana had the palaces built by whom, using the wealth of diamonds and cat's eye gems won in battles?

**Options:**
- 1. Shukracharya
- 2. Maya Brahma
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Virupaksha

**Correct answer:** Maya Brahma

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana, Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** After seeing many palaces, Hanuman saw the Pushpaka Vimana, which was like heaven on earth. With whom did Ravana fight and win to bring it?

**Options:**
- 1. Varuna
- 2. Shankara
- 3. Vali
- 4. Kubera

**Correct answer:** Kubera

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana, Kubera

#### Q3

**Question:** While searching meticulously in Ravana's great mansion for Sita, Maruti saw a woman sleeping on a special bed among some divine women sleeping near Ravana on a divine bed. For a moment, he thought she might be Sita. Who was she?

**Answer:** Mandodari

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Hanuman, Mandodari

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Hanuman search for Sita in Ravana's inner palace?

**Answer:** Searching for Sita, Hanuman entered Ravana's inner palace without being seen by anyone. That Ravana mansion was half a yojana wide and one yojana long, vast and spacious. The building was guarded by many armed rakshasas. That great palace was filled with Ravana's wives and also princesses he had forcibly brought by his valor. The wealth and splendor of Kubera, the lord of wealth, and the opulence like Indra's were established in that royal palace. There were many secret chambers there. In those houses on the Pushpaka, Maruti saw people who had become tired from drinking, eating, and sports until midnight, and were falling asleep. There, while Ravana slept, the lamps seemed to stare without blinking at his radiance. Among all the women there, some were abducted by Ravana, while others had come attracted to him. All were attracted to Ravana. But Hanuman thought that if Sita, the wife of Rama, were also happily united with her husband like these women, then it would have been well for Ravana. Thus, no matter how much Hanuman searched in Ravana's mansion, he could not find any trace of Sita.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Ravana, Kubera, Indra, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Hanuman rejoice when he mistakenly thought Sita was in Ravana's mansion? What did he think afterwards?

**Answer:** Maruti, searching very keenly for Sita in Ravana's mansion, saw a bed. It was inlaid with crystals and gems. That place was filled with various fragrant breezes and incense. Some women were holding chowries and fanning. Hanuman saw the great hero Ravana sleeping on that bed. Then Maruti, approaching Ravana, thought 'Fie! This is a wicked man who has abducted another's wife.' He saw a woman of exceptional beauty among all the sleeping women, sleeping on a specially arranged couch. Her form was charming with pure radiance. Seeing her, Maruti was overjoyed, thinking he had found Sita, and rejoiced greatly. Immediately, that great monkey began to think correctly about Sita. 'Is it possible for Sita, separated from Rama, to sleep like this? In that state, would she have any interest in food and drink? Would she think of wearing ornaments? No matter how great a man, would she allow him near her? Not only humans, are there any gods equal to Rama? Therefore, this is not Sita.' Deciding thus, Hanuman became eager to search for Sita again and began to wander here and there.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Ravana, Rama

### Chapter 61: Sixty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 12-16
- Source PDF pages: 153, 154, 155
- Printed page numbers: 157, 158, 159
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Sampati, Rama, Ravana, Jatayu, Jambavan, Vali, Viradha, Khara
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove, Rishyamuka

**Summary:** Hanuman searches Lanka but cannot find Sita. He recalls Sampati's words that Sita is in Lanka. He enters the Ashoka grove and hides in a flowering tree, waiting for Sita. He sees a woman in soiled silk, surrounded by rakshasis, and identifies her as Sita based on descriptions from Rama and the golden-bordered garment. He laments her suffering.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Hanuman searched all of Lanka including Ravana's harem but could not find Sita, he became somewhat disappointed. Nevertheless, whose words did he recall that Sita was indeed in Lanka?

**Options:**
- 1. Jatayu
- 2. Svayamprabha
- 3. Sampati
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Sampati

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Ravana, Sita, Sampati

#### Q2

**Question:** After searching all over Lanka and not finding any trace of Sita, Hanuman was distressed in various ways and finally entered a grove. What is the name of that grove?

**Options:**
- 1. Ashoka Grove
- 2. Saugandhika Grove
- 3. Chaitraratha Grove
- 4. Nandana Grove

**Correct answer:** Ashoka Grove

**Key entities:** Lanka, Sita, Hanuman, Ashoka Grove

#### Q3

**Question:** Maruti thought that if Sita were alive, she would surely come to this river with sacred waters. Waiting for the sight of Rama's wife in that grove, he hid among the dense leaves of a tree that was in full bloom and looked around. What is the name of the tree that Hanuman climbed?

**Answer:** Ashoka tree

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Hanuman recognize Sita?

**Answer:** Hanuman, seated on the Ashoka tree, waited for a glimpse of Sita, looking all around and thoroughly surveying the Ashoka grove. The grove was adorned with kalpavrikshas and creepers. Trees bearing fruit in all seasons were laden with fruits and flowers, bending under their weight. As he admired the beauty of the grove, Maruti turned his gaze and saw a woman wearing soiled garments, with a suitable form and auspicious features, seated firmly on the ground. Around her were rakshasi women. He noticed she was emaciated by fasting, dejected, and sighing repeatedly. Then Maruti reasoned within himself and began to think in various ways to identify her. She wore a single garment; though soiled, it was silk and still lustrous. With a body faded by sorrow, as if in meditation, with modesty, head bowed, grieving, she was very dejected. Based on the reasons he considered, Hanuman thought, 'This is the Sita who was abducted by the lustful Ravana.' The features of the lady he saw while passing over Rishyamuka Mountain were visible in her. All the form, beauty, and splendor that Rama had described were seen in her. Therefore, this is indeed Sita. The green garment with a golden border that was dropped on Rishyamuka Mountain when Ravana abducted Sita is the same as the one she wears. This is sufficient to firmly conclude that she is Sita. Thus Maruti recognized Sita.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Ashoka Grove, Ravana, Rishyamuka, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** Seeing Sita in distress, how did Maruti lament?

**Answer:** Seeing Sita seated on the bare ground, Hanuman thought thus: Praising in his mind Sita and Rama, who are worthy of praise by all people in the world and are endowed with good qualities, he became absorbed in meditation for a moment and, seeing Sita's dejected state, began to weep profusely. 'For this treasure of good qualities, Rama killed Vali. Not only Vali, but also Viradha, Khara, and fourteen thousand other rakshasas were destroyed for her sake. Moreover, for this great pativrata, Rama could give up even the lordship of the three worlds. She is holding on to her life with the hope that she will one day obtain her husband. Seeing her, who is worthy of enjoying divine pleasures with Rama, suffering among these rakshasi women, even my mind is disturbed. What then of the supremely compassionate Rama?' Thus the great hero Hanuman, after thoroughly considering these matters, firmly concluded 'This is Sita' and remained hidden among the leaves of that tree, grieving.

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Rama, Vali, Viradha, Khara

### Chapter 62: Sixty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 17-21
- Source PDF pages: 155, 156, 157, 158
- Printed page numbers: 159, 160, 161, 162
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Ravana, Rama, Janaka, Indra, Lakshmana
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Hanuman, hidden in a tree, observes Sita surrounded by demonesses. Ravana approaches Sita in the morning, attempts to seduce her with promises of wealth and power, but Sita rebukes him, declaring her devotion to Rama and threatening him with Rama's vengeance.

#### Q1

**Question:** Seeing Sita guarded by demonesses of various grotesque forms, Maruti rejoiced thinking 'Whatever happens, I have seen Rama's wife.' But at that time, which constellation did Sita appear to him like, surrounded by inauspicious planets?

**Options:**
- 1. Chitta
- 2. Vishakha
- 3. Swati
- 4. Rohini

**Correct answer:** Rohini

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Hanuman, perched on a branch of a tree near the tree where Sita was sitting, hidden by dense leaves and flowers. When did Ravana, lustful and accompanied by many harem women, come to the place where Sita was?

**Options:**
- 1. Noon
- 2. Morning
- 3. Evening
- 4. Midnight

**Correct answer:** Morning

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** When the demon king Ravana approached her, Sita, distressed and frightened, with folded hands, appeared to Hanuman as if praying to whom for Ravana's defeat by Rama?

**Answer:** Kuladevata (family deity)

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Hanuman, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** While Hanuman watched from amidst the leaves on the tree, in what manner did Ravana try to tempt Sita?

**Answer:** Ravana, accompanied by harem women, approached Sita and said: 'O beautiful one! Sita! You hide your face seeing me. O large-eyed one, I love you. O beloved! Accept me. O Sita, neither humans, nor demons, nor gods or gandharvas can do anything to me. You need not fear me. Forcibly abducting and enjoying other women is the very dharma of demons. Though lust is aroused in me, I will not touch you without your love. Do not fear. Trust me. Love me wholeheartedly. O auspicious one! Look at me once, and behold my wealth, splendor, and fame. Rama, wearing bark garments and exiled to the forest, can give you nothing. Rama has lost victory and wealth, is exiled to the forest, observing the vow of a sage, sleeping on the bare ground. Whether he is alive or dead is unknown. It is impossible for him to regain you from me. In my harem there are many women endowed with all virtues. If you accept me, they will all serve you. O beautiful one! Rama is in no way equal to me, nor can he be. I will give you the wealth and kingdom under my control. Accept me.' Thus Ravana tried to tempt Sita in many ways, and Hanuman saw it.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana, Sita, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sita scornfully speak to Ravana when he tried to tempt her?

**Answer:** Hearing the words of the terrifying Ravana, the distressed Sita, crying, meditating on her husband Rama who had used a blade of grass as a Brahmastra against Kakasura, placing a blade of grass as a barrier, said: 'O Ravana! Remove your mind from me and turn it towards your own wives. I was born in the noble Janaka dynasty and married into the pure Raghu dynasty. I am the lawful wife of Rama, who is devoted to a single wife. As a pativrata, have proper vision. Follow the disciplined way of life of virtuous men. Are there no virtuous men in this land? Take yourself as an example and enjoy with your wives. If you wish to avoid a violent death at Rama's hands, unite me with the righteous Rama. Rama is a knower of dharma and compassionate to those who seek refuge. He will surely forgive you. Even if you escape weapons wielded by Indra and other gods, no one can save you from Rama's arrow. My husband, the destroyer of enemies, will soon take me from you. O wretch! Unable to defeat my people in battle, you chose a time when Rama and Lakshmana were absent and abducted me like a thief. In all the fourteen worlds, no one can save you from Rama's arrow.' Thus Sita scornfully spoke to Ravana, and Hanuman heard.

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Rama, Janaka, Indra, Lakshmana, Hanuman

### Chapter 63: Sixty-third Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 22-26
- Source PDF pages: 158, 159, 160
- Printed page numbers: 162, 163, 164
- Key entities: Ravana, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Ravana threatens Sita with a deadline to accept him, and demonesses try to persuade her. Unable to bear their harassment, Sita laments and contemplates suicide but decides her life belongs to Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** Angered by Sita's words, Ravana threatened: 'O Sita! Within this deadline I have set, change your mind and become mine, or I will kill you.' What was the deadline set by Ravana?

**Options:**
- 1. One month
- 2. Two months
- 3. Three months
- 4. Four months

**Correct answer:** Two months

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana

#### Q2

**Question:** The demonesses surrounding Sita came to her and said: 'O Sita! Ravana is most excellent and great-souled. Becoming his wife is your fortune. Therefore accept Ravana.' To which dynasty did they say Ravana belonged?

**Options:**
- 1. Chandra dynasty
- 2. Bhrigu dynasty
- 3. Pulastya dynasty
- 4. Surya dynasty

**Correct answer:** Pulastya dynasty

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** Unable to bear the harassment of the demonesses who said 'Rama, a mere human, can never reach this Lanka surrounded by ocean under any circumstances. Trust our words, accept Ravana as husband and enjoy royal pleasures,' Sita got up from there and went under which nearby tree?

**Answer:** Shimshapa tree

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Ravana, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** Unable to bear the words of the demonesses, how did Janaki Devi lament?

**Answer:** Hearing the harsh words of the demonesses around her, Janaki Devi began to lament. Frightened by their words, the great chaste Sita shed tears and with a choked voice and faltering speech, said: 'No human woman has ever become the wife of a demon. Kill me as you wish.' Like a fawn caught among wolves in the forest, Sita curled up her body and trembled violently. Disturbed by grief, she thought of her husband and worried. The words of those demonesses pierced her like spears. 'Separated from my husband Sri Rama, I am like one who has swallowed deadly poison; it is not good to live any longer. What sin did I commit in a previous birth that this terrible grief has befallen me? Under the control of these demonesses, I can never reach Sri Rama again. Therefore, it is better for me to end this life, drowned in endless sorrow. But my life belongs to my husband Sri Rama; I have no right to abandon it at my will.' Thus Janaki Devi pondered in many ways.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** In her time of distress, how did Sita decide about her survival?

**Answer:** Janaki Devi, continuously shedding tears and lamenting under the tree, fell to the ground as if insane. 'Alas! When Sri Rama went after the magical deer, the demon Ravana, who can assume any form, forcibly abducted me and brought me here while I was crying. Later, these demonesses have kept me under their control and threaten me cruelly. Immersed in such grief, I have no hope in life. Being the righteous wife of the lord of the universe, Sri Rama, why have I fallen into such a miserable state? Has my fortune turned? Death is better than living separated from my great lord. Perhaps those two great men, having set aside their weapons, have taken up the life of ascetics in the forest, eating roots and fruits? Or has the wicked Ravana killed the great heroes Rama and Lakshmana through some deceit? In such a difficult time, whatever I think, death is my only refuge. But even in this grief, death does not come to me. I am far from Rama, who is a knower of the self and the embodiment of love. I am in the clutches of the sinful Ravana. In this state, there is no other way but to die.' Thus Sita decided.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Ravana, Lakshmana

### Chapter 64: Sixty-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 27-31
- Source PDF pages: 160, 161, 162, 163
- Printed page numbers: 164, 165, 166, 167
- Key entities: Sita, Trijata, Rama, Hanuman, Ravana, Dasharatha, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Sampati
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Sita, tormented by the rakshasis, decides to end her life. A rakshasi named Trijata wakes from a dream prophesying Rama's victory and the destruction of the rakshasas, and rebukes the others. Sita, seeing auspicious signs, feels hope. Hanuman, perched on a tree, observes everything and plans to console Sita by narrating Rama's story in a soft voice.

#### Q1

**Question:** While Sita was speaking about giving up her life and some rakshasis were threatening her, a rakshasi who had just woken up rebuked the rakshasis and said, 'I had a dream just now. In that dream, destruction for the rakshasas and victory for Sri Rama will occur.' What is the name of that rakshasi?

**Options:**
- 1. Ajāmukhi
- 2. Śūrpaṇakhā
- 3. Pragḥasa
- 4. Trijatā

**Correct answer:** Trijatā

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Unable to bear the torments inflicted by the rakshasis, Sita decided to hang herself with which tool?

**Options:**
- 1. With a rope
- 2. With her own braid
- 3. With the end of her saree
- 4. With a banyan root

**Correct answer:** With her own braid

**Key entities:** Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** Janaki, who was distressed and ready to give up her life, after some time felt that something auspicious was about to happen and her mind became calm. For what reason did she feel that way?

**Answer:** Due to some auspicious omens

**Key entities:** Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** Hanuman, perched on the Ashoka tree and calmly observing everything, what kind of thoughts did he begin to have?

**Answer:** Hanuman, calmly observing everything from the tree, fully heard Sita's words, Trijata's dream account, and the words of the rakshasis threatening Sita. Then Maruti began to think about Sita. 'Millions of monkeys have gone in all directions to find Sita. The fortune of seeing her has come only to me. Like a spy who thoroughly learns the enemy's strengths while awake, I have moved unseen and learned everything. I have fully understood the characteristics of these rakshasas. I have seen the entire city of Lanka. I have understood Ravana's power and his ways. Sita's mind is deeply agitated by intense grief. If I go without consoling her, my journey will be meaningless. If I try to speak to her, rakshasis are all around. For now, I must be patient and when the rakshasis are careless, I should speak to her in simple language like an ordinary human. Already Sita is afraid of Ravana; she might mistake me for Ravana's illusion. So, without being seen by her, I should praise Rama's virtues and make her happy.' Thinking thus, Maruti, staying among the branches of the tree, looking at Sita, decided to speak sweetly in a low voice so that only she could hear, and attempted accordingly.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Trijata, Lanka, Ravana, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** In a low voice so that Sita could hear, how did Hanuman describe the story of Rama?

**Answer:** Maruti, speaking from the tree in a low voice so that Sita could hear, said: 'In the Ikshvaku dynasty, there was a great king named Dasharatha. Among his four sons, the eldest is Sri Rama. He is the embodiment of wisdom, foremost among bowmen, protector of dependents, all beings, and all dharmas. He is immensely powerful and valorous, truthful. Obeying the command of his aged father, Sri Rama went to the forests with his wife Sita and his brother Lakshmana. In that great forest, he slew many rakshasas who could change form at will. Hearing this news, the rakshasa Ravana came in anger, deceived Sri Rama through a magical deer, and abducted Sita. Then Sri Rama, searching for Sita, befriended the monkey Sugriva in that forest. By the command of the monkey king Sugriva, thousands of monkeys went in all directions to search for Sita. Among them, following the indication of Sampati, I crossed the ocean of a hundred yojanas and came here for Sita's sake. I had heard from Rama about Sita's form, beauty, special radiance, and some identifying marks. I have seen here Sita endowed with those auspicious signs.' Hearing these words of Hanuman, Janaki was astonished, remembered Sri Rama, looked carefully at the tree where she was, and saw Hanuman.

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Rama, Dasharatha, Lakshmana, Ravana, Sugriva, Sampati

### Chapter 65: Sixty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 32-36
- Source PDF pages: 163, 164, 165, 166
- Printed page numbers: 167, 168, 169, 170
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Ravana, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Vali
- Places: Kishkindha

**Summary:** Hanuman, hiding in a tree, is seen by Sita who initially suspects him to be a demon. He descends, reassures her by describing Rama's qualities and showing Rama's signet ring, and convinces her of his identity as Rama's messenger.

#### Q1

**Question:** Seeing Maruti hidden among the branches and leaves, Sita confirmed it was not a dream but reality. As he praised Rama's virtues, what did Janaki consider that monkey form to be?

**Options:**
- 1. As a demon capable of changing form
- 2. As a disguised form of Ravana
- 3. As a partisan of Rama
- 4. As a monkey who came to deceive her

**Correct answer:** As a partisan of Rama

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Hanuman descended from the Simshupa tree, bowed to Sita, recognized her as Sita, and asked about her plight. At that time, what happened to the demonesses guarding Janaki?

**Options:**
- 1. They went to Ravana.
- 2. All were sleeping.
- 3. They fled seeing Hanuman.
- 4. All went for food.

**Correct answer:** All were sleeping

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** As Sita was sinking in a series of sorrows, he came close and spoke to her. Sita suspected him to be a magical form of Ravana. How did Hanuman dispel her doubt?

**Answer:** He praised Rama's virtues.

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Hanuman, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Maruti instill confidence in Sita about himself?

**Answer:** Hanuman narrated the story of Rama. Sita rejoiced and asked how he knew Rama, how friendship between monkeys and humans occurred, and requested him to describe Rama and Lakshmana's qualities. Hanuman then described Rama's beauty from head to toe, told how Rama and Lakshmana came searching for her, how he introduced them to Sugriva, how Rama killed Vali and made Sugriva king of Kishkindha, how they found her ornaments, and how Sugriva sent monkeys in all directions to search for her. He concluded by saying he was Rama's messenger and asked her to trust him.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Vali, Kishkindha

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Hanuman give the token sent by Rama to convince Sita?

**Answer:** To fully convince Sita, Hanuman said, 'O fortunate one! I am a monkey, Rama's messenger. See this ring inscribed with Rama's name. The great Rama gave it to me to bring to you for your trust. Calm down, mother! Soon all your sorrows will vanish.' He presented the ring. Sita took it, touched it as if it were her husband, examined it, and was filled with great joy as if she had obtained her husband. She said, 'Hanuma! My Rama did not grieve when he left the kingdom to obey his father's word. But now, is he not grieving because I am far away? Among those who love Rama, there is none equal or superior to me.' Then Maruti said, 'Mother! You will soon see Rama shining on Prashravana hill. He is so absorbed in thoughts of you that he does not notice the forest flies, mosquitoes, and insects on his body. O Sita! Like the moon covered by autumn clouds, once the clouds clear, you will soon rejoice in seeing Rama.' Thus Hanuman consoled and convinced Sita.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Sita

### Chapter 66: Sixty-sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 37-40
- Source PDF pages: 166, 167, 168, 169
- Printed page numbers: 170, 171, 172, 173
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Sugriva, Ravana, Lakshmana, Indra, Varuna
- Places: Ayodhya, Lanka

**Summary:** Hanuman offers to carry Sita back to Rama, but Sita refuses, saying it is better for Rama to come himself. She gives Hanuman her chudamani (crest-jewel) as a token. Sita expresses doubts about how the monkeys and bears can cross the ocean. Hanuman reassures her of Rama's might and the strength of Sugriva's army. Sita then sends a message through Hanuman to Rama, urging him to come quickly before the deadline set by Ravana.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Hanuman pleaded with Sita to come with him, what did she reply?

**Options:**
- 1. She remained silent without saying anything
- 2. She said it is better for Rama himself to come and take me
- 3. She became angry with Hanuman
- 4. She suspected Hanuman to be Ravana's illusion

**Correct answer:** She said it is better for Rama himself to come and take me

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** When Hanuman pleaded, 'Mother! If you do not wish to come with me, give me some token that Rama can recognize,' what object did Sita give to Hanuman?

**Options:**
- 1. Necklace
- 2. Her anklets
- 3. Crest-jewel (chudamani)
- 4. Girdle

**Correct answer:** Crest-jewel (chudamani)

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Sita

#### Q3

**Question:** Sita said to Hanuman, 'O monkey hero! I have a doubt about the monkey and bear warriors who are your helpers, and about the princes Rama and Lakshmana.' What doubt did she express to Hanuman?

**Answer:** How will all of you cross the ocean?

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q4

**Question:** Knowing that Hanuman was about to depart to Rama, what topics did Sita discuss with him?

**Answer:** Hanuman told Sita that Rama, accompanied by bear and monkey heroes, would soon come and destroy the enemies. Sita praised Hanuman's words and suggested he rest in a secret place and leave the next day. She expressed uncertainty about her life lasting until his return. She said that if Rama defeats Ravana and takes her to Ayodhya, it would bring her glory; if he destroys Lanka with his arrows and takes her, it would enhance his valor. Hanuman reassured her that Sugriva, king of the monkeys, has millions of powerful monkey and bear warriors ready to sacrifice their lives for her. He said Rama of the Raghu dynasty will kill Ravana and take her to Ayodhya. He then prepared to depart.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Sita, Ravana, Ayodhya, Lanka, Sugriva

#### Q5

**Question:** What message did Sita send to Rama through Hanuman?

**Answer:** Sita told Hanuman: 'O best of monkeys! I am very happy to see you, though I am emaciated with grief. I desire to attain my noble husband. Tell Rama this: You who have valor equal to Indra and Varuna, how can you bear that your wife Sita was abducted by Ravana and is spending time among demons? I have preserved this divine crest-jewel until now; whenever I see it, I rejoice as if seeing you. The sorrows caused by the terrible demonesses are unbearable. I have endured them until now with the hope that you will come and rescue me someday. If you do not come within the deadline set by Ravana, my life will not remain. Tell my Rama thus. Also, ask about the welfare of Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva and others.' Hearing this message, Hanuman felt fulfilled and, thinking about the remaining task, resolved to go north.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Hanuman, Indra, Varuna, Ravana, Lakshmana, Sugriva

### Chapter 67: Sixty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 41-44
- Source PDF pages: 169, 170, 171
- Printed page numbers: 173, 174, 175
- Key entities: Hanuman, Sita, Ravana, Rama, Sugriva, Prahasta
- Places: Ashoka Grove, Lanka

**Summary:** Hanuman, after leaving Sita, decides to display his prowess to the demons. He destroys the Ashoka grove, fights and kills many demon warriors sent by Ravana, including Jambumali, and threatens the demons.

#### Q1

**Question:** After leaving Sita, what did Hanuman intend to do to show his prowess to the demons?

**Options:**
- 1. He went to kill Ravana
- 2. He went to kill the guards of Sita
- 3. He went to destroy the city of Lanka
- 4. He undertook to destroy the Ashoka grove

**Correct answer:** He undertook to destroy the Ashoka grove

**Key entities:** Sita, Hanuman, Ashoka Grove

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing the destruction of the Ashoka grove, the demons went to Ravana and reported. Enraged, how many demon warriors did Ravana send against Hanuman?

**Options:**
- 1. Sixty thousand
- 2. Seventy thousand
- 3. Eighty thousand
- 4. Ninety thousand

**Correct answer:** Eighty thousand

**Key entities:** Ashoka Grove, Ravana, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** What did the demon women do upon seeing Hanuman destroying the Ashoka grove and the great monkey hero?

**Answer:** They ran in all directions

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ashoka Grove

#### Q4

**Question:** In what manner did Hanuman destroy the Chaitya palace?

**Answer:** After killing all the demon warriors sent by Ravana in the Ashoka grove, Maruti saw the nearby Chaitya palace. He jumped on it to destroy it. The guards of the Chaitya palace surrounded Maruti with weapons, various maces, arrows, spears, swords, and axes. Then the son of Vayu, shouting victory to Sri Rama, angrily uprooted the golden pillars of the palace and whirled them around. The fire that arose from it burned the palace. Then, watching the burning palace, Maruti killed hundreds of demons. All-powerful Hanuman flew into the sky and threatened the demons, saying, 'We roam the entire earth under the command of the monkey king Sugriva. They are all more powerful than me. You have enmity with the great Sri Rama. The countless monkey army following Sugriva will destroy all of you. Neither this city of Lanka nor Ravana will remain under our monkey strength.' Thus Hanuman, after destroying the Chaitya palace, threatened the demons there.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana, Ashoka Grove, Rama, Sugriva, Lanka

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Anjaneya kill Jambumali?

**Answer:** Jambumali, the son of Prahasta, was very powerful. He had large fangs, wore red garments and flower garlands, held a bow, and came on a chariot yoked with donkeys. Seeing Jambumali approaching, Maruti rejoiced and roared. Then Jambumali twanged his bow and struck Hanuman with a crescent-shaped arrow. Then he struck Hanuman with a barbed arrow and ten more arrows, causing pain. Immediately, Maruti sprang up, uprooted a nearby sal tree, and began to whirl it. Jambumali cut that sal tree into pieces with four arrows. Then Hanuman, in anger, crushed Jambumali and his chariot with the trunk of that sal tree. Learning that the mighty eighty thousand Kinkaras and Jambumali had lost their lives, Ravana's eyes turned red with rage.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Prahasta, Ravana

### Chapter 68: Sixty-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 45-48
- Source PDF pages: 171, 172, 173
- Printed page numbers: 175, 176, 177
- Key entities: Hanuman, Ravana, Indrajit, Brahma, Sugriva
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** After Hanuman kills Jambumali, Ravana sends his minister's sons, then commanders with fourfold army, and finally his son Akshakumara. Hanuman defeats them all, including Akshakumara. Ravana then sends Indrajit, who uses the Brahmastra. Hanuman allows himself to be bound, pretending to be subdued, and is brought before Ravana.

#### Q1

**Question:** After killing Jambumali, how many minister's sons did Ravana send against Hanuman?

**Options:**
- 1. Seven
- 2. Eight
- 3. Nine
- 4. Ten

**Correct answer:** Seven

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** After learning of the minister's sons' deaths, Ravana, thinking carefully, sent how many commanders with the fourfold army against Hanuman?

**Options:**
- 1. Two
- 2. Three
- 3. Four
- 4. Five

**Correct answer:** Five

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** After learning that all the commanders with the fourfold army were killed by Hanuman, Ravana sent his son Akshakumara against Hanuman. The chariot Akshakumara rode was obtained through great penance and could travel in the sky. How many horses were yoked to that chariot?

**Answer:** Eight

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Maruti kill Akshakumara?

**Answer:** With Ravana's permission, Akshakumara, accompanied by the fourfold army, approached Hanuman who was seated at the entrance of the grove. Immediately, Akshakumara, ready for battle, strung his bow and shot three arrows at Maruti. Struck by three arrows at once, Hanuman looked at Akshakumara as if to burn him. Then Akshakumara flew into the sky and pursued Hanuman with his chariot, as Hanuman moved beyond the reach of his arrows. Hanuman, moving in various ways to avoid the enemy, destroyed Akshakumara's horses and chariot. Leaving the destroyed chariot, Hanuman caught the flying Akshakumara by both legs, whirled him around many times, and dashed him to the ground on the battlefield. From that blow, Akshakumara's hands, legs, and bones were crushed, his body soaked in blood, and he died. Thus killing Akshakumara, Maruti instilled fear in Ravana. Then Hanuman returned to the entrance of the grove and waited for the enemies.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the battle between Hanuman and Indrajit take place?

**Answer:** Hearing that Akshakumara was killed by Hanuman, Ravana was inwardly anxious but composed himself. Looking at his son Indrajit, he said, 'O son! You are the best among archers. You have acquired many divine weapons including the Brahmastra. I have no confidence in anyone as much as in you. Considering the excellent intelligence, physical strength, and valor of that monkey, and also considering your own strength and valor, make timely decisions and go, reciting the Brahmastra. He will not yield to anything except the Brahmastra.' After circumambulating and bowing to his father, Indrajit mounted his chariot with his army and went to the battlefield. Hanuman, hearing the sound of Indrajit's chariot, was delighted to have to fight a worthy opponent and prepared for battle. As soon as Indrajit twanged his bow and released arrows, Hanuman would dart aside like playing hide and seek. Indrajit did not know how to defeat Hanuman, nor did Hanuman know how to defeat Indrajit. Then, determined, Indrajit, intending to kill Hanuman, released the Brahmastra. Hanuman, feeling the effect of the Brahmastra, pretended to be subdued. But by the boon of Brahma, the power of that weapon vanished in an instant. However, pretending to be bound, he allowed the rakshasas to capture him, wanting to see Ravana. When the rakshasas bound Maruti with jute ropes, the effect of the Brahmastra completely disappeared. The rakshasas then brought Hanuman before Ravana. Then, with Ravana's permission, the ministers asked Hanuman, 'Who are you?' He replied that he was a messenger sent by Sugriva.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Indrajit, Ravana, Brahma, Sugriva

### Chapter 69: Sixty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 49-52
- Source PDF pages: 173, 174, 175, 176
- Printed page numbers: 177, 178, 179, 180
- Key entities: Hanuman, Ravana, Sugriva, Rama, Sita, Vibhishana, Mahaparshva, Prahasta, Nikumbha, Brahma, Dasharatha, Lakshmana, Vali
- Places: Lanka, Ayodhya, Dandaka Forest, Rishyamuka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Hanuman, bound by the Brahmastra but pretending to be captive, is brought before Ravana. Ravana, surrounded by ministers, questions him. Hanuman delivers Sugriva's message, describes Rama's glory, and advises Ravana to return Sita. Vibhishana advises against killing the messenger.

#### Q1

**Question:** When the demons brought Hanuman, who was pretending to be bound by the Brahmastra, and stood him before Ravana, how many ministers surrounded Ravana, who was accompanied by his entire retinue?

**Options:**
- 1. Four
- 2. Five
- 3. Six
- 4. Seven

**Correct answer:** Seven

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Ravana

#### Q2

**Question:** Ravana, carefully observing the monkey standing before him, ordered which of his ministers to find out who he was and why he had come to his golden Lanka?

**Options:**
- 1. Durdhara
- 2. Mahaparshva
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Nikumbha

**Correct answer:** Mahaparshva

**Key entities:** Ravana, Lanka, Mahaparshva

#### Q3

**Question:** When Prahasta asked Maruti, 'Who are you? Why have you come here?', Hanuman said he came on a royal mission and stated that by whose grace he is not bound by any weapon?

**Answer:** Brahma

**Key entities:** Prahasta, Hanuman, Brahma

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Maruti describe the glory of Sri Rama in Ravana's court?

**Answer:** In the full court, Hanuman said to Ravana: 'O King! I have come to your city of Lanka with Sugriva's message. Sri Rama is the eldest of the four sons of King Dasharatha of Ayodhya, who possesses a fourfold army. He is long-armed, all-capable, and greatly valiant. Following dharma, he came to Dandaka forest with his brother Lakshmana and wife Sita, as per his father's command. That Sita is a great noble lady. She was abducted in Dandaka forest. Searching for her, Rama and Lakshmana came to Rishyamuka mountain, met Sugriva, and made a pact: Sugriva would search for Sita, and Rama would make Sugriva king of the monkey kingdom. As agreed, Rama killed Vali and made Sugriva king. King Sugriva sent his followers in all directions to search for Sita. I am one of them. My name is Hanuman, son of Vayu. Searching for Sita, I easily crossed the hundred-yojana ocean and entered Lanka. While searching for Mother Sita, I found her in the Ashoka grove. Such dangerous deeds, contrary to dharma and causing destruction of lineage, should not be done by wise men like you. Therefore, I speak for your good. Listen to my words, return Sita to Rama, and seek refuge in him. You and your relatives can live for ten ages.' Thus Hanuman described the glory of Sri Rama to Ravana.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Ravana, Lanka, Sugriva, Dasharatha, Ayodhya, Dandaka Forest, Lakshmana, Sita, Rishyamuka, Vali, Ashoka Grove

#### Q5

**Question:** When Ravana ordered Hanuman to be killed in the court, who told Ravana that it was not dharma, and in what manner?

**Answer:** Ravana, considering the words 'Even Brahma cannot save one whom Rama wishes to kill in battle' as displeasing, became angry, reddened his eyes, and ordered, 'Kill this monkey!' Hearing this, Ravana's brother Vibhishana did not agree. Desiring his brother's welfare, he thought well and said, 'O King of rakshasas! Forgive me, give up anger. Listen to my words with compassion. No prince who knows what is proper and improper kills a messenger. This is not the custom of the world. You know dharma and what is appropriate. Therefore, O great king! Do not kill the messenger; punish him appropriately.' Then Vibhishana said, 'Brother! Elders have taught us many ways to punish a messenger, but under no circumstances is killing a messenger against dharma. Moreover, if you release him, he will go and bring Rama and Lakshmana here. Then it will be easy to destroy your enemies.' Considering Vibhishana's suggestions as excellent, Ravana sincerely gave up his attempt.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman, Brahma, Rama, Vibhishana, Lakshmana

### Chapter 70: Seventieth Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 53-56
- Source PDF pages: 176, 177, 178
- Printed page numbers: 180, 181, 182
- Key entities: Ravana, Hanuman, Vibhishana, Sita, Prahasta, Mahaparshva, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Mainaka
- Places: Lanka, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Ravana orders Hanuman's tail to be set on fire. Hanuman burns Lanka but spares Vibhishana's house. He extinguishes his tail in the sea and worries about Sita's safety. After hearing celestial beings praise the miracle of Sita's protection, he returns to Sita, reassures her, and departs by leaping from Arishtagiri mountain.

#### Q1

**Question:** Ravana, having refrained from killing the messenger, ordered which part of Hanuman's body to be set on fire?

**Options:**
- 1. Feet
- 2. Hands
- 3. Tail
- 4. Head

**Correct answer:** Tail

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** During the burning of Lanka, whose house did Hanuman leave unburnt?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta
- 2. Mahaparshva
- 3. Vajradamshtra
- 4. Vibhishana

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Lanka, Hanuman, Vibhishana

#### Q3

**Question:** After completely burning Lanka, where did Maruti fully extinguish the fire on his tail?

**Answer:** In the sea

**Key entities:** Lanka, Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** After extinguishing his tail, about whom and in what manner did Maruti grieve?

**Answer:** Anjaneya, after extinguishing the fire on his tail in the sea, began to think about Sita. 'Alas! What a great mistake I have made by burning this Lanka. If Lanka is completely burnt, will Sita also be consumed in it? Overcome by anger, I have committed treason against my master. The entire city of Lanka has turned to ashes. There is no place that is not burnt. Therefore, Sita must have surely died. If due to my perverse intellect, my action has turned disastrous and endangered the life of Mother Sita, then it is better for me to give up my life. Otherwise, having completely ruined the mission, how can I show my face to Sugriva, the lord of the vanaras, and to the great men Rama and Lakshmana? It is well known that the mind of a vanara is unstable. Due to my foolish anger, I have displayed the fickleness natural to vanaras.' Thus the son of Vayu lamented to himself. While he was thinking, 'For the success of Rama's mission, the Mainaka mountain in the sea came forward, but will fire burn the great chaste Sita?', the Charanas traveling in the sky spoke among themselves, saying, 'Even though all of Lanka has burnt, it is astonishing that fire did not even reach the vicinity where Sita is. This is a wonder.' Hearing these words, Maruti became extremely joyful. He decided to see Sita once more and then return.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Lanka, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Mainaka

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Anjaneya cross the sea again?

**Answer:** Hanuman prostrated at the feet of Sita, who was sitting in the shade of an Ashoka tree, and said, 'Mother! By divine grace, I have been able to see you safe and without any danger.' Then Sita asked Hanuman, 'O virtuous one! How can the countless armies of vanaras and bears, or Rama and Lakshmana, cross this vast ocean? This strong doubt does not leave me. What do you, who are capable of accomplishing the task, think about removing this obstacle? What is your answer?' Hanuman replied, 'Mother Sita! Sugriva is the lord of crores of vanara and bear warriors. The mighty Sugriva, along with Rama and Lakshmana, will come here and destroy the city of Lanka. Sri Rama will soon kill Ravana along with his relatives and friends, and will go to his city Ayodhya with you. Mother! Be comforted, good will come to you. Be patient for a little while. Soon you will see Sri Rama kill Ravana.' Then Hanuman bowed to Sita and, eager to see Sri Rama, decided to go across the ocean. He climbed a great mountain nearby named Arishtagiri, which had a width of ten yojanas and a height of thirty yojanas. That Arishtagiri sank under the pressure of Hanuman's footsteps. Desiring to cross the salt ocean, Maruti leaped into the sky.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Lanka, Ravana, Ayodhya

### Chapter 71: Seventy-first Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 57-60
- Source PDF pages: 178, 179, 180, 181
- Printed page numbers: 182, 183, 184, 185
- Key entities: Hanuman, Angada, Sita, Jambavan, Sugriva, Rama, Ravana, Nila, Nala, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Hanuman returns from Lanka and meets Angada and the other monkeys. He first tells them he saw Sita. They ask about Sita's condition, and Hanuman describes her pitiable state. Angada suggests they go to Lanka to rescue Sita, but Jambavan advises they first report to Sugriva and Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** After crossing the ocean and reaching the northern shore, meeting Angada and others, what was the first thing Hanuman said to them?

**Options:**
- 1. I saw Lanka
- 2. I saw Sita
- 3. I saw Ravana
- 4. I set Lanka on fire

**Correct answer:** I saw Sita

**Key entities:** Angada, Hanuman, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** Who, upon seeing Hanuman, with great joy asked him: 'Maruti! How did you recognize Sita? How is that virtuous lady? Tell us the information about Sita'?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Angada
- 3. Nila
- 4. Nala

**Correct answer:** Jambavan

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Jambavan

#### Q3

**Question:** While telling Angada and others about his search for Sita, at what time did Hanuman say he reached Lanka?

**Answer:** At sunset time

**Key entities:** Angada, Sita, Hanuman, Lanka

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Hanuman describe Sita's pitiable condition to Angada and others?

**Answer:** Hanuman told Angada and others about seeing Sita and her pitiable condition: 'O foremost of monkeys! Sri Rama's effort has succeeded. Sugriva's vow is fulfilled. My mind is overwhelmed with devotion by Sita's virtuous influence. In her devotion to her husband, she is unparalleled. Ravana, the rakshasa king, is powerful with penance, but even touching her did not destroy him due to his penance. I have learned all the details of Lanka. We can all go together, destroy Lanka, kill the rakshasas, and deliver the virtuous Sita to Sri Rama. In Ravana's Ashoka grove, under the shade of a Shimshapa tree, the great Sita is in distress. Around her, rakshasi women guard her. Though she has the beauty of the full moon, she is dim like a moon covered by clouds. Though the arrogant Ravana torments her, the beautiful and chaste Janaki does not care for him. Sita, endowed with auspicious signs, is solely devoted to Sri Rama with purity of thought, word, and deed. She still wears the same garment she wore when abducted. Her body is covered with dust and dirt, and she is emaciated with grief and sorrow.' Thus Maruti described Sita's sad tale to all his companions.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Angada, Rama, Sugriva, Ravana, Lanka, Ashoka Grove

#### Q5

**Question:** After hearing Hanuman's words, how did Angada and Jambavan express their opinions?

**Answer:** Hearing Maruti's words, Angada said: 'O monkey heroes! Even after knowing Sita's whereabouts, it is not proper for us to go to Sri Rama without her. In flying and valor, none can equal us. My opinion is that we should go to Lanka, conquer the rakshasas, and bring Janaki back.' To Angada, Jambavan replied: 'O wise Angada! Your words do not seem appropriate. Sugriva, the lord of monkeys, and the great Sri Rama sent us to the southern direction to search for Sita, but not to bring her back. In any case, taking Sita with us may not please Sri Rama. Sri Rama will bring Sita by his own valor; he does not depend on others. That lord has vowed in the presence of all monkeys that he will conquer the enemy and bring Sita. How will he agree to break his vow? Then all our effort would be futile. Therefore, let us all go and inform Sugriva and Rama and Lakshmana of what has happened so far.' Thus Jambavan expressed his opinion.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Angada, Jambavan, Sita, Rama, Lanka, Sugriva, Lakshmana

### Chapter 72: Seventy-second Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 61-64
- Source PDF pages: 181, 182, 183
- Printed page numbers: 185, 186, 187
- Key entities: Angada, Hanuman, Jambavan, Sugriva, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Sushena
- Places: Kishkindha, Dandaka Forest

**Summary:** Angada, Hanuman, and others, heeding Jambavan's advice, enter the Madhuvana forest on their return journey. The forest guard Dadhimukha complains to Sugriva about their destruction. Sugriva interprets this as a sign of success and sends Dadhimukha to bring them. The vanaras arrive at Kishkindha, and Hanuman informs Rama that he has seen Sita, bringing great joy.

#### Q1

**Question:** Angada, Anjaneya and others, respecting Jambavan's suggestions, and accordingly intending to see Sugriva, Rama and Lakshmana, on their return journey, entered which forest with joy and shouts?

**Options:**
- 1. Ashoka forest
- 2. Dandaka forest
- 3. Saugandhikavana
- 4. Madhuvana

**Correct answer:** Madhuvana

**Key entities:** Angada, Hanuman, Jambavan, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana

#### Q2

**Question:** The forest that Hanuman and others entered was under Sugriva's control, yet unable to bear the troubles caused by those vanaras, who was the forest guard that went to Sugriva?

**Options:**
- 1. Tarudu
- 2. Dadhimukha
- 3. Sushena
- 4. Shatavali

**Correct answer:** Dadhimukha

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sugriva

#### Q3

**Question:** What did Angada and others do after entering Madhuvana?

**Answer:** They drank honey and ate fruits.

**Key entities:** Angada

#### Q4

**Question:** When Dadhimukha reported the news that Hanuman and others had destroyed Madhuvana, what did Sugriva do?

**Answer:** The great hero Dadhimukha came to Sugriva, bowed at his feet, and said that Hanuman and others had destroyed Madhuvana. Then Lakshmana asked, 'What is the reason for this vanara, the forest guard, to come here? Why is he grieving?' Then Sugriva said, 'O Lakshmana! This Dadhimukha says that the prominent heroes including Angada, who went to the southern direction for searching Sita, entered Madhuvana, eating fruits, drinking honey, and destroying the forest. This is joyful news, because without the success of their mission, they would not engage in such acts. Even after the deadline I set, they have boldly entered Madhuvana and are happily sporting, meaning their mission must have succeeded. Sita must have been seen by them. There is no doubt. The achiever of this task may be Hanuman himself.' Hearing these delightful words from Sugriva's mouth, the righteous Rama and Lakshmana were filled with great joy. Then Sugriva ordered Dadhimukha, 'Uncle! What you have told us is good news. Therefore, go and quickly send Hanuman and others here. Rama, Lakshmana, and I are very eager to hear the details of the search for Sita from their mouths.'

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Angada, Sita, Rama

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Angada and others, upon coming to Kishkindha, convey the news of seeing Sita?

**Answer:** Having received Sugriva's order, Dadhimukha immediately went to Madhuvana and told Angada, 'O prince! Forgive our faults. I went to your uncle Sugriva and reported what happened here. They all rejoiced and ordered me to send all of you quickly to Kishkindha.' Hearing Dadhimukha's words, Angada said to his companions, 'O vanara warriors! After the task is accomplished, we should not stay here even for a moment. Our fatigue is also relieved. Only going to Sugriva remains.' According to Angada's words, all the vanaras said, 'Alright, let us go that way,' and they flew into the sky, traveled some distance, and came to the place where Sugriva, Rama, and Lakshmana were. They came there with the desire to see Sri Rama, placing Angada and Hanuman in front. Seeing their approach, Sugriva rejoiced, thinking that they must have achieved Rama's task. Then the mighty-armed Hanuman prostrated before Sri Rama and said the nectar-like words, 'I have seen Sita.' Hearing from Hanuman's mouth, Rama and Lakshmana were filled with supreme joy. Sugriva, Rama, and Lakshmana, who had faith that Hanuman alone could accomplish the task, looked at Maruti with respect.

**Key entities:** Angada, Kishkindha, Sita, Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Hanuman

### Chapter 73: Seventy-third Chapter

- Kanda: Sundara Kanda
- Sarga range: 65-68
- Source PDF pages: 183, 184, 185, 186
- Printed page numbers: 187, 188, 189, 190
- Key entities: Hanuman, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Janaka, Ravana, Sugriva
- Places: Lanka, Chitrakuta, Ayodhya

**Summary:** Hanuman returns to Rama and Lakshmana, reports that he has seen Sita, and delivers her message and token. He recounts Sita's doubts and his reassurances, and describes the state of Lanka.

#### Q1

**Question:** What object did Hanuman tell Rama that Sita gave him as a token?

**Options:**
- 1. A necklace
- 2. The crest-jewel
- 3. A gem bracelet
- 4. Anklets

**Correct answer:** The crest-jewel

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** While telling Rama about Sita's situation, Hanuman said that she told him she would live for how long?

**Options:**
- 1. One year
- 2. Six months
- 3. Three months
- 4. One month

**Correct answer:** One month

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** When Rama saw the divine crest-jewel sent by Sita through Hanuman, he pressed it to his heart and recalled who had given it to Sita as a gift?

**Answer:** Her father-in-law, King Janaka

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Hanuman, Janaka

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Hanuman explain Sita's message to Rama?

**Answer:** Hanuman told Rama: 'O lord! Janaki told me to remind you of the incident that happened earlier at Chitrakuta. O Ramachandra! While sleeping peacefully with you, Janaki woke up first. At that time, a crow injured her chest. Knowing this, you woke up and, after chanting a Brahmastra on a blade of darbha grass, released it at that crow. Due to the intensity of that astra, the crow wandered through all the worlds and finally sought refuge in you. Though the crow deserved to be killed, you, being compassionate to those who seek refuge, removed the crow's right eye to pacify the Brahmastra. O Rama! Rama and Lakshmana, the best of men, are immensely strong and radiant like fire. They are invincible even to the gods. Why do such great heroes ignore me? Is there any fault on my part?' Saying this, Vaidehi wept pitifully. Hearing her words, I said, 'Mother Janaki! I swear to you. Rama is grieving for you and is in a state of confusion. Because he is immersed in sorrow, Lakshmana is also distressed. At last, I was able to see you. This is not a time to grieve. Mother! Soon all your troubles will be removed. Rama will kill Ravana and take you to Ayodhya. This is true.' Thus she conveyed her message to you in many ways. Therefore, O lord! Knowing these words I have spoken, believe that she is safe.' Thus Hanuman conveyed Sita's message to Lord Ramachandra.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Chitrakuta, Lakshmana, Ravana, Ayodhya

#### Q5

**Question:** What words did Hanuman tell Rama that he used to resolve Sita's doubts in Lanka?

**Answer:** Hanuman told Rama: 'O best of men! Janaki spoke to me, saying, 'O Maruti! You are fully capable. Setting you aside, how will the other vanara and bear warriors, Rama and Lakshmana, cross this great ocean that is impossible to cross? What are you planning for them to cross this great ocean? Tell me. My son! O Hanuman! You alone are sufficient to accomplish this task. But if Rama comes with all his forces, kills Ravana in battle, and takes me to Ayodhya as a victor, that would be glorious for both the lord and me. Rama is a great hero. I am a hero's wife. You devise a method so that Rama destroys Lanka with his own arm strength and takes me away.' Thus Janaki spoke to me. O Rama! To her meaningful and logical words, I replied, 'Mother! Sugriva is the lord of the vanara and bear warriors. As soon as he resolves, they will all come here. Mother! You will soon see Rama and Lakshmana, who have the prowess of lions, standing at the gates of Lanka.' Thus I gave Sita courage in many ways. O lord! With many words of courage and auspicious speech, I consoled my mother Maithili and made her cheerful. Then that mother attained peace in my presence.' Thus Hanuman told Rama how he resolved Sita's doubts.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Sita, Lanka, Lakshmana, Ravana, Ayodhya, Sugriva

### Chapter 74: Seventy-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 1-4
- Source PDF pages: 186, 187, 188
- Printed page numbers: 190, 191, 192
- Key entities: Rama, Hanuman, Sita, Sugriva, Jambavan, Angada, Ravana, Lakshmana
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Rama hears Hanuman's account of seeing Sita and is overjoyed. He embraces Hanuman. Sugriva advises Rama to channel his anguish into anger. Hanuman describes Lanka's defenses. Rama orders the army to march to the seashore.

#### Q1

**Question:** After hearing Hanuman's account of seeing Sita, Rama was very happy and thrilled. What did Rama give to Hanuman who did such a great favor?

**Options:**
- 1. Praised him
- 2. Gifted a garland
- 3. Gave the joy of an embrace
- 4. Blessed him

**Correct answer:** Gave the joy of an embrace

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Rama, thinking deeply about crossing the ocean, began to suffer. Who first told him that they could build a bridge over the ocean and enter Lanka?

**Options:**
- 1. Sugriva
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Jambavan
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Sugriva

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Sugriva

#### Q3

**Question:** While Rama was in a state of agitation that spoiled all purposes, what did Sugriva advise him to abandon the agitation and adopt?

**Answer:** Anger (fire of anger)

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva

#### Q4

**Question:** At Rama's request, how did Hanuman describe the defense system of Lanka?

**Answer:** When Rama asked about the defense system of Lanka, Hanuman said: 'O Lord! All the inhabitants of Lanka are happy and comfortable. That city is filled with mad elephants, countless chariots, and a demon army. Therefore it is impenetrable to enemies. The city has four gates on four sides, built wide and high. Around them are moats. On the gates are powerful machines that can rain arrows and stones, stopping enemy armies attacking the city. At those gates, many demon warriors have placed hundreds of catapults made of metal. The rampart around the city is made of gold. In the moats around the rampart, water-dwelling animals like crocodiles roam. O Lord! Ravana is always eager for war. He is always vigilant in overseeing his armies. Attacking Lanka is impossible; even the gods cannot enter it. Countless demon armies guard the gates on all four sides. O Lord! I have filled the bridges over the moats and the moats themselves with stones and bricks. I have leveled most of the ramparts. I destroyed a quarter of the demon army. I set that Lanka city ablaze. If we can enter Lanka with our army by some means, victory will be ours. Therefore, O Lord! Being fully prepared, decide on an auspicious time for our departure and command Sugriva, Angada, and others.' Rama listened attentively to what Hanuman said.

**Key entities:** Rama, Hanuman, Lanka, Ravana, Sugriva, Angada

#### Q5

**Question:** As per Rama's command, how did the monkey army reach the seashore?

**Answer:** Hearing the details of Lanka told by Hanuman, Rama said to Sugriva: 'O best of monkeys! We have heard about the wicked Ravana-ruled Lanka. Let us destroy it immediately. Now the sun has reached the middle of the sky. This is the victory moment. Today is the auspicious Uttara Phalguni nakshatra. This is a suitable day for travel and victory. So it is better to depart now.' Hearing Rama's words, Lakshmana and Sugriva were delighted, prepared for the journey, appointed suitable leaders for the various army divisions, and Sugriva commanded the monkey army leaders to proceed on the correct path as directed by Rama, avoiding cities and other settlements, passing through places with good tasty fruits and sweet waters. As they proceeded, they saw the Sahyadri mountain. On the way, they saw lakes, ponds, and forests blooming with flowers. Thus, all of them traveled happily, following Rama southward, and reached the seashore filled with all kinds of aquatic creatures.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Hanuman, Sugriva, Ravana, Lakshmana

### Chapter 75: Seventy-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 5-8
- Source PDF pages: 188, 189, 190, 191
- Printed page numbers: 192, 193, 194, 195
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Hanuman, Ravana, Lakshmana, Indrajit, Vibhishana, Kumbhakarna, Mandodari, Prahasta, Nikumbha, Sugriva
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Rama reaches the seashore with the monkey army and expresses his grief over separation from Sita. In Lanka, after Hanuman's destruction, Ravana holds a council with his ministers and commanders, who boast of their strength and vow to destroy Rama and the monkeys.

#### Q1

**Question:** Rama, having reached the seashore with the monkey army, told Lakshmana: 'Brother! What kind of fire, caused by separation from Sita, is burning me completely?'

**Options:**
- 1. Submarine fire
- 2. Fire of separation
- 3. Fire of anger
- 4. Fire of jealousy

**Correct answer:** Fire of separation

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sita

#### Q2

**Question:** After Hanuman had wreaked havoc in Lanka city, who addressed the demon assembly saying 'What would be the best course of action?'

**Options:**
- 1. Indrajit
- 2. Vibhishana
- 3. Kumbhakarna
- 4. Ravana

**Correct answer:** Ravana

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Lanka, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** Seeing Ravana's valor, which prominent demon gave his daughter Mandodari in marriage to him?

**Answer:** Maya

**Key entities:** Ravana, Mandodari

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana's ministers speak words of encouragement to him?

**Answer:** After Hanuman had destroyed Lanka city, Ravana convened a council with his ministers and addressed them: 'O prominent demons! In such a critical situation, to protect ourselves and our city of Lanka, all of you think well and give appropriate suggestions.' Then all of them, one after another, saluted the lord and said: 'Lord! We have immense military strength. Our weaponry is also commensurate. In such a state, why are you worried? Have you forgotten the occasions when you defeated Yakshas, Nagas, and Danavas in battle and subjected them to various tortures? Moreover, you have conquered many mighty kings on this earth. Compared to those kings, this Rama is nothing. For you who conquered such kings, is this Rama any account? O great king! You need not exert yourself. Your mighty son Indrajit alone is enough to annihilate the entire monkey army. This Indrajit has performed many sacrifices to please the Supreme Lord and has obtained boons unattainable by others. Lord! The strength of Hanuman is far less than the splendor of those we conquered earlier. Do not overestimate him or his prowess. O king! You can surely kill Rama and achieve victory over them.' Thus Ravana's ministers submitted to him.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman, Lanka, Rama, Indrajit

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Ravana's army commanders boast before him?

**Answer:** After the ministers had spoken words of encouragement to king Ravana in the assembly, his army commanders Prahasta, Durmukha, Vajradamshtra, Nikumbha, and Vajrahanu, one after another, said: 'O great king! Devas, Danavas, Gandharvas, Pisachas, Nagas, and kings of birds could not do anything to you. What can monkeys do to you? We were complacent, thinking we had no enemy fear. That is why Hanuman struck us. Otherwise, that monkey would not have left Lanka alive.' Then another commander said: 'Lord! Entering the inner apartments without our permission and burning Lanka city are all insults to the great king. Therefore, I alone will go and kill all those monkeys.' Then another commander, gnashing his teeth and seizing a terrible iron club, said: 'Lord! Rama along with Sugriva and Lakshmana is our enemy. I alone will go and destroy them.' Immediately another commander said: 'O great king! Let you and this demon army remain as is. I alone can kill Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Hanuman, and the entire monkey army.' Then another commander, trembling with anger, said: 'O lord of demons! All of you stay calm and happily drink sweet wine. I alone will go and kill all our enemies including Rama.' Thus all of Ravana's commanders boasted in various ways.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Prahasta, Nikumbha, Hanuman, Lanka, Rama, Sugriva, Lakshmana

### Chapter 76: Seventy-sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 9-12
- Source PDF pages: 191, 192, 193
- Printed page numbers: 195, 196, 197
- Key entities: Vibhishana, Ravana, Rama, Kumbhakarna, Lakshmana, Indrajit, Sita, Indra, Sugriva, Brahma
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** After Vibhishana warns Ravana about Rama's prowess, Ravana leaves the assembly and goes to his palace. He then summons his chief ministers and allies for counsel. Kumbhakarna, awakened from his long sleep, arrives and speaks to Ravana, offering to kill Rama and Lakshmana.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Vibhishana told Ravana about Sri Rama's valor, where did Ravana go after leaving the assembly?

**Options:**
- 1. To the Ashoka garden
- 2. To the anger chamber
- 3. To his own palace
- 4. To Indrajit's palace

**Correct answer:** To his own palace

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** When Vibhishana, wishing Ravana's welfare, advised him to return Sita to Rama, Ravana said that even if Rama came with whom, he cannot stand before me?

**Options:**
- 1. With Indra and other gods
- 2. With Sugriva and others
- 3. With Brahma and others
- 4. With all the people of the world

**Correct answer:** With Indra and other gods

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Ravana, Sita, Rama, Indra

#### Q3

**Question:** Thinking that the time had come to consult with his important ministers and friends, where did Ravana go?

**Answer:** To the council chamber

**Key entities:** Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** In what manner did Ravana summon all those important to him?

**Answer:** Ravana, the evil-doer who committed the sinful act of abducting Sita, despite the good advice of Vibhishana and other relatives and friends, rejected their words due to his desire for Sita. He was distressed and weakened, not knowing what to do. War seemed inevitable; danger was approaching. So he thought that the time had come for deep consultation with his important ministers and friends. Immediately, he mounted a wonderful chariot and went to the council chamber. Then he ordered the messengers there, 'The time has come to show our strength and capabilities. So depart at once and bring all the prominent rakshasas in our city.' Immediately, the rakshasa soldiers went throughout the city of Lanka, entered without hesitation into pleasure houses, bedchambers, and gardens, and announced the lord's command to all the prominent rakshasas. Upon hearing the king's order, they all came running on their respective chariots, elephants, horses, or on foot. They parked their vehicles at a distance from the assembly hall where the great king resided, entered the hall on foot, and had an audience with Ravana. The king welcomed all who came. Thus they all waited for the king's command.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sita, Vibhishana, Lanka

#### Q5

**Question:** Among all those assembled in Ravana's court, how did Kumbhakarna converse with Ravana?

**Answer:** Ravana addressed all those who had come to the court: 'O courtiers! War seems inevitable. Enchanted by the beauty of Sita, Rama's wife, I abducted her. Keeping these two things in mind, give me advice that ensures my victory. My brother Kumbhakarna has awakened from sleep and has just arrived at the court. But since Kumbhakarna was immersed in sleep until now, I could not discuss these matters with him.' Hearing the lamentation of the lustful Ravana, Kumbhakarna said angrily: 'O lord! It would have been better if you had consulted us and taken a decision before deceiving Rama and Lakshmana and abducting Sita from their hermitage. O brother! If one performs deeds contrary to dharma through improper means, they bring about calamities. The faults of a fickle-minded person who boasts 'I am strong' and acts hastily are noticed by the enemy, who then easily strikes him. Because of your thoughtless action, we now have to deliberate. But do not grieve. I will kill them and protect you from that danger. Why should you fear while I am alive? I will kill Rama and Lakshmana and devour the vanaras. When Rama is slain by my hand, Sita will be permanently yours.' Thus Kumbhakarna spoke to his elder brother.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Kumbhakarna, Sita, Rama, Lakshmana

### Chapter 77: Seventy-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 13-16
- Source PDF pages: 193, 194, 195
- Printed page numbers: 197, 198, 199
- Key entities: Ravana, Mahaparshva, Vibhishana, Indrajit, Rama, Brahma, Indra, Sita, Angada
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** In the council hall, Ravana's ministers discuss strategy. Mahaparshva suggests using the four upayas. Vibhishana advises peace, but Indrajit and Ravana reject his counsel. Angered, Ravana insults Vibhishana, who then leaves the assembly with his four ministers and flies to Rama's side.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who cursed that if Ravana forcibly enjoys another's wife, his head will split and he will die?

**Options:**
- 1. Indra
- 2. Punjakasthala
- 3. Sita Devi
- 4. Brahma

**Correct answer:** Brahma

**Key entities:** Ravana, Brahma

#### Q2

**Question:** Observing Ravana's anger, Mahaparshva told his king which of the four upayas should we follow?

**Options:**
- 1. Sama (conciliation)
- 2. Dana (gift)
- 3. Bheda (division)
- 4. Danda (punishment)

**Correct answer:** Danda (punishment)

**Key entities:** Ravana, Mahaparshva

#### Q3

**Question:** Who told the story of Ravana's curse and spoke words beneficial to him?

**Answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Ravana, Angada

#### Q4

**Question:** In the council hall, how did Indrajit respond to Vibhishana's words?

**Answer:** Indrajit, unwillingly hearing the words of Vibhishana who spoke for Ravana's welfare like a second Brihaspati, said in the council hall: 'O uncle! You speak useless words like a coward. In our Pulastya lineage, no one like you was born before. O coward Vibhishana! What are those mere human princes before us? One ordinary rakshasa among us is enough to kill them. Not only are you afraid, but why do you frighten us? I have dethroned Indra, the lord of the three worlds. For a great hero like me, what is a mere human prince?' Hearing this, Vibhishana replied: 'My son! Indrajit! You are still a child. You do not have the ability to decide what is to be done and what is not. By speaking such meaningless words, you will certainly bring destruction to Ravana.' While Vibhishana was thus answering Indrajit, all those present heard.

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Vibhishana, Ravana, Indra

#### Q5

**Question:** Why did Vibhishana leave the council hall?

**Answer:** Not heeding Vibhishana's words spoken for his welfare, Ravana, impelled by death, said harshly: 'O rakshasa! One may live with a deadly venomous serpent, but one should never live with a relative like you who behaves like a friend but has a biased mind. I know well the nature of kinsmen in all worlds. All these relatives rejoice greatly when their kinsmen fall into sorrow. In this world, kinsmen insult one who has reached a higher state, who is efficient, learned, righteous, and heroic. Moreover, whenever they get an opportunity, they humiliate him. These wicked ones not only do not help but also contemplate treachery. In that way, you, being my kinsman, are trying to harm us who are in distress. O Vibhishana! I am honored and respected in all worlds. I am wealthy. I am born in an excellent lineage. I have trampled my enemies. Seeing this greatness, you, my kinsman, are envious. O traitor to your clan! You were born evil in the rakshasa lineage. If anyone else had spoken like this, I would have taken his life. You survive only because you are my brother.' Hearing Ravana's rude words, the righteous Vibhishana, thinking he should not stay there any longer, took his mace and flew into the sky. His four ministers also followed him.

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Ravana

### Chapter 78: Seventy-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 17-20
- Source PDF pages: 195, 196, 197, 198
- Printed page numbers: 199, 200, 201, 202
- Key entities: Vibhishana, Rama, Sugriva, Ravana, Hanuman, Angada, Jambavan, Nala, Nila, Brahma, Kumbhakarna, Indra, Indrajit, Agni, Vali, Sita
