- Places: Lanka, Kishkindha

**Summary:** Vibhishana seeks refuge in Rama, and after initial suspicion by Sugriva, Rama accepts him. Vibhishana reveals the strengths of Ravana's forces. Later, Ravana's messenger Shuka comes in the form of a parrot to deliver a message to Sugriva, but is captured and released by Rama's order.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who first told Rama that Vibhishana, who came to seek refuge, should not be given shelter, as he is an enemy?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Angada
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Sugriva

**Key entities:** Rama, Vibhishana, Sugriva

#### Q2

**Question:** Who informed Rama that Vibhishana is worthy of refuge and trustworthy?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Nala
- 3. Nila
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Rama, Vibhishana, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** Quoting the instructive words of which great sage did Rama tell Sugriva that granting refuge to Vibhishana is righteous?

**Answer:** Kandu Maharshi

**Key entities:** Rama, Sugriva, Vibhishana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Rama learn about the strengths and weaknesses of the demons through Vibhishana, who sought refuge at his feet?

**Answer:** As soon as Vibhishana learned that Rama had granted him safety, he approached Rama's feet and bowed. Then Rama said, 'Vibhishana! Tell me the strengths and weaknesses of the demons in Lanka.' Then Vibhishana said, 'O prince! Ravana has obtained extraordinary boons from Brahma. By their power, he cannot be slain by any of the gods, Gandharvas, Yakshas, or demons. My elder brother Kumbhakarna is a great warrior, equal to Indra in battle. Ravana's son Indrajit, wearing an impenetrable armor in battle, fights invisibly as an archer. He performed a sacrifice, satisfied Agni, and gained immense power. Moreover, O Rama! Ravana's ministers and commanders fight on earth like the guardians of the directions. The countless demon army living in Lanka eats flesh and blood. Some of them are shape-shifters.' Hearing this, Rama said, 'Vibhishana! You have told the truth. I have understood everything. I will sacrifice Ravana and his relatives and friends on the battlefield and make you king of Lanka.' Then Vibhishana bowed his head and saluted Rama.

**Key entities:** Rama, Vibhishana, Lanka, Ravana, Brahma, Kumbhakarna, Indra, Indrajit, Agni

#### Q5

**Question:** As Ravana's messenger, Shuka came to the place where Sugriva and others were. What topics did he discuss?

**Answer:** By Ravana's order, the demon Shuka, being a shape-shifter, took the form of a parrot and reached Rama's army on the far shore of the ocean. Remaining in the sky, he intended to deliver Ravana's message to Sugriva. He said, 'O king of monkeys! You are the brother of the mighty Vali. Therefore you are like a brother to our great king. So abandon Rama's side and join mine. What benefit will you get by fighting on Rama's side? It is true that I abducted Sita, Rama's wife. But what loss is that to you? Think it over. You are a monkey; he is a man. There is no relation between you two. So go back to Kishkindha. Even if you all try, crossing the ocean and reaching Lanka is impossible.' As Shuka spoke, some monkey warriors flew into the sky, caught the demon Shuka, brought him down, and began to punch him and pluck the feathers of the parrot-shaped Shuka. Then Shuka, frightened, sought refuge in Rama, saying, 'Lord! Protect me. Killing a messenger is not righteous.' Then Rama, showing compassion, ordered them to release him. Accepting Rama's command, they did so.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sugriva, Rama, Vali, Sita, Kishkindha, Lanka

### Chapter 79: Seventy-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 21-24
- Source PDF pages: 198, 199, 200
- Printed page numbers: 202, 203, 204
- Key entities: Rama, Garuda, Lakshmana, Angada, Nila, Jambavan, Sushena, Sugriva
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Rama, having built a bridge across the ocean and reached Lanka with his army, seeks to pacify the ocean god. He lies on a bed of darbha grass for three days. Angered by the ocean's silence, he prepares to use the Brahmastra, upon which the ocean god appears and advises him to build a bridge. Rama then arranges his army in the Garuda formation and discusses ominous portents with Lakshmana.

#### Q1

**Question:** On which bed did Sri Rama lie for three days, taking a vow to propitiate the ocean god in order to reach Lanka with his army?

**Options:**
- 1. On a bed of darbha grass
- 2. On a bed of grass
- 3. On a bed of leaves
- 4. On a stone platform

**Correct answer:** On a bed of darbha grass

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka

#### Q2

**Question:** Knowing the power of which weapon that Rama, enraged at the ocean, was about to discharge, did the ocean god become propitiated?

**Options:**
- 1. Varunastra
- 2. Agneyastra
- 3. Brahmastra
- 4. Aindrastra

**Correct answer:** Brahmastra

**Key entities:** Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** By what means did the ocean god tell Sri Rama that he could cross the ocean and go to Lanka?

**Answer:** By building a bridge

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka

#### Q4

**Question:** What kind of portentous omens that appeared to him did Sri Rama describe to Lakshmana?

**Answer:** Rama, having built a bridge over the ocean and reached Lanka with all his people, and having set up camps there, said to Lakshmana: 'Brother! This place, with abundant cool waters and full of fruit trees, is very suitable for our army. From here, let us proceed with proper battle formation. I think that based on the portents we see, a terrible fearful situation may arise. Especially for the prominent rakshasas, this will be the cause of destruction. But I also feel that danger lurks for our vanara and bear heroes. Suddenly, winds mixed with dust particles and polluted are blowing. The earth is trembling. Mountains are also slightly shaking. Clouds are roaring harshly, causing fear. The twilight is very terrifying, as if smeared with red sandalwood. Cruel animals and birds, with dejected faces, look towards the sun and cry out cruelly. All this is an indication of a fearful situation.' Thus Sri Rama told his brother that they should immediately be ready to attack Lanka city.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Lanka

#### Q5

**Question:** According to war strategy, how did Sri Rama divide his army?

**Answer:** Sri Rama, following war strategy, divided his army and commanded thus: 'Let the valiant Angada, along with Nila, stand at the chest part of the army. Let the foremost of monkeys, Rishabha, with his troops, be on the right flank. Let the mighty Gandhamadana be on the left flank of the army. I and Lakshmana, with our forces, will be alert at the head of the army. Let Jambavan, Sushena, and Vegadarshi, who are skilled in warfare, the vanara and bear heroes, stand at the belly part of the army and protect it. Let Sugriva, the lord of the vanaras, be at the rear of the army and protect it.' Then, following the Garuda formation, that army, well divided and protected by prominent vanara and bear heroes, appeared like the sky covered with clouds. The warriors in that vanara army, eager to destroy enemies on the battlefield, holding mountain peaks and great trees, besieged Lanka. They were all firmly determined to crush Lanka into pieces.

**Key entities:** Rama, Angada, Nila, Lakshmana, Jambavan, Sushena, Sugriva, Garuda, Lanka

### Chapter 80: Eightieth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 25-29
- Source PDF pages: 200, 201, 202
- Printed page numbers: 204, 205, 206
- Key entities: Rama, Ravana, Hanuman, Sugriva, Sita, Prahasta, Nikumbha, Jambavan, Lakshmana, Vibhishana
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Rama and his army reach Lanka. Ravana sends spies Shuka and Sarana to assess the enemy forces. They report back, praising the strength of the vanara army, including Hanuman, Sugriva, and others. Ravana, angered by their praise of the enemy, rebukes them. The chapter also includes Ravana's attempt to deceive Sita with a magical head of Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Sri Rama reached Lanka with his army, whom did Ravana send to ascertain the strengths and weaknesses of the enemy army?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta
- 2. Vajradamshtra
- 3. Nikumbha
- 4. Shuka and Sarana

**Correct answer:** Shuka and Sarana

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Ravana

#### Q2

**Question:** After hearing the words of his messengers, Ravana, desiring to see Rama's army along with Shuka and Sarana, where did he go?

**Options:**
- 1. On top of a mountain
- 2. Onto his palace
- 3. Outside the city of Lanka
- 4. Into the Ashoka grove

**Correct answer:** Onto his palace

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** While showing Rama's army, Sarana among Shuka and Sarana, while informing Ravana about the bear warriors, especially praised whom?

**Answer:** Jambavan

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Jambavan

#### Q4

**Question:** While informing Ravana about the vanara army, how did Shuka describe the strength and valor of Hanuman and others?

**Answer:** While Ravana was watching the vanara army from his palace, Shuka, having gone in a disguised form and gathered information, told the rakshasa lord: 'Lord! Look at the great warriors on the enemy side. They are immensely strong like mad elephants. They can fight like gods in battle. Therefore, it is impossible to face them. All these are followers of Sugriva. They are born from the aspects of gods and gandharvas. Look, Lord! There stand two youths, Mainda and Dvivida. They have divine forms. O King! After careful inquiry, I have learned that there is no one stronger than Hanuman, nor anyone with a greater physique or eloquence. He alone, without anyone's help, intends to destroy the city of Lanka. Lord, near Hanuman, the great hero of dark complexion is Sri Rama himself. He never transgresses dharma. He is skilled in the use and withdrawal of the Brahmastra. He is learned in Vedic knowledge. On his right side is his brother Lakshmana. He is like Rama's right arm. On his left side is your brother Vibhishana. Between Vibhishana and Sri Rama stands Sugriva. All of them are eager to fight Lanka.' Thus Shuka informed his lord Ravana.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Hanuman, Sugriva, Lanka, Rama, Lakshmana, Vibhishana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Ravana rebuke Shuka and Sarana?

**Answer:** After hearing what Shuka and Sarana said, Ravana saw the vanara commanders and Rama etc. standing facing Lanka and felt a little afraid in his heart. Angry that Shuka and Sarana praised the enemies, he rebuked them. They bowed their heads in fear and stood with folded hands. 'O Shuka and Sarana! A king is capable of restraint and favor. Ministers or anyone else who are recipients of his grace should not speak words displeasing to him. Is it proper for you to praise the enemy party that is coming to fight against us? You know the science of statecraft. Yet you speak thus; it is due to your ignorance. That I rule a kingdom with such foolish ministers is my greatness. A king is capable of restraint and favor. I am now letting you go without punishment because your past services have cooled my anger.' Thus Ravana spoke, and Shuka and Sarana, ashamed, bowed their heads and said 'Victory to Ravana' and left from there.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Lanka

### Chapter 81: Eighty-first Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 30-34
- Source PDF pages: 202, 203, 204
- Printed page numbers: 206, 207, 208
- Key entities: Ravana, Rama, Sita, Vibhishana, Indrajit, Prahasta, Lakshmana, Hanuman
- Places: Dandaka Forest, Ashoka Grove, Ayodhya

**Summary:** After Shuka and Sarana, Ravana sends spies to learn about Rama's forces. He orders Vidyujjihva to create a magical head of Rama to deceive Sita. When Ravana shows the head to Sita, a doorkeeper announces someone's arrival. Sarama, Vibhishana's wife, consoles the grieving Sita and later reports Ravana's secret plans.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Shuka and Sarana, whom did Ravana send as spies to find out about Sri Rama's forces?

**Options:**
- 1. Vajradamshtra
- 2. Indrajit
- 3. Shardula and others
- 4. Prahasta

**Correct answer:** Vidyujjihva

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** To frighten and deceive Sita and conquer her, whom did Ravana command to create Sri Rama's head?

**Options:**
- 1. Vidyujjihva
- 2. Shardula
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Akshakumara

**Correct answer:** Indrajit

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Rama, Indrajit

#### Q3

**Question:** When Ravana showed the magical head of Sri Rama and asked Sita to surrender, who did the doorkeeper announce had come to see him?

**Answer:** Prahasta

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Sita, Prahasta

#### Q4

**Question:** Who consoled Sita, who was grieving upon seeing the magical head of Sri Rama, and how?

**Answer:** Among the rakshasi women appointed by Ravana to guard Sita, there was a rakshasi named Sarama, who was Vibhishana's wife and kind-hearted. She came to Sita, who was deluded by Ravana's magic and grieving, and consoled her. Taking courage due to her previous friendship with Sita, she said, 'Mother Sita! Calm down, be brave. I heard Ravana's words to you while hiding behind a tree. I have no attachment to life. I have been moving unseen and learning their affairs. The head of Sri Rama shown to you is Ravana's magical creation. That rakshasa king has used his illusion on you. Mother! Sri Rama has now crossed the ocean with the monkey army via the bridge. Sri Rama is under the protection of mighty monkeys, Vibhishana, and Lakshmana. No one can even lift their eyes to look at Rama. You have heard the war drums sounded by Ravana. If he had truly killed Rama, why would he make these war efforts? O Sita! The rakshasas are afraid. Soon you will hear good news.' Thus Sarama consoled Sita.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Ravana, Vibhishana, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** At Sita's request, what details did Sarama reveal to Janaki?

**Answer:** Sita said to the very capable Sarama, 'Friend, if you are determined to do me good, go to Ravana and find out what he is doing and tell me. I am anxious and fearful due to that magician's actions. I tremble with fear here because of him.' Sarama replied, 'Mother! I will leave now. I will fully learn the efforts and thoughts of the enemies there.' She immediately went near Ravana. While Ravana was talking with his ministers, she hid behind a pillar and learned his secret plans. Then she quickly returned to Sita and said, 'Vaidehi! Ravana's mother Kaikesi, and a close relative and old minister named Aviddha, both advised Ravana at length to return you to Sri Rama. Citing the incident in Dandaka forest, Rama's prowess, Hanuman's crossing the ocean, visiting you in Ashoka grove, and killing many rakshasas in battle, they tried to convince the rakshasa king in many ways. But the greedy Ravana is unwilling to release you. Only when he falls on the battlefield under the impact of Sri Rama's fierce arrows will Sri Rama safely take you to Ayodhya.' Thus Sarama told Sita the details she had seen in Ravana's inner palace.

**Key entities:** Sita, Ravana, Rama, Dandaka Forest, Hanuman, Ashoka Grove, Ayodhya

### Chapter 82: Eighty-second Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 35-39
- Source PDF pages: 204, 205, 206
- Printed page numbers: 208, 209, 210
- Key entities: Ravana, Rama, Vibhishana, Prahasta, Indrajit, Nila, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Indra
- Places: Lanka, Kailasa

**Summary:** Ravana, seated in court with his ministers, is advised by his relative Malyavan to make peace with Rama. Ignoring this counsel, Ravana prepares for war and assigns guards to the gates. Following Vibhishana's advice, Rama assigns commanders to besiege Lanka. The army spends the night on Suvela mountain, and from there they observe the beauty of Lanka.

#### Q1

**Question:** When Ravana was seated with his ministers, who among his close relatives advised him, 'O king! It seems better to make peace with the mighty Rama'?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta
- 2. Malyavan
- 3. Indrajit
- 4. Vajradamshtra

**Correct answer:** Malyavan

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Disregarding whose words, spoken for his welfare, did Ravana prepare for war and first appoint whom for protection at the eastern gate?

**Options:**
- 1. Vidyujjihva
- 2. Indrajit
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Malyavan

**Correct answer:** Prahasta

**Key entities:** Ravana, Prahasta

#### Q3

**Question:** According to Vibhishana's advice, whom did Rama tell to stand at the eastern gate and confront those there, in order to besiege Lanka?

**Answer:** Nila

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Rama, Lanka, Nila

#### Q4

**Question:** On the night when Rama made the battle formation to conquer Lanka, where and how did they all spend it?

**Answer:** To conquer Lanka, Rama decided who should confront at which gate and told Vibhishana that the vanaras are shape-shifters, but during war they should not assume human forms. In the war we are about to wage, the vanara forces alone will be our mark. This will be our sign to identify our side. During the war, only I, Lakshmana, you my friend, and your four followers—seven of us in total—will be in human form. Thus Rama addressed his people and Vibhishana. Then Rama, along with Sugriva, Vibhishana, and Lakshmana, said to all his followers, 'Friends! Now all of us should go to this beautiful Suvela mountain, which is full of various minerals like red ochre. Let us all go to this mountain and spend the night there.' Thus Rama with all his followers went to Suvela mountain and spent the night comfortably.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Vibhishana, Lakshmana, Sugriva

#### Q5

**Question:** From Suvela mountain, how did Rama and others observe Lanka?

**Answer:** The entire vanara army with Rama spent the night comfortably on Suvela mountain. Afterwards, they all enjoyed the beauties of Lanka city on Trikuta mountain. They saw its gardens, groves, and level grounds without hills and valleys. They saw many beautiful places between Trikuta and Suvela mountains, with various trees, flowering trees, divine trees, and different kinds of creepers entwined around them, and flowers blooming on the treetops—all delightful to behold. Seeing Lanka thus adorned, shining like Indra's Amaravati, they were all amazed. The royal palace in Lanka, built with a thousand pillars, touching the sky like the peak of Kailasa, served as an ornament to the city. That Lanka city, with wonderful forests, was the abode of various-shaped rakshasas. The greatly radiant Rama, along with all his followers, observed that Ravana's Lanka city, abounding in all wealth like grains and riches, and was amazed.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lanka, Indra, Kailasa, Ravana

### Chapter 83: Eighty-third Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 40-44
- Source PDF pages: 206, 207, 208
- Printed page numbers: 210, 211, 212
- Key entities: Ravana, Sugriva, Rama, Indrajit, Lakshmana, Angada, Jambavan, Vibhishana, Brahma
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** The chapter describes the initial battle between the vanaras and rakshasas, including the duel between Ravana and Sugriva, Rama's siege of Lanka, and the night battle where Indrajit uses the Nagastra to bind Rama and Lakshmana.

#### Q1

**Question:** In the battle between Ravana and Sugriva, which weapon did Ravana use that made Sugriva flee?

**Options:**
- 1. Brahmastra
- 2. Varunastra
- 3. Maya Shakti
- 4. Agneyastra

**Correct answer:** Maya Shakti

**Key entities:** Ravana, Sugriva

#### Q2

**Question:** After besieging Lanka on all sides, whom did Sri Rama send as an envoy to Ravana according to war strategy?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Angada
- 3. Sugriva
- 4. Vibhishana

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Lanka, Rama, Ravana, Angada

#### Q3

**Question:** When Ravana learned from his soldiers that Sri Rama had besieged Lanka on all sides, where did he go to observe the scene?

**Answer:** From atop his palace

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Lanka

#### Q4

**Question:** How did the initial battle between the vanaras and rakshasas take place?

**Answer:** A fierce battle raged between the vanara and rakshasa warriors, with both sides filled with rage. The cruel rakshasas, desiring victory for Ravana, roared with war cries, adorned with gold ornaments, horses, elephants, chariots, banners, and armor. The vast vanara army, eager for victory, charged at the shape-shifting rakshasas. Then a duel broke out between the vanaras and rakshasas, each fighting suitable opponents. The rakshasas used their weapons, while the vanaras fought with sharp claws, teeth, and trees. In this duel, like the battle between devas and danavas, the rakshasas bit the dust under the blows of the vanaras. Swords, maces, spears, iron clubs, and broadswords fell on the battlefield. Broken chariots, dead horses and elephants, and the corpses of vanaras and rakshasas, along with chariot wheels, axles, and yokes, were scattered everywhere. Jackals gathered in packs to devour the dead bodies. Then, hoping that their strength would increase after sunset, the rakshasas waited for that time.

**Key entities:** Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the night battle between the vanara and rakshasa warriors proceed?

**Answer:** While the vanaras and rakshasas were fighting, the sun set and darkness enveloped them. Yet the warriors did not stop the battle, each determined to conquer. In the darkness, the rakshasas attacked the vanaras, killing and devouring them. The vanaras, not yielding, tore the rakshasas apart with their teeth and agitated them with fury. Then Rama and Lakshmana killed both visible and invisible rakshasas with their arrows. In that terrible battlefield, rivers of blood flowed horribly. The cries of severely wounded rakshasas and the lamentations of blood-soaked vanaras were heard dreadfully. Angada, seeking to kill his rival Indrajit, performed heroic feats on the battlefield. Indrajit was wounded by his assault; his chariot and horses died, and his charioteer fell. Then Indrajit, helpless, abandoned his chariot and disappeared. Rama and Lakshmana praised Angada's battle skill. Defeated by Angada, Indrajit, using the boon from Brahma, fought invisibly with the art of disappearing. In anger, Indrajit released the Nagastra on Rama and Lakshmana. Due to that, both were wounded, bound by the Nagastra, and fell unconscious. The leading vanaras saw Rama and Lakshmana in that state. Thus the night's battle took place.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Angada, Indrajit, Brahma

### Chapter 84: Eighty-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 45-49
- Source PDF pages: 208, 209, 210, 211
- Printed page numbers: 212, 213, 214, 215
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Indrajit, Sugriva, Vibhishana, Ravana, Sita, Trijata, Angada, Jambavan, Hanuman, Prahasta, Mandodari
- Places: Lanka, Kishkindha, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Rama and Lakshmana are bound by the Nagastra (serpent weapon) of Indrajit. Sugriva is terrified, but Vibhishana consoles him. Indrajit returns to Lanka and boasts to Ravana that he has killed Rama and Lakshmana. Ravana orders demonesses to show Sita the bound brothers, causing her immense grief. The demoness Trijata consoles Sita, assuring her that Rama and Lakshmana are alive. Rama regains consciousness and laments over Lakshmana's condition, then advises Sugriva to return to Kishkindha, but the monkeys weep. Vibhishana arrives with a mace.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who consoled Sugriva when he was frightened seeing Rama and Lakshmana bound by the Nagastra?

**Options:**
- 1. Angada
- 2. Jambavan
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Vibhishana

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Rama, Lakshmana, Vibhishana

#### Q2

**Question:** To whom did Indrajit first announce in Lanka with great joy that Rama and Lakshmana were killed by him?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta
- 2. Ravana
- 3. Vajradamshtra
- 4. Mandodari

**Correct answer:** Ravana

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Lanka, Rama, Lakshmana, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** Who consoled Sita when she was overwhelmed with endless grief after demonesses showed her Rama and Lakshmana bound by the Nagastra as per Ravana's order?

**Answer:** Trijata

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ravana, Trijata

#### Q4

**Question:** Who among the demonesses guarding Sita consoled her when she saw Rama and Lakshmana bound by the Nagastra? How did she console her?

**Answer:** On the battlefield, as per Ravana's command, demonesses took Sita on the Pushpaka Vimana and showed her Rama and Lakshmana bound by the Nagastra. Seeing this, Sita thought they were dead and lamented endlessly. Then Trijata, one of the demonesses guarding her, consoled Sita saying, 'O Devi! You need not grieve. Your husband is alive. Both Rama and Lakshmana are alive. Otherwise, O Vaidehi, this divine vimana would not have brought a woman who has lost her husband. Moreover, based on my dream, it is impossible for Rama and Lakshmana to die. So stop grieving and thinking wildly.' Hearing these nectar-like words, Sita joined her palms in gratitude and said, 'O Trijata! May your words come true!' Then the distressed Janaki returned to Ashoka Vana with Trijata and other demonesses, still deeply sorrowful thinking of Rama and Lakshmana.

**Key entities:** Sita, Rama, Lakshmana, Ravana, Trijata, Ashoka Grove

#### Q5

**Question:** What did Sri Rama contemplate after regaining consciousness while bound by the Nagastra?

**Answer:** Rama and Lakshmana were bound by terrible serpent nooses and sighing. Sugriva and other foremost monkeys surrounded them grieving. Though bound by serpent nooses, the greatly valiant Sri Rama, being courageous, strong, and of firm physique, regained consciousness after a while and opened his eyes. Then he saw Lakshmana wounded and bleeding. Seeing him, Sri Rama thought, 'Alas! Lakshmana, who is my life, has been defeated in battle and lies on the ground. While I am alive, I have to see my brother in this state! For whom should I live? What is Sita to me now? Why should I live? My desire to live is waning. It is better to give up my body here. Because of me, he has come to this condition.' Then Rama called Sugriva and said, 'O best of monkeys! Sugriva! I will give up my life. When I am gone, Ravana will consider you weak and drive you away. So you should immediately return to Kishkindha from here. You and your followers have risked your lives and fought for me. I am pleased with that. Sugriva! No human can overcome destiny. You have done all that you could for me. All these monkey warriors, out of affection for me, have fought wonderfully until now. Now you may go to your respective places as you wish.' Hearing Rama's words, all the monkeys shed tears from their reddened eyes. Then Vibhishana, mace in hand, came there and saw Rama.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Sita, Ravana, Kishkindha, Vibhishana

### Chapter 85: Eighty-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 50-54
- Source PDF pages: 211, 212, 213
- Printed page numbers: 215, 216, 217
- Key entities: Rama, Lakshmana, Garuda, Ravana, Hanuman, Angada, Jambavan, Vibhishana, Indrajit, Nikumbha, Sugriva
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** After Rama and Lakshmana are freed from the Nagapasha (serpent arrows) by Garuda, Ravana sends demons to fight. Dhumraksha is killed by Hanuman. Then Ravana sends Vajradamshtra, who is confronted by Angada. After a fierce battle, Angada kills Vajradamshtra.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who is responsible for freeing Rama and Lakshmana from the Nagapasha bonds?

**Options:**
- 1. Jambavan
- 2. Hanuman
- 3. Vibhishana
- 4. Garuda

**Correct answer:** Garuda

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Garuda

#### Q2

**Question:** After learning that Rama and Lakshmana, freed from the Nagapasha bonds, became more radiant than before, whom did Ravana first send to the battlefield?

**Options:**
- 1. Indrajit
- 2. Dhumraksha
- 3. Nikumbha
- 4. Prajangha

**Correct answer:** Dhumraksha

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** By whose hands did the demon Dhumraksha die?

**Answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Angada confront Vajradamshtra who came to the battlefield?

**Answer:** Upon learning that Dhumraksha had fallen in battle, Ravana summoned the mighty, heroic, and magical Vajradamshtra and said, 'O hero! Go to the battlefield with a sufficient demon army and destroy Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, and other monkey warriors.' Thus he sent him to the battlefield. Carrying various weapons like sticks, small spears, strange tridents, pestles, lances, nooses, axes, swords, discs, maces, and large axes, the foot soldiers followed their commander Vajradamshtra and came to the southern gate where Angada was stationed. At that time, some ill omens appeared to the demons. But ignoring them, they all advanced with battle fervor. A fierce battle began between the terrifying and courageous monkey warriors and the demon warriors. The battle was so intense that the battlefield was filled with broken chariots, fallen horses, strangely lying banners, and the corpses of monkeys and demons. The ground was soaked with the blood of fallen heroes. The battlefield, with the cries of warriors, resembled an autumn night. Angada, with his unparalleled valor, terrified the demon forces.

**Key entities:** Angada, Ravana, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the slaying of Vajradamshtra take place?

**Answer:** The mighty Vajradamshtra was skilled in archery. Immediately, he strung his bow and rained arrows on the monkey army. The heroic demon warriors also continued fighting with various weapons. The best among the monkeys, holding great rocks, fought from all sides. At that time, the demon warriors hurled thousands of weapons at the monkey warriors. The monkey warriors also attacked the demons with tree branches and rocks. All bodies were covered with streams of blood. There, monkeys and demons fell unable to bear the blows of battle. Vultures, eagles, crows, and jackals gathered in flocks to eat the corpses. Seeing all this, Vajradamshtra's anger burst forth, and he shot sharp arrows at the monkeys. Then the invincible hero Angada, holding a tree, hurled it at Vajradamshtra. Vajradamshtra cut the approaching tree with his arrows. Seeing that, Angada picked up a great rock and threw it at Vajradamshtra. To avoid the oncoming rock, the demon jumped down from his chariot holding a mace. The chariot was destroyed by the rock. Then Angada threw another stone. Struck by it, Vajradamshtra lost consciousness. After a while, the demon regained consciousness and came at Angada, engaging in fistfight. In that fight, they kicked each other with knees, and both fell to the ground exhausted. Quickly recovering, Angada snatched the sword from Vajradamshtra's hand and struck the demon's head, splitting it in two. Thus Vajradamshtra died at the hands of Angada.

**Key entities:** Angada

### Chapter 86: Eighty-sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 55-59
- Source PDF pages: 213, 214, 215, 216
- Printed page numbers: 217, 218, 219, 220
- Key entities: Angada, Ravana, Prahasta, Hanuman, Nila, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Rama, Indrajit, Kumbhakarna, Vibhishana, Jambavan, Tara
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** After Vajradamshtra is killed by Angada, Ravana sends Prahasta to lead the demon army. Hanuman kills Akampana, and then Prahasta leads the demons. Prahasta is confronted by the vanara Nila, who kills him with a boulder. Ravana then enters the battlefield, fights with Sugriva, Lakshmana, and Hanuman, and finally with Rama. Rama, seeing Ravana exhausted, tells him to return to the city and come back the next day.

#### Q1

**Question:** After Vajradamshtra was killed by Angada, under whose leadership did Ravana lead the demon army?

**Options:**
- 1. Prahasta
- 2. Akampana
- 3. Dhumraksha
- 4. Indrajit

**Correct answer:** Prahasta

**Key entities:** Angada, Ravana, Prahasta

#### Q2

**Question:** After Akampana was killed by Hanuman, under whose leadership did the demon warriors enter the battlefield?

**Options:**
- 1. Vajradamshtra
- 2. Ravana
- 3. Prahasta
- 4. Kumbhakarna

**Correct answer:** Prahasta

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Prahasta

#### Q3

**Question:** Who stopped Ravana's commander-in-chief Prahasta on the battlefield?

**Answer:** Nila

**Key entities:** Ravana, Prahasta, Nila

#### Q4

**Question:** How and by whom was the demon commander Prahasta killed?

**Answer:** Seeing Prahasta arrive on the battlefield, Sri Rama smiled and asked Vibhishana, 'O mighty-armed one! Who is this coming angrily with a great army?' Then Vibhishana said, 'Lord! This is Prahasta, the commander-in-chief of all the armies of Ravana, the lord of Lanka. He is extremely strong and valorous.' While he was speaking, Prahasta roared and advanced towards the vanara army. The demon army came holding various weapons. Seeing the demon army approaching, the vanara army also became fully ready, holding trees, branches, and large boulders. A fierce battle began between the two sides. Many demon warriors killed many vanara warriors. The prominent vanaras, all over the battlefield, were crushing the demons with trees and large boulders. Then Prahasta's ministers, the four demon warriors named Narantaka, Kumbhahanu, Mahanada, and Samunnata, were dealing death blows to the vanaras. Seeing this, the vanara warriors Dvivida, Jambavan, Tara, and Durmukha came and killed those four demon warriors. Seeing this, Prahasta, enraged, from his chariot, killed vanara warriors with a shower of arrows. Seeing this, the vanara warrior Nila confronted Prahasta. Uprooting a nearby maddi tree, Nila destroyed Prahasta's chariot, horses, and charioteer. Immediately, Nila forcefully snatched the bow from Prahasta's hand and broke it into pieces. Prahasta jumped to the ground. As Prahasta rushed towards him, Nila killed him by smashing his head with a large boulder. Thus Prahasta died at the hands of Nila.

**Key entities:** Prahasta, Rama, Vibhishana, Ravana, Jambavan, Tara, Nila

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the first battle between Rama and Ravana take place?

**Answer:** Learning that Prahasta, the commander-in-chief of all demons, had died at the hands of the vanara warrior Nila, Ravana mounted a chariot yoked with excellent horses and went to the battlefield. He sent back some of the prominent demons who were following him for the protection of the city. Sugriva hurled a mountain peak at Ravana, who was advancing towards the vanara army. Ravana avoided it with his arrows. Then, enraged, Ravana shot an arrow that struck Sugriva, who lost consciousness and fell on the battlefield. Then the vanara warriors sought refuge in Sri Rama. Immediately, Rama took up his bow and started forth, but Lakshmana said he would go and finish Ravana. With Rama's permission, Lakshmana fought with Ravana for a while and lost consciousness due to the strike of the Shakti weapon hurled by Ravana. Then Hanuman, enraged, rushed at Ravana. That Maruti clenched his fist and struck Ravana on the chest, causing Ravana to lose consciousness. At that time, Hanuman picked up the unconscious Lakshmana and brought him to Sri Rama. Then Rama mounted Hanuman's shoulders and went to battle. After fighting with Ravana for a while, Rama saw that Ravana was very tired and weak, and said, 'Ravana! You are very tired now. So go back to the city and come again tomorrow. Then you will know how great my strength is.' Ravana, according to Sri Rama's words, stopped the battle and went to the city.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Prahasta, Nila, Sugriva, Lakshmana, Hanuman

### Chapter 87: Eighty-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 60-64
- Source PDF pages: 216, 217, 218
- Printed page numbers: 220, 221, 222
- Key entities: Ravana, Rama, Prahasta, Kumbhakarna, Mahodara, Sita, Lakshmana, Indrajit, Trishira, Vibhishana, Hanuman, Sugriva, Jambavan
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Ravana, recalling his humiliation by Rama and the death of Prahasta, considers whom to send next into battle. Kumbhakarna is awakened and after a conversation with Ravana, prepares for war. Mahodara proposes a deceptive plan to trick Sita into believing Rama and Lakshmana are dead.

#### Q1

**Question:** Remembering his humiliation at the hands of Sri Rama and the death of Prahasta, whom did Ravana think of introducing next into battle?

**Options:**
- 1. Indrajit
- 2. Kumbhakarna
- 3. Trishira
- 4. Mahodara

**Correct answer:** Kumbhakarna

**Key entities:** Rama, Prahasta, Ravana, Kumbhakarna

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing Kumbhakarna's entry into battle, whom did Sri Rama ask about his story?

**Options:**
- 1. Anjaneya
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Vibhishana
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Rama, Vibhishana

#### Q3

**Question:** When Kumbhakarna, waking up with great difficulty, asked his elder brother Ravana 'From whom do you have fear?', whose name did Ravana mention?

**Answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** Before entering the battlefield, how did Kumbhakarna converse with his elder brother Ravana?

**Answer:** Having woken from a long sleep, Kumbhakarna entered Ravana's inner palace and said laughingly, 'O King! Earlier, some of us pointed out the flaw in your decision and spoke for your good, but you turned a deaf ear. This war is the result of that; the fruit of your sin has quickly come to experience. O great king! Before abducting Sita, you should have considered the pros and cons of this act. But out of sheer pride in your strength, you failed to think about it. However strong and proud one may be, one should think about the consequences of the action one is about to undertake. When one does not do so, one must suffer the result.' Then Ravana said to Kumbhakarna, 'Kumbhakarna! There is no use thinking about the past now. Think about what needs to be done now. Tell me what would be beneficial for us at present. What is done is done. Correct my mistake with your ability.' To this, Kumbhakarna replied, 'O great king! You do not wish to return Sita to Rama as our brother Vibhishana advised. So now be carefree. Give up anger and steady your mind. As long as there is life in my body, you need not worry. It is about Sri Rama that you are thinking, is it not? I will surely kill him. Now in the battlefield, I will display valor against the enemy, kill Sri Rama, and bring his head from the battlefield. Seeing that, you will rejoice.' Thus Kumbhakarna became ready for war.

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Sita, Rama, Vibhishana

#### Q5

**Question:** What kind of deceptive plan did Mahodara reveal to Ravana?

**Answer:** After Kumbhakarna said 'I alone will go and kill Rama', Mahodara, who was present there, said to Ravana, 'O lord! I will tell you a stratagem that I know, better than conquering Rama in battle. If you think it is excellent, follow it. O great king! You brought Sita here because you desired her. If you wish, she will come under your control. My plan is this: I, Kumbhakarna, Vidvijjihva, Samhradi, and Vitardhana – we five will go to the battlefield to kill Rama. If we conquer Rama, no stratagem is needed. If Rama conquers us, then we, struck by Rama's arrows and with blood-smeared bodies, will fall at your feet and say, 'We have killed and devoured Rama and Lakshmana.' Then you should have it proclaimed in the city of Lanka that Rama and Lakshmana have died in battle. This news will spread throughout Lanka and also reach Sita. Thereafter, you may enter the Ashoka grove and, with soothing words, tempt Sita and win her over. Learning of this, Rama will stop the war. Then you will have no need to fight. So, O great king! I have told you the plan that occurred to me. If you think it will bring you benefit, you may try it.' Thus Mahodara revealed his plan to Ravana.

**Key entities:** Mahodara, Ravana, Kumbhakarna, Rama, Sita, Lakshmana, Lanka, Ashoka Grove

### Chapter 88: Eighty-Eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 65-70
- Source PDF pages: 218, 219, 220, 221
- Printed page numbers: 222, 223, 224, 225
- Key entities: Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Rama, Vibhishana, Sugriva, Hanuman, Angada, Nila, Trishira, Atikaya, Indra, Mahodara, Mahaparshva, Brahma
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Kumbhakarna, with Ravana's permission, goes to the battlefield and boasts about whom he will kill first. The monkeys flee in fear upon seeing Kumbhakarna's form and roars, but are stopped by someone with soothing words. Kumbhakarna is eventually slain. Ravana laments upon hearing the news of Kumbhakarna's death. Ravana's sons and brothers go to battle and are killed by various monkey warriors.

#### Q1

**Question:** With Ravana's permission, as Kumbhakarna goes to the battlefield, whom does he tell the accompanying demon army he will kill first?

**Options:**
- 1. Vibhishana
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Sri Rama
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Ravana, Kumbhakarna, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Who stopped the monkeys fleeing in fear upon seeing Kumbhakarna's form and hearing his roars in the battlefield, using soothing words?

**Options:**
- 1. Sri Rama
- 2. Nila
- 3. Vibhishana
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Angada

#### Q3

**Question:** Who killed Kumbhakarna, who was roaming valiantly on the battlefield and terrifying the monkeys?

**Answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Rama

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Ravana lament upon hearing the news of Kumbhakarna's death?

**Answer:** When the demons reported to Ravana that Kumbhakarna had died at the hands of Sri Rama, Ravana was immersed in endless grief and fell unconscious. Ravana's sons Devantaka, Narantaka, Trishira, and Atikaya also grieved for their uncle for a while. Ravana lamented, 'Alas! Kumbhakarna! You were immensely strong, having killed many enemies. Being a great hero, you left everyone and went away alone before helping me in my distress! Brother! You were like my right arm. As long as you were my support, I feared neither gods nor demons. Now that you have fallen, I am as good as dead! Great hero, you did not fear even Indra's thunderbolt! How then were you killed by Rama? All the gods along with the sages will be overjoyed to learn of your fall on the battlefield. Brother! Kumbhakarna! Earlier, due to my stubbornness, I ignored the good words spoken by Vibhishana. Now I see the result clearly.' Thus Ravana lamented in many ways, falling to the ground.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Kumbhakarna, Rama, Trishira, Atikaya, Indra, Vibhishana

#### Q5

**Question:** How were Ravana's sons Trishira, Devantaka, Mahodara, and Mahaparshva killed in the battlefield, and by whom?

**Answer:** Seeing Ravana suffering in endless grief, his four sons Trishira and others told their father, 'O great king! The death of our mighty uncle is fate. A noble person like you should not lament thus. You are capable of ruling the three worlds. By Brahma's grace, you are endowed with various weapons. Therefore, you can easily conquer Rama. O king! If you command, we will go to war. Be at ease.' Hearing his sons' words, Ravana was somewhat comforted, blessed them, and sent his brothers Mahaparshva and Mahodara along with them for protection. Driven by fate, Ravana's sons Trishira, Devantaka, Narantaka, Atikaya, and his brothers Mahaparshva and Mahodara, six great warriors, went to the battlefield. They were all skilled in magic and could travel through the sky. On the battlefield, they fought with the monkey warriors according to their respective strengths. Narantaka was killed by Angada's fist blow. Devantaka's head was shattered by Hanuman's fist and he fell on the battlefield. Mahodara's head was split by a rock thrown by Nila and he fell dead. Hanuman snatched Trishira's sword and cut off his head with it. Mahaparshva was felled by the monkey chief Rishabha. Thus, Ravana's sons and brothers were killed by the monkey chiefs.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Trishira, Mahodara, Mahaparshva, Brahma, Rama, Atikaya, Angada, Hanuman, Nila

### Chapter 89: Eighty-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 71-75
- Source PDF pages: 221, 222, 223
- Printed page numbers: 225, 226, 227
- Key entities: Ravana, Indrajit, Rama, Lakshmana, Jambavan, Hanuman, Sugriva, Kumbha, Nikumbha, Atikaya, Kumbhakarna, Narayana, Brahma, Shiva, Indra, Vibhishana
- Places: Himalaya, Lanka

**Summary:** Ravana mourns his fallen sons and brothers, but Indrajit consoles him and goes to battle. Indrajit uses the Brahmastra to render Rama and Lakshmana unconscious. Jambavan sends Hanuman to bring the four life-restoring herbs from the Himalayas. Unable to identify the herbs, Hanuman brings the entire mountain, and the herbs revive the fallen warriors. Sugriva then orders the vanaras to set Lanka on fire. Ravana sends Kumbha, Nikumbha, and other rakshasas to fight.

#### Q1

**Question:** By which weapon, launched by Lakshmana, did Atikaya, the son of Ravana, fall to the ground?

**Options:**
- 1. Brahmastra
- 2. Varunastra
- 3. Agneyastra
- 4. Pashupatastra

**Correct answer:** Brahmastra

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Atikaya, Ravana

#### Q2

**Question:** Unable to bear that his sons and brothers like Kumbhakarna had become sacrifices on the battlefield, Ravana thought that Rama was not an ordinary person. As whose incarnation did he consider Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. As Brahma
- 2. As Parama Shiva
- 3. As Indra
- 4. As Sriman Narayana

**Correct answer:** Sriman Narayana

**Key entities:** Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Rama, Narayana

#### Q3

**Question:** While Ravana was grieving thinking that all his people had become sacrifices on the battlefield, who consoled him and, as Indrajit went to the battlefield, which animals did he yoke to his chariot?

**Answer:** The answer is in the answer column.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Indrajit

#### Q4

**Question:** Why did Rama and Lakshmana lose consciousness? In what manner did Hanuman bring the Sanjivini mountain?

**Answer:** Indrajit, who had received boons from Brahma, remained invisible and attacked from the sky, injuring all the prominent vanaras. Then he released the Brahmastra on Rama and Lakshmana. Seeing this, Rama told Lakshmana, 'Brother, this rakshasa hero has released the Brahmastra on us. Its power is unimaginable. So let us lie down as if we have withdrawn from battle.' They did so. Seeing this, Indrajit rejoiced that Rama, Lakshmana, and all the vanara warriors had fallen on the battlefield, and went to Lanka city to tell his father everything. Then, on the battlefield, Jambavan summoned Hanuman with Vibhishana and said, 'Maruti! This is the time for you to act. Go immediately across the sea to the Himalayan region, near a place called Vrishabhagiri, in the mountain region called Kailasagiri, and bring the four herbs named Mritasanjivani, Vishalyakarani, Sandhanakarani, and Savarnyakarani.' Hanuman went to Kailasagiri in the Himalayas as instructed. Unable to identify the herbs, he lifted the entire herb mountain and descended among the vanara army. As soon as the fragrance of the herbs touched them, all the vanaras, Rama, and Lakshmana, who were barely alive, rose as if from sleep and became radiant.

**Key entities:** Rama, Lakshmana, Hanuman, Indrajit, Brahma, Lanka, Jambavan, Vibhishana, Himalaya

#### Q5

**Question:** With the vanara army energized by the Sanjivini herbs, how did Sugriva besiege Lanka?

**Answer:** Sugriva informed Rama of what had happened so far and what needed to happen next, and told Hanuman, 'Maruti! Kumbhakarna, Ravana's sons, and relatives have died; that rakshasa king is dejected. In his current state, he will not come to battle. Therefore, let our vanara warriors take torches and burn Lanka!' As per Sugriva's command, the prominent vanaras took torches and set fire to Lanka's gates, royal palaces, and rakshasa houses during the first watch of that night. The fire consumed the lofty mansions, priceless objects, and wealth. Then Ravana sent Kumbha and Nikumbha, sons of Kumbhakarna, to battle, along with Yupaksha, Shonitaksha, Prajangha, and Kampana as their companions, ordering them to conquer the vanaras. They all went to the battlefield with the rakshasa army and fought a fierce battle with the vanara heroes.

**Key entities:** Sugriva, Lanka, Rama, Hanuman, Kumbhakarna, Ravana, Kumbha, Nikumbha

### Chapter 90: Ninety-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 76-81
- Source PDF pages: 223, 224, 225
- Printed page numbers: 227, 228, 229
- Key entities: Kumbha, Sugriva, Nikumbha, Hanuman, Ravana, Indrajit, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Angada, Nila, Jambavan, Khara
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** After the burning of Lanka, the battle continues. The demon Kumbha is killed by Sugriva, and Nikumbha by Hanuman. Ravana then sends Indrajit to battle. Indrajit performs a sacrifice to gain invisibility and attacks Rama and Lakshmana with a rain of arrows. He creates a illusory Sita and beheads her in front of Hanuman, causing grief.

#### Q1

**Question:** After the vanara warriors set Lanka ablaze on Sugriva's orders, in the ensuing battle, by whom was the prominent demon named Kampana killed?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Mainda
- 3. Dvivida
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Angada

**Key entities:** Lanka, Sugriva, Angada

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing his brother Kumbha killed by Sugriva, Nikumbha became enraged and fought fiercely. By whom was Nikumbha killed?

**Options:**
- 1. Sugriva
- 2. Nila
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Kumbha, Sugriva, Nikumbha, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** Hearing the news that Kumbha and Nikumbha had fallen in battle, whom did Ravana send to the battlefield?

**Answer:** Indrajit

**Key entities:** Kumbha, Nikumbha, Ravana, Indrajit

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sri Rama slay Makaraksha?

**Answer:** Makaraksha, son of Khara, came to the battlefield with a demon army and attacked the vanara army. He wounded many vanara warriors with his arrows, causing them to flee in confusion. Seeing the vanaras scattered, Sri Rama stopped the demons with his arrows. Unable to withstand Rama's onslaught, the demons halted. Enraged, Makaraksha challenged Rama, boasting that he would kill him. Rama replied that victory is not achieved by boasting but by valor. Makaraksha shot arrows at Rama, but Rama destroyed them. After a brief duel, Rama broke Makaraksha's bow, killed his charioteer, and destroyed his chariot. Makaraksha then hurled a trident at Rama, which Rama cut into three pieces with arrows. Finally, Rama felled Makaraksha with the Agneyastra. The vanaras rejoiced.

**Key entities:** Rama, Khara

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Indrajit, obedient to his father's command, display his magical powers after going to the battlefield?

**Answer:** Hearing of Makaraksha's fall, Ravana sent Indrajit to battle. Indrajit went to the sacrificial ground, kindled a fire, offered a black goat as oblation, propitiated the gods, and gained the power of invisibility. Then mounting a chariot equipped with all weapons, he went to the battlefield. Becoming invisible, he rained a torrent of arrows from the sky, wounding Rama and Lakshmana. Despite Rama and Lakshmana shooting divine weapons, none affected Indrajit. Many prominent vanaras fell to his arrows. Lakshmana suggested using the Brahmastra, but Rama said it would destroy the entire demon race and they should use other weapons to kill only Indrajit. Meanwhile, Indrajit created an illusory Sita, brought her before Hanuman, grabbed her hair, and beheaded her with a sharp sword. Seeing this, Hanuman grieved, believing the real Sita had been killed.

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Ravana, Rama, Lakshmana, Sita, Hanuman

### Chapter 91: Ninety-first Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 82-87
- Source PDF pages: 225, 226, 227, 228
- Printed page numbers: 229, 230, 231, 232
- Key entities: Indrajit, Sita, Hanuman, Vibhishana, Rama, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Jambavan, Ravana
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Indrajit creates a magical illusion of Sita and kills her in front of Hanuman, causing grief. He then goes to perform the Nikumbila homa. Vibhishana consoles Rama, revealing the illusion, and urges Lakshmana to go with him to stop the homa and kill Indrajit. Lakshmana, accompanied by Vibhishana and the monkey army, confronts Indrajit's forces. Indrajit stops the homa and engages in battle. A verbal dispute occurs between Indrajit and Vibhishana regarding Vibhishana's betrayal.

#### Q1

**Question:** After showing Hanuman and others that he killed Sita through his magical power, which homa did Indrajit go to perform?

**Options:**
- 1. Vishvajit sacrifice
- 2. Ashvamedha
- 3. Ishti homa
- 4. Nikumbila homa

**Correct answer:** Nikumbila homa

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Indrajit

#### Q2

**Question:** When Maruti told Rama that Indrajit had killed Sita in front of him, and Rama was grieving in various ways, who consoled Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Lakshmana
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Jambavan
- 4. Hanuman

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Rama, Indrajit, Sita, Vibhishana

#### Q3

**Question:** Who told Rama that what Indrajit killed was not the real Sita but a Maya Sita?

**Answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Rama, Indrajit, Sita, Vibhishana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Vibhishana inspire Lakshmana with war enthusiasm to kill Indrajit?

**Answer:** When Rama was immersed in grief upon hearing from Maruti that Indrajit had killed Sita, Vibhishana came to Rama and said, 'Lord! It is not true that Indrajit killed Sita. That is merely an illusion. Having plunged us into sorrow, Indrajit has gone to perform the Nikumbila homa. If Indrajit completes the Nikumbila homa, he will become invincible. Therefore, send Lakshmana with me now to kill him. Lakshmana will surely slay him.' Hearing Vibhishana's words, Rama was pleased and turning to Lakshmana said, 'Lakshmana! Take Sugriva, some more monkey forces, bear forces, and Jambavan with you, follow Vibhishana, and conquer that deceitful Indrajit. Vibhishana knows all the ins and outs of that area. He will accompany you with his ministers.' Following his elder brother's command, Lakshmana, together with Vibhishana, took his excellent bow, wore armor, donned a sword, bowed at Rama's feet, and said, 'Brother! May the arrows I release today tear apart that son of Ravana!' Then, following Vibhishana, he went and saw Indrajit's forces.

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Lakshmana, Indrajit, Rama, Hanuman, Sita, Sugriva, Jambavan, Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the battle between Lakshmana and Indrajit take place? Describe the dispute between Indrajit and Vibhishana.

**Answer:** Following Vibhishana, Lakshmana reached the Nikumbila chaitya. Vibhishana said to Lakshmana, 'O younger brother of Rama! Without destroying this visible rakshasa army, Indrajit, who is performing the abhicara homa, will not come out. So first, this rakshasa army must be scattered.' Immediately, Lakshmana rained arrows on the rakshasa army. Taking trees and mountain peaks, the monkey army fiercely confronted the rakshasa army. Then the rakshasa army, with weapons in their hands, confronted the monkey and bear warriors. Seeing his army scattered in fear of the monkey warriors' onslaught, Indrajit stopped the abhicara homa, mounted his chariot, and prepared for battle. Then Hanuman uprooted a great tree and hurled it at the rakshasas. Noticing that Indrajit was determined to kill Hanuman, Vibhishana informed Lakshmana. Lakshmana came forward to confront Indrajit. Seeing this, Indrajit said to Vibhishana, 'O rakshasa! You were born and raised on this earth. You are the real brother of my father. You are my uncle. Having such a relationship, you are committing such treachery against me. O evil-minded one! You have forgotten that you belong to the Pulastya lineage.' To these words of Indrajit, Vibhishana replied, 'O son of Ravana! It is true that I was born in the cruel rakshasa clan as you say. I do not like unrighteous deeds. But just because a younger brother's nature is opposed to his elder, can the elder drive the younger out of his house? For this reason, I had to behave in this manner.' Thus Vibhishana answered Indrajit.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Indrajit, Vibhishana, Rama, Hanuman, Ravana

### Chapter 92: Ninety-second Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 88-93
- Source PDF pages: 228, 229, 230
- Printed page numbers: 232, 233, 234
- Key entities: Lakshmana, Indrajit, Hanuman, Ravana, Sita, Sugriva, Vibhishana, Jambavan, Rama
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** Lakshmana and Indrajit engage in a fierce battle. Indrajit fights from a chariot while Lakshmana fights from Hanuman's shoulders. After a prolonged fight, Lakshmana kills Indrajit with the Aindra astra. Ravana, upon hearing of his son's death, becomes grief-stricken and attempts to kill Sita but is dissuaded by his minister Suparshva.

#### Q1

**Question:** While a fierce battle was raging between Lakshmana and Indrajit, Indrajit was riding a chariot. Where was Lakshmana fighting from?

**Options:**
- 1. Standing on the ground
- 2. From Hanuman's shoulders
- 3. From Sugriva's shoulders
- 4. From a chariot

**Correct answer:** From Hanuman's shoulders

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Indrajit, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** During the fierce battle between Indrajit and Lakshmana, both their bodies were wounded and fatigued. Who came forward to help Lakshmana?

**Options:**
- 1. Sugriva
- 2. Vibhishana
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Lakshmana, Vibhishana

#### Q3

**Question:** All of Ravana's forces were destroyed. Only Indrajit remained. Who encouraged the Vanara army saying that if he is killed, victory is ours?

**Answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Ravana, Indrajit, Vibhishana

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Lakshmana kill Indrajit?

**Answer:** The great warriors Lakshmana and Indrajit fought on the battlefield, raining arrows on each other. During that fierce battle, it was impossible to tell who was striking whom. Victory seemed uncertain. At that time, Lakshmana severely struck the four horses yoked to Indrajit's chariot with arrows. Then that younger brother of Rama cut off the head of the demon charioteer with a very powerful arrow. Then Indrajit himself drove the chariot and continued fighting. Then, with overflowing enthusiasm, four Vanara warriors named Pramadi, Sharabha, Rabhasa, and Gandhamadana killed Indrajit's horses. Left with no choice, Indrajit began fighting from the ground. Both Lakshmana and Indrajit, skilled archers, sought to kill each other. At that time, Indrajit told the demons, 'I will go to Lanka now and return with another chariot. Until then, fight with courage.' Indrajit went to Lanka and returned on another chariot. Thus arriving, Indrajit confronted Lakshmana and Vibhishana. In his battle fury, Indrajit shot arrows at his uncle Vibhishana and tormented him. Vibhishana, with his mace, struck and killed Indrajit's chariot horses and charioteer. Then Indrajit descended to the ground and fought a most terrible battle with Lakshmana. In that combat between the two warriors, using various missiles and weapons, finally Lakshmana killed Indrajit with the Aindra astra.

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Indrajit, Rama, Lanka, Vibhishana

#### Q5

**Question:** After Indrajit's death, what did Rama and Ravana do?

**Answer:** Lakshmana, wounded and covered in blood, along with Vibhishana, Hanuman and others, approached his elder brother and humbly informed him of Indrajit's death. Then Vibhishana told Rama that it was Lakshmana who had cut off Indrajit's head. Rama was greatly pleased, praised Lakshmana, and rejoiced that they had now conquered the demons. Meanwhile, in Lanka, Ravana's ministers heard the news of Indrajit's death, went to the battlefield, saw the lifeless Indrajit, and wept for a long time. Then they informed Ravana of Indrajit's death. Hearing that news, Ravana lost consciousness. Grief-stricken over his son, Ravana thought that it would be better to kill Sita. Immediately, ignoring the pleas of his well-wishers, Ravana, sword in hand, went to the Ashoka grove. Then Suparshva, the wisest of Ravana's ministers, said, 'O king! It is not proper for a valiant man like you to kill a woman. Direct your anger at Rama on the battlefield. If you defeat him, Sita will surely come under your control.' With many conciliatory words, he dissuaded Ravana from his attempt to kill Sita.

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Rama, Ravana, Lakshmana, Vibhishana, Hanuman, Lanka, Sita, Ashoka Grove

### Chapter 93: Ninety-third Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 94-99
- Source PDF pages: 230, 231, 232, 233
- Printed page numbers: 234, 235, 236, 237
- Key entities: Ravana, Indrajit, Rama, Surpanakha, Sugriva, Virupaksha, Mahodara, Angada, Mahaparshva, Hanuman, Indra, Vishvamitra, Dasharatha, Sita, Khara, Sushena, Jambavan, Vali
- Places: Lanka

**Summary:** Ravana, grieving Indrajit's death, sends all his warriors to battle. Rama defeats them all by evening and mentions that only he and one other possess the divine weapon. The demon women lament the destruction of their men, blaming Surpanakha. Ravana then proceeds to the battlefield. Sugriva kills Virupaksha and Mahodara. Angada kills Mahaparshva.

#### Q1

**Question:** Upon hearing the news of Indrajit's death, Ravana, overwhelmed with grief, sent all the demon warriors with him to the battlefield, saying, 'All of you go and kill Rama.' In the battle that day, Rama performed heroic feats and by evening felled all the demons. Then Rama told Hanuman and others, 'This divine weapon power exists only in me and one other.' Who is that person Rama mentioned?

**Options:**
- 1. Parashiva
- 2. Indra
- 3. Vishvamitra
- 4. Dasharatha

**Correct answer:** Parashiva

**Key entities:** Indrajit, Ravana, Rama, Hanuman

#### Q2

**Question:** Knowing that all the four-fold army sent by Ravana had died at Rama's hands, the demon women lamented and pondered who was the root cause of all this?

**Options:**
- 1. Sita
- 2. Khara
- 3. Surpanakha
- 4. Ravana

**Correct answer:** Surpanakha

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Surpanakha

#### Q3

**Question:** While the demon women were lamenting that all their men had fallen on the battlefield, who set out for the battlefield?

**Answer:** Ravana

**Key entities:** Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** By whom and in what manner did Virupaksha and Mahodara die?

**Answer:** When Ravana set out for the battlefield, all the remaining demon warriors in Lanka followed him. Among them were Virupaksha, Mahodara, and Mahaparshva. On the battlefield, due to Ravana's heroic exploits, some monkeys had their heads severed, some had their chests broken, and others had their limbs cut off. Seeing this situation, Sugriva entrusted the protection of the army camp to Sushena and resolved to fight Ravana, picking up a huge tree. Seeing this, the demon Virupaksha descended from his chariot, mounted an elephant, and roaring fiercely, shot arrows at Sugriva. Sugriva was wounded by those arrows. Recovering quickly, Sugriva roared in anger, picked up a huge tree, and struck with it. That blow felled the elephant Virupaksha was riding. Immediately, Virupaksha took a sword and shield and advanced on Sugriva. In the ensuing close combat, Sugriva's blow caused Virupaksha to fall to the ground with a blood-soaked body, blood flowing from his nine orifices like streams, and he died. Seeing Virupaksha fall, Ravana sent Mahodara against Sugriva. Mahodara also fought with Sugriva for a while and finally had his head severed by Sugriva and died.

**Key entities:** Virupaksha, Mahodara, Ravana, Lanka, Mahaparshva, Sugriva, Sushena

#### Q5

**Question:** By whom and in what manner did Mahaparshva die?

**Answer:** Seeing Mahodara and Virupaksha die at Sugriva's hands, the extremely powerful Mahaparshva, his eyes red with anger, began to torment Angada and his monkey army with his arrows. Due to the impact of that night-wanderer's arrows, the heads of prominent monkeys in the monkey army started falling off. Seeing his forces thus diminishing, Angada picked up an iron mace lying nearby and struck Mahaparshva severely. That blow caused the demon, along with his charioteer, to lose consciousness and fall from the chariot to the ground. Then Jambavan and Gavaksha picked up large boulders and destroyed Mahaparshva's chariot horses and chariot. Then Mahaparshva regained consciousness and struck Angada with arrows. Next, Angada picked up a parigha weapon and hurled it at Mahaparshva. That parigha weapon caused Mahaparshva's bow, arrows, and helmet to fall to the ground. Then Mahaparshva hurled a large axe at Angada. That son of Vali dodged the blow and with his diamond-like fist, shattered Mahaparshva's chest and killed him. Thus Mahaparshva died at Angada's hands.

**Key entities:** Mahaparshva, Mahodara, Virupaksha, Sugriva, Angada, Jambavan, Vali

### Chapter 94: Ninety-fourth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 100-106
- Source PDF pages: 233, 234, 235
- Printed page numbers: 237, 238, 239
- Key entities: Ravana, Rama, Lakshmana, Hanuman, Indra
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Ravana, after his forces are destroyed, comes to fight Rama. He first uses the Tamasastra on the monkeys. In the fierce battle, Ravana strikes Lakshmana unconscious with a weapon. Lakshmana is revived by Hanuman with the Sanjivani herb. Indra sends his chariot and weapons to aid Rama. Ravana's charioteer diverts the chariot due to exhaustion, explaining the horses are thirsty and Ravana needs rest.

#### Q1

**Question:** When all his men perished on the battlefield, Ravana came to the battlefield to fight Sri Rama. Which astra did he first use against the monkeys?

**Options:**
- 1. Tamasastra
- 2. Agneyastra
- 3. Varunastra
- 4. Brahmastra

**Correct answer:** Tamasastra

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** In the Rama-Ravana war, with which weapon did Ravana strike Lakshmana unconscious?

**Options:**
- 1. Modaki weapon
- 2. Musala weapon
- 3. Tamasastra
- 4. Shakti weapon

**Correct answer:** Shakti weapon

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Lakshmana

#### Q3

**Question:** How did Lakshmana, who lost consciousness due to Ravana's weapon, regain consciousness?

**Answer:** Through the Sanjivani brought by Hanuman

**Key entities:** Lakshmana, Ravana, Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** When the battle between Rama and Ravana reached its peak, how did Indra help Sri Rama?

**Answer:** During the fierce battle between Rama and Ravana, they were trying to kill each other with arrows and counter-arrows. At that time, Sri Rama was fighting from the ground while Ravana was on a golden chariot. Then Indra, the lord of the gods, ordered his charioteer Matali to take his chariot and hand it over to Sri Rama. Immediately, Matali brought the chariot before Rama, bowed to him, and said, 'Rama! Indra has sent this chariot to bring you victory in this war. Moreover, that lord has also presented you with a divine great bow, armor, arrows, and a sharp Shakti weapon. O mighty lord! Ascend this chariot. I will be your charioteer.' After Matali's words, Sri Rama circumambulated the chariot, bowed to it, and ascended it. Then a wonderful and tumultuous battle ensued between Rama and Ravana. While they were exchanging great divine weapons, Rama saw Ravana's fierce trident weapon coming towards him. He tried to stop it with a volley of arrows, but seeing that they were neutralized by the force of Ravana's trident, Rama immediately used the Shakti weapon sent by Indra. Then, by the power of the Shakti weapon, Ravana's trident weapon was neutralized. Thus, Indra provided appropriate help to Sri Rama.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Indra

#### Q5

**Question:** When the battle between Rama and Ravana reached its peak, why did Ravana's charioteer divert his chariot to the side? What explanation did the charioteer give to Ravana for that?

**Answer:** In the battlefield, Ravana, having been struck by Sri Rama's blows, was enraged, his eyes blazing with fire, and he severely wounded Sri Rama. Then Sri Rama rained a shower of arrows on Ravana who was nearby. In the battle, Sri Rama, desiring to kill his enemy, had his archery skill, valor, and battle enthusiasm doubled. All the weapons came to his memory quickly. Noticing this, Rama began to strike Ravana fiercely. Ravana, badly injured by the stone attacks of the monkey warriors and the volley of Sri Rama's arrows, his mind becoming deranged, could not resist by drawing his bow and using arrows and weapons. Even though he tried to shoot arrows with patience, as his end was approaching, they were of no use. Seeing this, Ravana's charioteer, observing his dire condition, carefully and slowly turned the chariot to another side. To the enraged Ravana, the charioteer said, 'Lord! The horses are thirsty. I noticed that you need some rest, so I turned the chariot aside. That is all, nothing else. Now, as per your command, I will stop the chariot before Rama.' And the charioteer did accordingly.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana

### Chapter 95: Ninety-fifth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 107-111
- Source PDF pages: 235, 236, 237, 238
- Printed page numbers: 239, 240, 241, 242
- Key entities: Rama, Ravana, Agastya, Shiva, Narayana, Kausalya, Sugriva, Vibhishana, Lakshmana
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** The chapter describes the intense battle between Rama and Ravana. Sage Agastya advises Rama to worship the Aditya Hridaya mantra. Matali positions the chariot to the right of Ravana's chariot. Rama struggles to kill Ravana as his heads keep regenerating. Matali reminds Rama of the Brahmastra, which Rama then uses to slay Ravana. The gods and allies rejoice.

#### Q1

**Question:** Seeing Sri Rama exhausted from fighting, Sage Agastya, watching from the sky along with the gods, desiring Rama's victory, which mantra did he teach and advise him to worship?

**Options:**
- 1. Shiva mantra
- 2. Narayana mantra
- 3. Aditya Hridaya mantra
- 4. Narasimha mantra

**Correct answer:** Aditya Hridaya mantra

**Key entities:** Rama, Agastya

#### Q2

**Question:** Seeing Ravana returning ready for battle, Matali, as per Sri Rama's indication, positioned his chariot on which side of Ravana's chariot?

**Options:**
- 1. Right side
- 2. Left side
- 3. Rear side
- 4. Far away

**Correct answer:** Right side

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama

#### Q3

**Question:** When the battle between Rama and Ravana reached its peak, were the series of weapons they were using physical or illusory?

**Answer:** Illusory

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana

#### Q4

**Question:** Why did Sri Rama fall into deep thought regarding the slaying of Ravana?

**Answer:** Both Rama and Ravana, from their chariots, were provoking each other with anger on the battlefield, intending to kill each other, and their forms were extremely fierce. The monkeys and rakshasas stopped fighting and watched with wide eyes. Thus the battle between Rama and Ravana continued incessantly for a day and night. Then Sri Rama, with immense rage, strung a sharp arrow like a great venomous serpent and severed Ravana's head. The head of Ravana, adorned with glittering earrings, fell to the ground, seen by all the worlds. Immediately, another head exactly like the previous one sprouted from Ravana's body. Rama swiftly cut off that head too with another arrow. Immediately, as before, another head grew. Then many heads cut by Rama's arrows grew back with equal splendor, and Ravana was not killed. Rama, the joy of Kausalya, was a great hero knowing all weapons, possessing many missiles. Yet such a Sri Rama fell into deep thought about how to kill that rakshasa king. The charioteer Matali noticed this.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ravana, Kausalya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did the slaying of Ravana take place?

**Answer:** In that battle between Rama and Ravana, Rama was only countering Ravana's arrows but not attempting to kill him. Matali thought, 'O descendant of Raghu! Why are you following him like an ignorant person? This one will die at the hands of a human. Therefore, kill him with the Brahmastra that resides in you.' Hearing the charioteer's words, Sri Rama remembered the Brahmastra. Immediately, that great hero took an arrow that hissed like a great serpent and shone with light. Sri Rama, endowed with great strength and valor, duly consecrated it with Vedic mantras, placed the Brahmastra on his bow, drew it to his ear, and released that Brahmastra, capable of severing the vital points, at Ravana. Immediately, the weapon struck Ravana's chest and pierced his heart. The next moment, having taken Ravana's life, the weapon struck the ground and then, like a humble servant who has completed his duty, returned to Sri Rama's quiver. Then Ravana's bow along with arrows fell from his hand to the ground along with his life. That mighty and radiant rakshasa king, losing his life, fell from his chariot onto the battlefield like Vritrasura slain by the thunderbolt. Then all beings rejoiced. Sugriva, Vibhishana, and Lakshmana, along with their followers, duly worshipped and praised Sri Rama on the battlefield.

**Key entities:** Ravana, Rama, Sugriva, Vibhishana, Lakshmana

### Chapter 96: Ninety-Sixth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 112-116
- Source PDF pages: 238, 239, 240
- Printed page numbers: 242, 243, 244
- Key entities: Ravana, Vibhishana, Rama, Mandodari, Hanuman, Sita, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Indra
- Places: Lanka, Ashoka Grove

**Summary:** After Ravana's death, Vibhishana grieves over his brother's body and is consoled by Rama. The women of the inner palace mourn and rush to the battlefield through the northern gate. Mandodari, Ravana's chief queen, laments. Rama arranges Vibhishana's coronation as king of Lanka. Hanuman visits Sita in Ashoka Vana and conveys Rama's message; Sita expresses her desire to see Rama.

#### Q1

**Question:** Who consoled Vibhishana when he was grief-stricken seeing his brother Ravana lying dead on the ground, killed by Sri Rama?

**Options:**
- 1. Lakshmana
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Sri Rama

**Correct answer:** Sri Rama

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Ravana, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** Through which gate did all the women of the inner palace come out, grieving upon hearing the news of Ravana's death, ignoring the people who tried to stop them, to go to the battlefield?

**Options:**
- 1. Southern gate
- 2. Northern gate
- 3. Eastern gate
- 4. Western gate

**Correct answer:** Northern gate

**Key entities:** Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** Among the women lamenting upon seeing Ravana's body on the battlefield, Mandodari was Ravana's how many wife?

**Answer:** first wife

**Key entities:** Ravana, Mandodari

#### Q4

**Question:** In what manner did Sri Rama conduct the coronation of Vibhishana as king of Lanka?

**Answer:** After the war concluded, Rama respectfully dismissed Matali, who had brought Indra's chariot. Then Rama embraced Sugriva and granted him the joy of a deep hug. Following Lakshmana's suggestion, Rama went with everyone to the military camps. Then Rama, seeing Lakshmana nearby, said, 'Brother! Vibhishana is affectionate towards me and is a supreme devotee. He greatly helped us in this war. Crown such a virtuous man as king of Lanka.' Lakshmana, delighted, entered Lanka city with Sugriva and other prominent vanaras, and with Vibhishana. Lakshmana selected swift messengers, gave them a golden vessel, and had them bring waters from the oceans. Then Lakshmana seated Vibhishana on the throne. The royal assembly was crowded with Vibhishana's friends and prominent vanaras. Then all the elders, according to Vedic rites, anointed Vibhishana on the throne with waters from the seven seas. They offered unbroken rice, fried grains, sweetmeats, flowers, and fragrant substances to that lord of rakshasas. By Rama's grace, Vibhishana became king of Lanka, fulfilling Rama's promise.

**Key entities:** Rama, Vibhishana, Lanka, Indra, Sugriva, Lakshmana

#### Q5

**Question:** After the war, when Hanuman visited Sita, what kind of message did she send to Sri Rama through Maruti?

**Answer:** By Rama's command, Maruti entered Lanka and, with Vibhishana's permission, visited Sita in Ashoka Vana. Seeing Hanuman approach, Sita recognized him as Maruti and was so overjoyed she could not speak. Then Hanuman, seeing her cheerful face, began to convey Rama's message: 'Mother Vaidehi! Rama and Lakshmana are well. Sugriva, Vibhishana, and all who helped in the war are well. Lord Ramachandra, who killed the tormentor of the world Ravana, asked about your welfare. I have told you these pleasing words that will give you great joy. O virtuous lady! It is my fortune that you have preserved your life till now; otherwise this victory of mine would be meaningless. Mother! Why are you still worrying? Why don't you speak to me?' Hearing Hanuman, the goddess with great joy and a choked voice said, 'Maruti! Hearing that my lord has achieved victory, I was unable to speak for a moment due to joy.' Then Janaki, standing before Maruti with folded hands, said, 'O venerable one! I will now go to that lord. Please grant me your message.' Then Janaki said, 'O best of vanaras! I wish to see my lord.' Then Hanuman, with her permission, quickly went and stood before Sri Rama.

**Key entities:** Hanuman, Sita, Rama, Lanka, Vibhishana, Ashoka Grove, Lakshmana, Sugriva, Ravana

### Chapter 97: Ninety-seventh Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 117-121
- Source PDF pages: 240, 241, 242
- Printed page numbers: 244, 245, 246
- Key entities: Vibhishana, Sita, Rama, Brahma, Narayana, Agni, Ravana, Sugriva, Hanuman, Dasharatha
- Places: None listed

**Summary:** Vibhishana brings Sita to Rama in a palanquin. Rama, fearing public opinion, speaks harshly to Sita, leading her to enter fire. Brahma and other gods appear, revealing Rama's divine nature as Narayana and Sita as Lakshmi. Agni returns Sita unharmed, and Rama accepts her after explaining his actions.

#### Q1

**Question:** How did Vibhishana bring Sita to Rama as per Rama's command?

**Options:**
- 1. Seated on an elephant
- 2. On a chariot
- 3. In a palanquin
- 4. In the Pushpaka Vimana

**Correct answer:** In a palanquin

**Key entities:** Vibhishana, Sita, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** When Rama told Sita, 'You have been seen by Ravana's sinful eyes, so I must doubt you. Henceforth you may go anywhere in the ten directions,' what decision did she make?

**Options:**
- 1. To enter fire
- 2. To seek refuge with Vibhishana
- 3. To seek refuge with Sugriva
- 4. To seek refuge with Hanuman

**Correct answer:** To enter fire

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Ravana

#### Q3

**Question:** Out of what fear did Rama speak harsh words to Sita?

**Answer:** Fear of public censure

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita

#### Q4

**Question:** When Sita entered the fire, what words did Brahma speak after appearing?

**Answer:** When Sita entered the fire, hearing the cries of the monkeys and rakshasas, the righteous Rama was very sorrowful, distressed, shedding tears, and fell into thought for a moment. Then Brahma and other gods appeared and said, 'Rama! You are the supreme one, foremost among the wise. How can you be indifferent while Sita enters the fire? You are the supreme among all gods, Lord Narayana. You do not realize that.' Then Rama bowed to Brahma and the gods and said, 'I think of myself as the son of King Dasharatha, an ordinary human.
