But who am I? Whose am I? Why have I come? I pray that Brahma explain to me.' Then Brahma said, 'O Rama of true valor! I will tell you the truth. You are Narayana, the cause of the world, endowed with six divine qualities. This Sita is Lakshmi. To kill the tormentor of the worlds, Ravana, you have incarnated as a human on earth. You have established dharma and fulfilled the gods' purpose. By praising you, desired wishes are fulfilled.' Thus Brahma himself told Rama.

**Key entities:** Sita, Brahma, Rama, Narayana, Dasharatha, Ravana

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Agni return Sita, who had entered the fire, to Rama?

**Answer:** As soon as he heard Brahma's auspicious words, Agni, like a father, brought Sita with him, came up from the fire pit, pushed aside the burning kindling, came out, and stood. Agni handed over that Sita, who had unparalleled beauty and splendor, to Rama. Then Agni, the witness of the world, said, 'O Lord Ramachandra! There is no fault in this Vaidehi, your wife. She always meditates on you with purity in thought, word, and deed. There is no fault in her.' Hearing Agni's words, Rama thought, 'Alas! I have unjustly hurt this noble woman with harsh words,' and became distressed, shedding tears. After thinking for a moment, he said to that best of gods, 'O Havyavahana! There is no fault in Sita. She is pure, but because she stayed for a long time under the shade of the Ashoka tree in Ravana's city, I had to conduct this test so that the three worlds would not doubt her. If I had accepted her without any test to reveal her purity, people would blame me, saying Dasharatha's Rama is lustful and foolish. I, who am always devoted to truth, remained indifferent while she entered the fire so that all three worlds would believe in Sita's chastity.' Then Rama took Sita close and lived happily.

**Key entities:** Agni, Sita, Rama, Brahma, Ravana, Dasharatha

### Chapter 98: Ninety-eighth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 122-126
- Source PDF pages: 242, 243, 244, 245
- Printed page numbers: 246, 247, 248, 249
- Key entities: Rama, Sita, Shiva, Bharata, Vibhishana, Indra, Sugriva, Dasharatha, Narayana, Brahma, Hanuman, Jambavan, Mandodari, Jatayu
- Places: Ayodhya, Lanka, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka, Ganga

**Summary:** After the fire ordeal, Rama accepts Sita. Shiva appears with all gods and shows Rama a divine being in a celestial chariot. Rama explains Bharata's vow to Vibhishana. At Rama's request, Indra revives the fallen monkeys. Rama prepares to return to Ayodhya, and Vibhishana offers the Pushpaka Vimana. Rama bids farewell to Sugriva and others, but they insist on accompanying him. They all board the Pushpaka and depart. During the journey, Rama points out various landmarks to Sita.

#### Q1

**Question:** Shiva, appearing with all the gods, said, 'Rama! Look at this great person seated in the divine chariot in the sky.' Who is that great person?

**Options:**
- 1. Narayana
- 2. Dasaratha
- 3. Brahma
- 4. Indra

**Correct answer:** Dasaratha

**Key entities:** Shiva, Rama, Dasharatha

#### Q2

**Question:** To whom did Lord Ramachandra explain Bharata's vow?

**Options:**
- 1. Hanuman
- 2. Sugriva
- 3. Vibhishana
- 4. Jambavan

**Correct answer:** Vibhishana

**Key entities:** Bharata, Vibhishana

#### Q3

**Question:** At Sri Rama's request, what did Lord Indra do to the fallen monkeys?

**Answer:** He revived them

**Key entities:** Rama, Indra

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Sri Rama set out for Ayodhya with all his people?

**Answer:** Vibhishana, at Rama's request, brought the beautifully decorated Pushpaka Vimana. Rama, after bidding farewell to Sugriva and others, agreed to take them along. All boarded the Pushpaka and thus Rama set out for Ayodhya with his people.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ayodhya, Vibhishana, Sugriva

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sri Rama converse with Sita while traveling on the Pushpaka?

**Answer:** Rama pointed out to Sita various places: Lanka, the battlefield, Mandodari mourning, the sea and the bridge, Madhuvana, Pampa, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka mountain, the banyan tree where Jatayu lived, the hermitages of Sharabhanga and other sages, the Ganga river, and Shringaberapura. Sita suggested bringing Sugriva's women to Ayodhya, and Rama agreed.

**Key entities:** Rama, Sita, Lanka, Mandodari, Kishkindha, Rishyamuka, Jatayu, Ganga, Sugriva, Ayodhya

### Chapter 99: Ninety-ninth Chapter

- Kanda: Yuddha Kanda
- Sarga range: 127-131
- Source PDF pages: 245, 246, 247
- Printed page numbers: 249, 250, 251
- Key entities: Rama, Hanuman, Bharata, Agastya, Vishvamitra, Sugriva, Vibhishana, Angada, Shatrughna, Sita, Jabali, Indra
- Places: Ayodhya

**Summary:** Rama lands the Pushpaka Vimana three yojanas from Ayodhya and enters the hermitage of Sage Bharadvaja. After accepting hospitality, he sends Hanuman ahead to Bharata. Hanuman informs Bharata of Rama's return, and Bharata joyfully prepares for Rama's coronation. Rama arrives, and the coronation ceremony is performed by Sage Vasishtha and other sages.

#### Q1

**Question:** At a distance of three yojanas from Ayodhya, after landing the Pushpaka Vimana, in which sage's hermitage did Sri Rama enter?

**Options:**
- 1. Sage Agastya
- 2. Sage Bharadvaja
- 3. Sage Vasishtha
- 4. Sage Vishvamitra

**Correct answer:** Sage Bharadvaja

**Key entities:** Ayodhya, Rama

#### Q2

**Question:** After accepting the hospitality arranged by the sage in the hermitage, whom did Sri Rama first send to Bharata?

**Options:**
- 1. Sugriva
- 2. Vibhishana
- 3. Hanuman
- 4. Angada

**Correct answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Rama, Bharata, Hanuman

#### Q3

**Question:** Who first told Bharata the story of Sri Rama's exile?

**Answer:** Hanuman

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama, Hanuman

#### Q4

**Question:** How did Bharata arrange the welcome and coronation preparations for Sri Rama?

**Answer:** Upon hearing Hanuman's words, Bharata joyfully looked at Shatrughna and said, 'Brother! Our elder brother Lord Ramachandra is coming here by dawn. Decorate the city of Ayodhya beautifully this very night.' As soon as he commanded, the citizens of Ayodhya decorated the city beautifully by the early morning. Then, as dawn broke, the queen mothers, preceptors, ministers, army chiefs, city leaders, soldiers holding flags and banners, along with priests, people of various professions, holding flower garlands and sweet items, with Vasishtha and others following, Bharata, delighted at the auspicious arrival of Sri Ramachandra, bowed his head to the Lord's sandals and waited with royal honors. Then, at a distance, the divine Pushpaka Vimana was seen. As the Vimana landed close to them, everyone there saw Lord Ramachandra in the Vimana. Then Bharata approached Sri Rama and said, 'Brother! Accepting our mother's words, I now return to you this kingdom that you gave me in trust. Therefore, O Lord! Be crowned king of this kingdom and rule us, your devotees and servants. May the whole world be filled with joy seeing your coronation festival.' To Bharata's words, Sri Rama said, 'So be it!' Then Bharata assigned the necessary arrangements for the coronation to each person according to their duty.

**Key entities:** Bharata, Rama, Hanuman, Shatrughna, Ayodhya

#### Q5

**Question:** How did Sri Rama's coronation take place?

**Answer:** After everyone reached Ayodhya in a procession from Nandigram, the platform with the jeweled throne for Rama's coronation was decorated in every way. Ministers, all government officials, and city leaders who came to witness the coronation sat in seats appropriate to their status. Then, the family priest Sri Vasishtha, amidst the chanting of Vedic mantras by the ritvijas, seated the fully ornamented Sri Sita and Ramachandra on the jeweled throne. Then, with auspicious music and Vedic mantras, Vasishtha, Vamadeva, Jabali, and other sages anointed Lord Ramachandra, the supreme among men, with pure fragrant waters, as the Vasus anointed Indra. Then, with Vedic mantras, they anointed Sita and Rama with holy waters mixed with various herbal essences. Then, the jeweled crown that Manu first wore at his coronation, and which all lords of Ayodhya had worn in succession, was placed on Lord Ramachandra, seated on the jeweled throne, by Sri Vasishtha Maharshi with Vedic mantras. Then the ritvijas also adorned the Lord with other ornaments. Thereafter, Lord Ramachandra became emperor, made Bharata the crown prince, performed many sacrifices like Ashvamedha, and ruled the kingdom for many years, looking after the people like his own children.

**Key entities:** Rama, Ayodhya, Sita, Jabali, Indra, Bharata
